# First Principles Cache

### 2026-04-22: 15 cross-volume AP entries added from Vol III Wave 11-19

Fifteen Vol I-specific cache framings accompany the new AP939--AP953 entries
in `notes/antipatterns_catalogue.md`. Each row lists the wrong claim, the
Vol I ghost theorem (the true statement behind the confusion), the precise
error, and the Vol I correction — mirroring the Vol III Wave 11-19
error/retraction catalogue as manifest in Vol I's bar--cobar / Koszul /
landscape-census framework. AP cross-references AP939--AP953 carry the
full statements; these cache rows are the compact Vol I-lens triples.

| # | Wrong Claim | Ghost Theorem | Precise Error | Correct Relationship | Type | AP |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| X1 | $\kappa(K3 \times E) = 2$ on the total space (bare $\kappa$, fibre value on product ambient). | Categorical Euler on products is Künneth-multiplicative: $\kappa_{\mathrm{cat}}(K3 \times E) = \chi(\cO_{K3}) \cdot \chi(\cO_E) = 2 \cdot 0 = 0$. | Bare $\kappa$ conflates $\kappa_{\mathrm{cat}}$ (total space, Künneth-multiplicative, $= 0$) with $\kappa_{\mathrm{fiber}}$ (K3 fibre alone, $= 2$). Vol I landscape-census and K3 bar-complex examples silently push the fibre value onto the total space. | Vol I names the subscript explicitly at every site: $\kappa_{\mathrm{cat}}(K3 \times E) = 0$; $\kappa_{\mathrm{fiber}}(K3) = 2$; $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}) = 5$ (paramodular); $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^K(K3 \times E) = 3$ (Heisenberg-level). Vol I archetype-$\mathbf B$ $K = 8$ row depends on naming $\kappa_\bullet$. | Künneth multiplicative discipline | AP939 |
| X2 | $c_{2d}(\mathcal T[A_1, \Sigma_{0, 24}]) = -14432/121$ (Wave 14 value). | $(c_{4d}, c_{2d}) = (107/6, -214)$ via Wave 15 Gaiotto verification against $c_{4d} = (5n - 13)/6$ at $n = 24$. | Single-route citation of a load-bearing structure constant whose Wave 14 value was retracted; AP274 citation-as-derivation. | Vol I uses two independent verification routes: (i) Shapere--Tachikawa 2008 universal formula; (ii) direct Sugawara-denominator recomputation on Gaiotto curve. Canonical value $(107/6, -214)$. | two-route verification for retractable constants | AP940 |
| X3 | $\eta^{-48}$ is a Virasoro minimal-model character. | Heisenberg--Mukai lattice partition function $\eta^{-48} = \prod_n (1 - q^n)^{-24}$ on the Mukai lattice $\mathrm{II}_{1, 1} \otimes \cO_{K3}$; iterated DS reduction $V_{24} = \mathrm{DS}^{24}(\mathrm{Heis}_{\mathrm{II}_{1, 1}})$. | Two distinct VOA presentations of the same generating function conflated; Heisenberg--Mukai has a free-field factor, Virasoro minimal-model does not. | Vol I K3 chiral Hall--Drinfeld sites name Heisenberg--Mukai lattice VOA and the iterated Drinfeld--Sokolov chain from higher-rank source. | VOA presentation confusion | AP941 |
| X4 | Macdonald framework applies to any W-algebra at non-critical level. | Macdonald framework is a theorem for Cherednik DAHA and admissible-level affine Lie algebras with minimal-model structure. | Extends Macdonald framework beyond admissibility domain; Pentagon coboundary $\phi^{(n)}$ silently relies on admissibility. | Vol I Macdonald-framework invocations name the admissibility constraint: admissible level $k + h^\vee = p/q$ with $(p, q) = 1$. Non-minimal targets use Kac--Roan 2014 residue or Feigin--Frenkel centre. | admissibility-scope discipline | AP942 |
| X5 | $k$-th Gritsenko--Clery form has Borcherds weight $k$. | Weights are non-monotone: $(w_1, \ldots, w_8) = (5, 2, 1, 1, 1/2, 1, 1/4, 0)$ with $c_N(0) \in \{10, 4, 2, 2, 1, 2, 1/2, 0\}$; universal $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Phi_N) = c_N(0)/2$. | Enumeration index confused with mathematical invariant; catalogue is enumerated by $\mathrm{Sp}_4(\Z)$-cover refinement, not by weight. | Vol I cites the eight-form catalogue with cover group ($\mathrm{Sp}_4$, $\mathrm{Mp}_4$, $\widetilde{\mathrm{Mp}}_4$) and weight listed per form. | eight-form catalogue discipline | AP943 |
| X6 | $c_2(0) = 4$ (or $= 8$) stated bare. | $c_2(0) = 4$ in Gritsenko 1999 twined convention; $c_2(0) = 8$ in Cheng--Duncan 2013 umbral convention. | Convention-dependent structure constant cited without declaration; ambient-qualifier drop (AP281). | Vol I declares convention at every twined $c_N(0)$ reference: "Gritsenko 1999 ($c_2(0) = 4$)" or "Cheng--Duncan 2013 ($c_2(0) = 8$)". Gritsenko is Vol I default. | convention declaration discipline | AP944 |
| X7 | Real-root subalgebra of $\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$ is $\widehat{\mathfrak{sl}_3}$. | Feingold--Frenkel rank-3 hyperbolic Kac--Moody algebra $F_3$ (Feingold--Frenkel 1983 *Math Ann* 263) with hyperbolic Cartan matrix, imaginary-root Weyl chamber non-empty, Humbert-divisor matching on K3 fibre. | Conflates affine Lie algebra (rank-2 + centre, no imaginary roots) with rank-3 hyperbolic Kac--Moody algebra (indefinite type, imaginary-root content). | Vol I genus-1 BKM real-root sites cite $F_3$ with hyperbolic Cartan matrix; Humbert-divisor match on K3 fibre named. | Kac--Moody type discipline | AP945 |
| X8 | $V_{24} = L_{-6}(\mathfrak{e}_8)$ (affine $\mathfrak{e}_8$ at level $-6$). | Iterated Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction $V_{24} = \mathrm{DS}^{24}(\mathrm{Heis}_{\mathrm{II}_{1, 1}})$; central charge $c(V_{24}) = 24$. $L_{-6}(\mathfrak{e}_8)$ has $c = -992/11$, so identification fails at $c$-level. | Conflates affine VOA at specific level with iterated-DS output of higher-rank chain. | Vol I $V_{24}$ references cite the iterated-DS chain with source, level, nilpotent orbit; three-path verification anchored at $\chi_{V_{24}} = \eta^{-48}$. | VOA construction discipline | AP946 |
| X9 | $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}} = \kappa_{\mathrm{ch}} + \chi(\cO_{\mathrm{fiber}})$ (additive decomposition). | Universal $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Phi_N) = c_N(0)/2$ (Borcherds weight); additive relation FALSE at every $N \in \{1, 2, 3, 4, 6\}$. At $N = 1$, left $= 5$, right $= 0 + 0 = 0$; at $N = 2$, left $= 4$, right $= 1$. | Borcherds lift is multiplicative automorphic-product functor, not additive; no lift-functoriality justifies the decomposition. | Vol I BRST ghost-charge trace identity reads with scope-split: Borcherds-weight side multiplicative on Mukai lattice; $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$ / $\kappa_{\mathrm{fiber}}$ bookkeeping is CY-categorical denominator; two scopes meet at $c_N(0)/2$. | scope-split discipline | AP947 |
| X10 | Fake Monster BKM is the Vol III $d = 3$ $K3 \times E$ output. | Fake Monster: Cartan rank $26$ on $\mathrm{II}_{25, 1}$ (Borcherds 1992), $d = 5$ on $K3 \times K3 \times E$ with $\Phi_{12}$. K3-BKM: Cartan rank $3$ on $\Lambda^{2, 1}_{\mathrm{II}}$, $d = 3$ on $K3 \times E$ with $\Phi_{10} = \Delta_5^2$. | CY-dimension confusion between two different BKMs indexed by two different Borcherds lifts. | Vol I Fake-Monster references cite $d = 5$ with $\Phi_{12}$; K3-BKM references cite $d = 3$ with $\Delta_5$. Canonical preamble rows 20--22 pin. | CY-dimension discipline for BKM | AP948 |
| X11 | $\chi_{V_{24}} = \eta^{-48}$ by direct character match. | Three-path verification: (i) iterated-DS character contraction; (ii) Sugawara-denominator recomputation; (iii) Borcherds lift on Mukai lattice. | Load-bearing identity cited without derivation; direct-match framing hides three-path verification. | Vol I sites citing $\eta^{-48}$ character identity name three verification paths and iterated-DS construction of $V_{24}$. | three-path verification discipline | AP949 |
| X12 | Gaiotto curve for K3-BKM is $\Sigma_{2, 0}$ closed genus-2. | $\Sigma_{0, 24}$ genus-0 with 24 $A_1$ punctures; trinion/tube count $(n_v, n_h) = (63, 88)$ (Chacaltana--Distler 2010). | Puncture-count / genus confusion; moduli dimension $6g - 6 + 2n = 42$ vs $6$. | Vol I Gaiotto-curve references use $\Sigma_{0, 24}$; $24$ punctures match $\chi(K3) = 24$ and the $24 I_1$ pentagon nodes. | Gaiotto curve identification discipline | AP950 |
| X13 | Vol I's Koszul Reflection $K$ is the CY-to-chiral functor directly. | Two-stage factorisation $\Phi_d = \mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\Sigma_{d-1}, C} \circ \Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_d$: Koszul Reflection $K$ is Stage 1 on the Koszul-self-dual locus; Vol I bar--cobar adjunction (Theorem A) is the Stage-2 $E_1$-chiral shadow on reference curve $C$. | Collapses two distinct $(\infty, 1)$-categorical operations into one; hides family parameter $(\Sigma_{d-1}, C)$. | Vol I names two stages and family parameter at every CY-to-chiral reference; Koszul Reflection $K$ is Stage 1 on Koszul-self-dual locus. | two-stage factorisation discipline | AP951 |
| X14 | PTVV table closes at $d = 4$; $d = 5$ is beyond PTVV. | PTVV extends to all $d$ with shift $-2d + 2$ on CY-$d$ moduli; $d = 5$ row $(5, -4, \mathrm{Poisson}\text{-}E_5)$ via Dunn--Lurie $E_3 \otimes E_2 = E_5$. | Incomplete dimensional enumeration. | Vol I PTVV enumerations close at $d = 5$ Poisson-$E_5$: $(1, 0, E_0), (2, -2, E_1), (3, -2, \mathrm{Poisson}\text{-}E_3), (4, -2, \mathrm{Poisson}\text{-}E_4), (5, -4, \mathrm{Poisson}\text{-}E_5)$. | PTVV table extension | AP952 |
| X15 | Pentagon single-colour coherence $H^3$ is uniformly $\Z/2$ across Mathieu classes. | Class-dependent: $H^3 \in \Z/2$ for 2A, $H^3 \in \Z/4$ for 2B; per-class refinement for all 25 $M_{24}$ classes. | Conjugacy-class-dependent torsion presented as class-independent. | Vol I Pentagon $H^3$ statements name the Mathieu class and its torsion value. | Mathieu-class-dependent $H^3$ discipline | AP953 |


### 2026-04-22: 12 constructive cache entries added (Wave 11-19 synthesis)

Twelve new cache entries C1--C12 inscribed below the main table as the ``Wave 11--19
constructive synthesis append.'' Unlike the preceding confusion-pattern entries, C1--C12
record the positive structure that emerged from the Wave 11--19 synthesis, lensed into
Vol I's Koszul reflection / denominator-scope $\kappa$ / BRST ghost charge framing:
the two-stage factorisation of $\Phi$; the universal positive-geometry grammar $Y^+(X)$
with $G(X) = D(Y^+(X))$; the universal Borcherds weight identity
$\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Phi_N) = c_N(0)/2$ on the eight Gritsenko--Cl\'ery forms; the
three-factor universal trace identity
$\mathrm{tr}_{\mathrm{ghost}}(Q_{\mathrm{BRST}}^2) = \mathrm{tr}_{\mathrm{Pentagon}} = \omega_{\mathrm{Borcherds}} = c_N(0)/2$;
$6$D hCS as $E_3$-algebra; three-tier hierarchy on the seven faces of $r_{\mathrm{CY}}$;
dimensional sibling catalogue (Monster, Igusa cusp form BKM, Fake Monster);
Serre-equivariant quasi-NCCR for $K3 \times E$; Gaiotto curve correction
($\mathcal T[A_1, \Sigma_{0, 24}]$); Heisenberg--Mukai $\eta^{-48}$ identity;
$V_{24}$ as iterated DS reduction; $F_3$ Feingold--Frenkel real-root subalgebra of
$\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$. Vol I lens: each entry relates to Vol I's Koszul self-duality
ceiling, derived-centre complementarity landmark $\mathsf B$-row $\kappa + \kappa^! = 8$,
BRST ghost-trace identity, and five-archetype G/L/C/M/B landscape.

| # | Wrong Claim | Ghost Theorem | Precise Error | Correct Relationship | Type |
|---|-------------|---------------|---------------|----------------------|------|
| 263 | Class C for $\beta\gamma$ or $bc$ is witnessed by the internal weight-changing line or by an unspecified charged stratum. | The $\beta\gamma$/$bc$ families do realize class C, and the weight-changing slice is a real computed locus. | Conflates a one-dimensional internal slice, where the shadow tower vanishes, with the actual family-level class-C witness. | The weight-changing line is shadow-trivial: $\Theta^{\le r}\vert_{\mathrm{w.c.}}=0$ for $r\ge2$. The class-C witness is the standard conformal-weight family $\beta\gamma_\lambda$ or $bc_\lambda$, with $S_2=6\lambda^2-6\lambda+1$, $S_3=0$, $S_4=-5/12$, and $S_r=0$ for $r\ge5$. | slice/family conflation |
| 264 | Bare `d(Vir)=3` or `d_{\mathrm{alg}}(\mathrm{Vir})=3`. | Virasoro does have a genuine depth-3 invariant in the Gelfand-Fuchs/generating sense. | Conflates generating depth with algebraic shadow depth. | The correct split is $d_{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathrm{Vir})=3$ and $d_{\mathrm{alg}}(\mathrm{Vir})=\infty$. Every Virasoro depth claim must name the depth invariant explicitly. | invariant conflation |
| 265 | Class C requires a `stratum separation` mechanism to add one extra finite level beyond the discriminant dichotomy. | The finite quartic witness and the impossibility of algebraic depth 3 are both real. | Replaces the first-principles depth-gap statement by an unsupported narration about charged sectors. | `prop:depth-gap-trichotomy` gives the correct finite possibilities: $d_{\mathrm{alg}}\in\{0,1,2,\infty\}$. The class-C case is the standard conformal-weight family with $S_3=0$, $S_4=-5/12$, $S_r=0$ for $r\ge5$; there is no separate finite depth-3 stage to be created by narration. | mechanism error |
| 266 | `\cite{Hinich2001}` names a live local bibliography item for the Hinich rectification remark. | A plausible bibkey automatically resolves to the intended canonical source, so the citation still grounds the sentence. | `chapters/theory/theorem_C_refinements_platonic.tex` cites `Hinich2001`, but `bibliography/references.tex` has only `HS87`, `HS93`, and `Hin97`; there is no `Hinich2001` entry, so the build produces `[?]` and the proof trail disappears. | Every cite key must match a live canonical alias in the bibliography. If the intended Hinich source is already present, cite its actual key (`HS87`, `HS93`, or `Hin97` here); otherwise add the missing entry before citing it. | citation-key phantom drift |
| 267 | `GR17` may be described in prose as `Francis--Gaitsgory`. | Any nearby Gaitsgory-adjacent source can be named from memory without checking the bibliography entry behind the key. | In `chapters/theory/theorem_C_refinements_platonic.tex`, the prose attribution says `Francis--Gaitsgory`, but `bibliography/references.tex` defines `GR17` as D. Gaitsgory and N. Rozenblyum, *A Study in Derived Algebraic Geometry*. | Prose attribution must match the actual bibliography entry attached to the cited key. `GR17` is Gaitsgory--Rozenblyum; any Francis--Gaitsgory claim needs the distinct Francis/Gaitsgory source and key. | citation-attribution drift |
| 268 | Finite-dimensional bar cohomology at each conformal weight is enough to discharge `lem:perfectness-criterion` and prove family perfectness. | Weightwise finiteness automatically upgrades to the total finite-dimensional flat fiber cohomology required by the perfectness lemma. | The proof of `prop:perfectness-standard-landscape` ends with `finite-dimensional at each conformal weight` / `finite graded dimension at each conformal weight`, while `lem:perfectness-criterion` requires total finite-dimensional flat fiber cohomology after the spectral sequence collapses to degree $0$. Infinitely many nonzero weights can still make the total fiber infinite-dimensional. | To invoke `lem:perfectness-criterion`, the proof must supply the missing bridge to total finite-dimensional degree-$0$ fiber cohomology, or else weaken the proposition to the weightwise statement it actually proves. Weightwise control alone is strictly weaker than total finiteness. | weaker-than-required proof discharge |
| 269 | The chiral bar-cobar adjunction $\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}} \dashv B^{\mathrm{ch}}$ holds at chain level (Theorem A stated without homotopical qualifier). | There is a bar-cobar adjunction of the right general form between chiral cobar and chiral bar, after suitable homotopical refinement. | Bar-cobar pairs in the filtered/chiral setting almost never give strict chain-level adjunctions: the counit $\epsilon: \Omega^{\mathrm{ch}} B^{\mathrm{ch}} A \to A$ and the unit $\eta: C \to B^{\mathrm{ch}} \Omega^{\mathrm{ch}} C$ require a coalgebra-splitting of the bar filtration that exists only up to coherent homotopy. The triangle identities hold on the nose only after passing to the homotopy category or to ind-completion. | State Theorem A as an adjunction of $(\infty,1)$-categories (or of the associated derived/homotopy categories), not as a strict chain-level adjunction. Every "adjunction" claim in the programme must specify one of: (i) strict chain-level (rare — needs explicit splitting witness), (ii) homotopy-category / derived-category level, (iii) $(\infty,1)$-categorical. The chiral version is (ii)/(iii), not (i). | adjunction-strictness conflation |
| 270 | "Every standard chiral algebra reduces, under the averaging map $\mathrm{av}: \mathfrak{g}^{E_1} \to \mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{mod}}$, to one of the four archetypes G / L / C / M." | The four archetypes (Heisenberg, affine Kac-Moody, $\beta\gamma$, Virasoro) do exhaust a precisely delimitable class of chiral algebras. | The word "standard" silently carries the scope hypothesis. Without a definition of "standard chiral algebra" (Koszul $E_1$-chiral? Finitely strongly generated? Freely generated? Affine-type?), the dichotomy silently excludes parafermions $\mathbb{Z}_k$, $\mathcal{W}_N$ at general $N$, coset VOAs, non-unimodular lattice VOAs, triplet / symplectic fermion, and logarithmic extensions — each of which can fail to fit the four-archetype classification. | Classification claims must name the hypothesis class under which exhaustiveness is proved (candidate: finitely strongly generated Koszul $E_1$-chiral algebras over a smooth curve, admitting a conformal vector). Handle the non-standard examples in a separate remark listing which archetypes they realize (or fail to realize). The dichotomy is a theorem about a class, not about "all chiral algebras". | classification-scope silently unstated |
| 271 | $r_{\max}(A)$ (shadow-tower depth / algebraic depth $d_{\mathrm{alg}}(A)$) is invoked as an invariant of the chiral algebra $A$ without a separate proposition establishing presentation-independence. | Depth is a real, well-defined invariant on an appropriate class of chiral algebras; Theorem D (obstruction-tower universality $\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$) rests on depth being a property of $A$, not of a chosen presentation. | Without a presentation-independence proposition, $r_{\max}$ is at most an invariant of the strong-generation set. Any classification theorem or universality statement that treats $r_{\max}(A)$ as algebra-level data is incomplete until presentation-independence is proved; drift here propagates silently from Theorem D to every numerical consequence. | Depth invariants must be paired with a presentation-independence proposition. Either (a) exhibit a canonical strong generating set stable under chiral automorphisms and prove $r_{\max}$ is computed on it, or (b) define $r_{\max}(A) := \inf_{\text{presentations}} r_{\max}$ and prove the infimum is attained. State and label the independence result separately (e.g., `prop:depth-presentation-independence`). | invariant vs presentation conflation |
| 272 | "The conformal vector $\omega$ kills the chiral direction, promoting $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ from $E_2$ to $E_3$." (Or analogous: "$X$ kills $Y$", "$X$ forces the transition", "$X$ promotes $E_n$ to $E_{n+1}$".) | Conformal-vector-driven topologization is a real mechanism; Deligne-style $E_n$ promotion by a chosen distinguished element (Hoch$^*(A) = E_2$ + conformal vector $\to E_3$) is classical. | "Kills the chiral direction" is narrative, not a chain-level operation. The conformal vector $\omega$ is a distinguished element of $A$, not an operator on $B(A)$ or on $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(A,A)$. Without exhibiting the explicit chain homotopy $h_\omega$ satisfying $[d, h_\omega] = \mathrm{id} - p_{\mathrm{top}}$ (projection onto the topological sector), or the explicit $E_3$-operad action built from $\omega$, the topologization step is unmathematized narration. | Every "X kills Y" / "X promotes $E_n$ to $E_{n+1}$" / "X forces the transition" claim must expose: (i) the chain-level map (chain homotopy, Koszul contraction, or operad-valued morphism) that does the killing/promoting, (ii) the homotopy identity it satisfies ($dh + hd = \mathrm{id} - p$ or equivalent), (iii) a check that the resulting operation assembles into an action of the claimed operad on the correct derived-centre pair. Otherwise restate as conjecture or heuristic. | narration as mechanism (chain-level map missing) |
| 273 | $\Phi: \mathrm{CY}_d\text{-categories} \to \mathrm{ChirAlg}_X$ is called a "functor" (Vol III central construction). | There is a systematic construction attaching a chiral algebra to each CY-d category in a suitable class; the object-level correspondence is real and productive. | Without a morphism-preservation theorem — does a CY functor $F: \mathcal{C} \to \mathcal{D}$ produce a chiral morphism $\Phi(F): \Phi(\mathcal{C}) \to \Phi(\mathcal{D})$? — $\Phi$ is an object-level correspondence, not a functor. Morphisms of CY-d categories (cyclic $A_\infty$ functors, shifted-Lagrangian correspondences, trace-preserving exact functors) do not obviously descend to chiral-algebra morphisms without an explicit bimodule / Maurer-Cartan-transport step. Different CY-morphism classes give different target morphism classes. | State $\Phi$ as an object-level construction unless morphism-preservation is proved and inscribed. If proved, name the source morphism class explicitly and construct $\Phi(F)$ via a named mechanism (defect bimodule, MC transport, deformation-quantization modular-operad map). In Vol III, audit every use of "$\Phi$ is a functor" against this standard; where morphism-preservation is not established, downgrade to "object-level correspondence" or "assignment". | functor vs object-level correspondence conflation |
| 274 | $\langle \Lambda | \Lambda \rangle = c(5c+22)/10$ (Zamolodchikov norm) or $S_4 = 10/[c(5c+22)]$ imported by citation to Zamolodchikov / BPZ. | The identity is correct and well-attested in the physics literature under standard conventions. | Cited numerical identities with convention-dependent factors (OPE coefficients, mode conventions, Virasoro-primary orthogonalization coefficient $3/10$, normalization of $T$) silently import the source's convention stack. A programme with first-principles epistemic standards cannot rely on citation for load-bearing constants that appear in $\kappa$ per family, shadow tower $S_k$, or derived-centre complementarity $\kappa + \kappa^!$. | Load-bearing numerical constants must be derived in-place from defining axioms: Virasoro OPE $T(z)T(w) = \tfrac{c/2}{(z-w)^4} + \tfrac{2T(w)}{(z-w)^2} + \tfrac{\partial T(w)}{z-w}$, or mode relations $[L_m, L_n] = (m-n)L_{m+n} + \tfrac{c}{12}(m^3-m)\delta_{m+n,0}$. State normalization conventions explicitly. Cross-check by $\ge 3$ independent paths (mode expansion, OPE contraction, Kac determinant / singular-vector). Citation is a sanity check after the derivation, not a substitute. | citation-as-derivation substitution (load-bearing constants) |
| 275 | "Topologization is proved for affine Kac-Moody at non-critical level." (Or analogously: "Theorem holds away from critical / admissible / resonant level" without obstruction statement.) | There is a genuine proof valid for $k \ne -h^\vee$; the critical-level obstruction is real and has well-known mathematical content. | Stating "proved at non-critical level" without identifying the critical-level obstruction treats $k = -h^\vee$ as a technicality. At critical level the centre of the affine VOA becomes infinite-dimensional (Feigin-Frenkel: $Z(V_{-h^\vee}(\mathfrak{g})) \cong \mathrm{Fun}(\mathrm{Op}_{{}^L\mathfrak{g}}(D^\times))$), the Sugawara conformal vector is undefined, and the argument using $\omega$ cannot even be stated — the obstruction is not a bug, it is the content. | Every "proved at non-critical level" (or analogous scope-qualifier) claim must be accompanied by (a) a remark stating what fails at the excluded level with mathematical content (centre becomes Op-algebra, Sugawara undefined, normalization denominator vanishes, etc.), (b) whether the conjecture admits a repaired statement at the excluded level via a named duality (Feigin-Frenkel, Wakimoto resolution, geometric Langlands dictionary), (c) whether the obstruction is local (isolated bad levels) or global (entire families). | scope-qualifier without obstruction statement |
| 276 | Bare "$E_n$-chiral algebra" (typically $E_1$- or $E_2$-chiral) without specifying which of the $\ge 5$ distinct notions is meant. | Each of the notions is a real object with its own natural derived centre; the programme needs all of them at different points. | At least five non-equivalent notions coexist: (A) $A_\infty$-algebra in factorizable $D$-modules on $X$; (B) operad map $A_\infty \to \mathrm{End}^{\mathrm{ch}}_A$ with meromorphic structure maps; (C) operad map $E_2^{\mathrm{homot}} \to \mathrm{End}^{\mathrm{ch}}_A$; (D) $A_\infty$-algebra in the category of $E_1$-chiral algebras (inner chiral + outer algebraic); (E) iterated $A_\infty$-in-$A_\infty$-in-factorizable-$D$-modules. No equivalence is established among them, and each has its own derived centre on its own operad. | Before writing any statement about "$E_n$-chiral algebra" or "derived centre of an $E_n$-chiral algebra": name the notion (A/B/C/D/E or a sixth), name the matching centre construction, name the output operad, and — if claiming $E_3$ — state the conformal-vector / non-critical-level hypothesis. Inscribe a definition block once per chapter fixing the notion, cross-reference the standalone memory register of notions. | E_n-chiral notion unspecified |
| 277 | "$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ is an $E_3$-operad" (or is invoked as an $E_3$-structure on $A$). | Swiss-cheese $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ is the correct intermediary between $E_1$-chiral and $E_3$; the $E_3$ promotion exists in appropriate cases. | $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ is bicoloured (two object classes: meromorphic-holomorphic disks and topological balls) with asymmetric mixed operations (no closed-to-open action); Dunn additivity $E_2 \otimes E_1 = E_3$ applies to single-colour operads and therefore does NOT identify $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ with $E_3$ on the nose. Promotion to $E_3$ requires an additional hypothesis (a conformal vector / Sugawara construction at non-critical level) that implements the topologization of the holomorphic direction. | State $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ explicitly as the bicoloured intermediary operad. Any "$E_3$" claim must cite the topologization hypothesis (conformal vector, Sugawara at $k \ne -h^\vee$, or general-chiral-algebra CONJECTURE with named scope) and exhibit the chain-level map implementing $E_2 \otimes E_1 \to E_3$ on the derived-centre pair. Compare AP167 (topologization PROVED for affine KM at non-critical level; CONJECTURAL for general). | SC bicoloured vs E_3 single-coloured conflation |
| 278 | "Holographic" applied to a statement (e.g. "boundary-linear bulk", "$E_n$-$E_{n-1}$ holographic duality") without naming the specific bulk-boundary identification at chain level. | The programme's holographic picture $H(T) = (A, A^!, C, r(z), \Theta_A, \nabla^{\mathrm{hol}})$ is a real structure with four recovery theorems, and holography is a genuine organizing principle. | "Holographic" as narrative replaces the named chain-level map with a metaphor. The actual content is: a bulk object (Hochschild cochains / derived centre / $E_n$) recovers a boundary object (algebra / $E_{n-1}$) via an explicit pullback along a specified inclusion of operads, with specified homotopy data (r-matrix, MC element, flat connection). Without the explicit map, "holographic" is rhetorical. | Every "holographic" / "bulk-boundary" / "open-closed" claim must name: (i) which object is bulk, which is boundary, (ii) the specific operadic inclusion $\mathcal{O}_{\partial} \hookrightarrow \mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{bulk}}$ or the specific restriction map $Z^{\mathrm{der}}(A) \to A$, (iii) the homotopy data (r-matrix, MC, connection) that witnesses the relation, (iv) the scope (Koszul locus? Global? Proved at formal disk but conjectural at finite-radius disk?). The global boundary-linear-bulk triangle is CONJECTURAL beyond the Koszul locus. | holography as narrative without operadic map |

| 306 | Convergence of an attack-heal cycle (or a rectification / audit / investigation loop) is declared after the first-pass hostile review returns silent, i.e., after one attack$\to$heal pass without a subsequent re-attack on the heal. | Hostile review really does certify robustness when the reviewer has looked hard enough, and a silent review IS evidence of robustness. Single-pass methodology is the minimal honest procedure, the one that catches the most visible error. | Silence from the first-pass hostile review conflates two distinct possibilities: (i) the reviewer found no obstruction because none exists, versus (ii) the reviewer found no obstruction because the healed layer has not yet been re-attacked with the depth that produced the original heal. The convergence criteria (materially stronger than baseline; no remaining obstruction in stated scope; every scope qualifier paired with boundary-obstruction content per AP275; strongest honest form per AP289; $\ge 3$ independent paths per numerical claim) are cumulative over iterations. A first heal reliably introduces a second-order obstruction -- a new scope qualifier without obstruction content, a defensive downgrade where a broader honest form exists on disk, a path-count that is $2$ not $3$ -- that only the re-attack layer surfaces. AP275 and AP289 are downstream symptoms of exactly this single-pass incompleteness. AP306 is CROSS-INDEXED with AP293 (premature-convergence via relabelling): AP306 flags the METHODOLOGICAL root (first-pass silence conflated with robustness), AP293 flags the SURFACE symptom (bookkeeping sweeps masquerading as mathematical progress); both must be absent for honest convergence. | Declare convergence only after the iterated cycle attack $\to$ heal $\to$ hostile-reviewer-re-attack the heal $\to$ re-heal $\to$ repeat reaches a fixed point where ALL six criteria simultaneously hold: (a) mathematics verifiably MATERIALLY STRONGER than the pre-attack baseline; (b) no remaining unresolved obstruction in the stated scope; (c) every inscribed proof hostile-reviewer-robust under iterated re-attack; (d) every numerical claim verified by $\ge 3$ genuinely independent paths (direct computation / alternative formula / limiting case / symmetry-duality / cross-family; literature is sanity not substitute); (e) every scope qualifier paired with the obstruction-content at its boundary (AP275); (f) never downgrade (AP289) -- inscribe the strongest honest form, closed ambients named, explicit all-weight corrections inscribed rather than scope-qualified away, per-family verifications enumerated rather than hidden behind "conjectural at programme level"; (g) AP293-negative -- the final report exhibits at least one of a new $\backslash\texttt{begin\{lemma|proposition|theorem|corollary\}}$ block with proof body, a falsifying parameter point, a sharpened hypothesis with rewritten proof body, or a $\backslash\texttt{cite}$ repair unlocking a $[?]$. A single attack-heal pass is INCOMPLETE by construction; its output is the "visible correction" layer, not the "invariant-under-re-attack" layer. | single-pass attack-heal declared convergent (methodological root of AP275 and AP289; surface-symptom partner of AP293) |
| 307 | One symbol $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(X)$ stands for both the Hodge supertrace $\sum_{q=0}^{d}(-1)^{q}h^{0,q}(X)=\chi(\cO_X)$ and the operational K\"unneth-additive chiral modular characteristic of the quantum chiral algebra $\Phi_d(D^b\Coh(X))$, and the identity $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(X)=\chi(\cO_X)$ is claimed globally on compact CY$_d$. | On the proved CY$_2$ slice with $h^{1,0}(X)=0$, the Serre-duality parity argument does kill the one-loop correction and the two invariants coincide at $\chi(\cO_X)$; the Hodge supertrace is genuinely what Serre-theoretic machinery computes; the K\"unneth-additive characteristic is what the product route and Mukai-rank computations produce; each is a real Vol~III invariant with its own compute-layer verification. | Two invariants are collapsed into one symbol. The Hodge supertrace $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{Hodge}}(X):=\sum_q(-1)^q h^{0,q}(X)=\chi(\cO_X)$ is \emph{K\"unneth-multiplicative}: $\chi(\cO_{X\times Y})=\chi(\cO_X)\cdot\chi(\cO_Y)$. The operational chiral modular characteristic $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(X)$ appearing in the product / Mukai-rank route is \emph{K\"unneth-additive}: $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(X\times Y)=\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(X)+\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(Y)$. The two functions cannot coincide on products of spaces with nonzero invariants. Concrete counterexample: on $K3\times E$ in complex dimension $3$, $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{Hodge}}(K3\times E)=\chi(\cO_{K3})\cdot\chi(\cO_E)=2\cdot 0=0$ while $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(K3\times E)=\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(K3)+\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(E)=2+1=3$. The naive identity therefore fails already at $d=3$ on the simplest K3-fibred product. The Vol~III compute layer reflects this split: \texttt{test\_kappa\_spectrum\_reconciliation.py} (44 passed) treats $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(K3\times E)=3$ as the operational chiral characteristic and separates it from $\chi(\cO)=0$; \texttt{test\_cy\_d\_kappa\_stratification.py} (39 passed) treats the Hodge supertrace as a separate scalar. Using one symbol for both invariants silently propagates a false identity across the manuscript. The Beauville--Bogomolov tri-stratum is sharp: odd $d$ gives $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{Hodge}}=0$ by Serre cancellation but leaves bare $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$ unconstrained; even strict CY gives $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{Hodge}}=2$ (Serre-duality endpoint contribution from $h^{0,0}+(-1)^d h^{0,d}$); irreducible holomorphic-symplectic of dimension $2n$ gives $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{Hodge}}=n+1$ (generated by $1,\sigma,\ldots,\sigma^n$). The three strata are disjoint and the bare-$\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$ / Hodge-supertrace coincidence is proved only on the CY$_2$ slice with $h^{1,0}=0$. | Every Vol~III $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$ appearance must disambiguate: write $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{Hodge}}(X)$ for the Serre supertrace $\sum_q(-1)^q h^{0,q}$, and keep bare $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$ exclusively for the K\"unneth-additive operational chiral modular characteristic produced by $\Phi_d(D^b\Coh(X))$. State the coincidence $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(A_\cC)=\chi(\cO_X)$ only within the proved $d=2$, $h^{1,0}=0$ slice (Vol~III Theorem CY-D item (i)); at $d\ge 3$, state the Beauville--Bogomolov tri-stratum comparison explicitly with the $K3\times E$ witness inscribed ($\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{Hodge}}=0$ vs $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}=3$). Summary tables must carry separate columns for the two invariants. Do not close \texttt{conj:cy-kappa-identification} on the basis of the naive identity -- the chapter proves the obstruction to the naive form, not its closure. | 318 | Reader-facing manuscript prose pontificates about previous incorrect versions or historical author-errors: ``The naive six-way isomorphism of the original CY-C is therefore falsified'', ``The earlier hypothesis $D_K = 18^{K-1}$ was refuted at $K = 3$'', ``the earlier $\fgl(4 \mid 20)$ designation is a misnomer'', ``previously it was conjectured that...'', ``in an earlier formulation...'', ``X is refuted by the data, unlike the original claim of...''. | Falsifying a naive ansatz, a competing definition, or a plausible-looking guess is a real mathematical act — and standalone-rigorous exposition must compare against the naive guess to motivate the correct definition. Beilinson's dictum (``what limits forward progress is the inability to dismiss false ideas'') is a correct epistemic discipline. | The error is orienting the comparison along the author's own historical timeline rather than along mathematical naivety. A reader of a standalone monograph has no access to (and no interest in) the manuscript's prior drafts, earlier conjectures, or retractions; naming them as ``the original X'', ``the earlier Y'', ``formerly claimed Z'' imports the author's memoir into the reader's space. It reads as apologetic signposting rather than mathematics, and it dates the manuscript: a reader three years later has no referent for ``the original CY-C''. The same falsification content can be expressed as a mathematical comparison with a NAIVE GUESS (a reader-level candidate, not an author-timeline candidate); this is stronger because the naive-guess comparison is timeless, reader-facing, and substantiates the correct definition. The prose template ``Naively one might expect X; Y obstructs this; instead, Z holds'' is the reader-facing form; ``the original W was wrong; we now know V'' is the author-facing form. | Manuscript prose replaces every historical-author-timeline phrasing with a naive-candidate comparison: \emph{instead of} ``The earlier hypothesis $D_K = 18^{K-1}$ was refuted at $K = 3$'', \emph{write} ``A naive exponential ansatz $D_K = 18^{K-1}$ would predict $D_3 = 324$; the direct value $D_3 = 972$ rules it out, and the sequence is governed instead by~\ldots''. \emph{Instead of} ``the earlier $\fgl(4 \mid 20)$ designation is a misnomer'', \emph{write} the correct label with a sentence on why the alternative fails on the form-structure. \emph{Instead of} ``The naive six-way isomorphism of the original CY-C is falsified'', \emph{write} ``Naively one might expect all six routes to assemble into a single Hopf object; the generator-rank stratification $\rho^{R_i} \in \{3, 12, 24\}$ obstructs the common quotient''. Each instance gets rewritten as a naive-candidate comparison or deleted. The manuscript is a standalone mathematical object, not a commentary on its own history. Related: AP186 (shallow correction vs substantive heal), AP312 (author-discipline jargon leakage). | AI-slop: reader-facing prose pontificates about past author errors / retracted claims / earlier versions |

Distinguish $\Phi_{10}$ (K3 $\times$ E, $\mathrm{Sp}_4(\mathbb{Z})$, hyperbolic $\Lambda^{2,1}_{II}$) from $\Phi_{12}$ (Fake Monster Lie algebra, $II_{25,1}$ Leech lattice) — different weights, different lattices, different Langlands duals. Every Vol III appearance of "K3 Yangian" must disambiguate (A) vs (B); every appearance of "BKM" must state whether it is a Lie algebra or Lie SUPERalgebra (the $\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}$ case is super). | W16-c2d-prime-107-factorisation | c_{2d}(A_1, Sigma_{0,24}, all max) = -312 = -24 * 13 with 13 = c_{4d}/2 interpretable as the bosonic-string critical dimension and 24 = chi(K3). | The Beem-Rastelli factor c_{2d} = -12 c_{4d} is correct; the class-S evaluation on Sigma_{0,24} is a well-defined number. | The Wave-14 ansatz c_{4d}(A_1, Sigma_{g,n}) = (12(g-1) + 7n)/6 giving c_{4d} = 26 at (0,24) fails the SU(2) N_f = 4 cross-check: at (0,4) it returns 8/3 whereas Shapere-Tachikawa 2008 Tab 4 and Tachikawa 2013 eq (13.6) give 7/6. The integer 107 is PRIME, so -214 admits no non-trivial integer factorisation apart from -2 * 107. The earlier "-24 * 13 = -312" numerology is a false-because-wrong-ansatz cache trap. Shadow tower at c = -214: S_2 = -107, S_3 = 2, S_4 = 5/112136, S_5 = 3/3000319; Zamolodchikov norm = 22427.2 > 0 (class M, generic stratum). Class-M heptagon face robust under -312 -> -214 retraction: both values in generic class-M stratum (nonvanishing 5c+22, S_4, Q_c irreducible). | W16-siegel-weight-5-vs-elliptic-integer | Mock-modular weight at K3 base point equals -c_{2d}/24 = 107/12. | Chiral partition function is a mock-modular form on some modular group. | 107/12 is NOT an integer, so the naive Cardy-regime weight -c/24 reading as an elliptic modular weight on SL_2(Z) fails type-check. | Correct modular covariance is SIEGEL (on Sp_4(Z)) not elliptic: partition function is a Siegel modular form of weight 5 on the Gritsenko-Nikulin double cover of Sp_4(Z), identified with Delta_5 = Phi_{10}^{1/2}. The bridge elliptic <-> Siegel is the Humbert-H_1 restriction, under which Delta_5 descends to a weight-5 Jacobi form of elliptic index 1 (NOT a weight-107/12 scalar modular form). | W17-BKM-Gram-principal-minor-vs-eigenvalues | Signature of the rank-3 Feingold-Frenkel hyperbolic Gram matrix G_BKM (entries {2,-2,-2}, symmetric) can be read off Sylvester's principal minors. | The rank-3 Gram is real symmetric, so its signature is a well-defined invariant; principal-minor tests DO work for strictly positive-definite matrices (leading minors all > 0 iff positive-definite). | The principal-minor ladder for G_BKM is (2, 0, -32): the 2x2 leading minor vanishes because alpha_1 + alpha_2 is isotropic in the {alpha_1, alpha_2}-subspace. Sylvester's criterion requires non-degenerate leading minors; when the 2x2 minor is exactly 0, Sylvester is silent and reading the signature from the ladder is invalid. A hasty Sylvester read would give (+, 0, -) which conflates with signature (1, 1, 1) or (2, 1, 0) -- the wrong answer is "hyperbolic with one null direction" rather than "hyperbolic (2,1) with isotropic 2-plane combination". | Compute eigenvalues directly: char poly = -lambda^3 + 6 lambda^2 - 32 has real roots {+4, +4, -2}, so signature is (2, 1). The isotropic combination alpha_1 + alpha_2 (giving m_2 = 0) is an artifact of the S_3-symmetric Cartan structure, NOT a null direction in the ambient (2,1)-Lorentzian form. Cross-verify via Gritsenko-Nikulin 1998 Thm 1.1: BKM g_{Delta_5} has real-root lattice II_{2,1} by construction (paramodular weight 5 via singular-theta lift on O(2,1) Grassmannian), so signature (2,1) is FORCED by the Borcherds lift independent of the eigenvalue computation. Primary: Feingold-Frenkel 1983 Math Ann 263 Thm 1.1; Gritsenko-Nikulin 1998 AJM 120 Thm 1.1; Kac 1990 Infinite Dim Lie Algebras Ch 14. | principal-minor-vs-eigenvalue-signature |
| W17-positive-energy-unitarity-vs-ambient-indefiniteness | "Unitary module of H_Delta5" means positive-definite inner product on the whole BKM representation. | Unitarity is a real, well-defined invariant for highest-weight modules over Kac-Moody and BKM algebras; there exist unitary highest-weight modules in this setting. | For a BKM algebra with hyperbolic Cartan, the BKM inner product is INDEFINITE Hermitian: signature (infty real-root positive, infty imaginary-root negative). No finite positive-definite projection captures the full BKM content; "unitary module" as a global Hilbert-space statement is impossible. | Unitarity statements must specify: (a) SUBMODULE SCOPE (real-root sector, positive-definite 2-plane P subset Cartan of signature (2,1) per W17-BKM-Gram) and (b) WEIGHT CONSTRAINT (lambda in P^*_+ AND (lambda, lambda) > 0; spacelike condition). Positive-energy unitary representations are {V^lambda : lambda in P^*_+, (lambda, lambda) > 0}, constructed as Frenkel-Kac vertex algebras on the positive-definite rank-2 lattice. Imaginary-root representations (timelike (lambda, lambda) < 0) are NOT unitary -- negative-norm ground state. The Fricke-fixed sub-MTC is Z/2-graded, fixed points projectively self-dual. Primary: Frenkel-Kac 1980 Invent Math 62; Frenkel-Lepowsky-Meurman 1988 Sec 8.8; Borcherds 1992 Invent 109 Sec 4; Gebert-Nicolai 1995 arXiv:hep-th/9504153 Sec 3; Kac 1990 Ch 14. | unitarity-scope-real-vs-imaginary-root |
| W17-CY2-landscape-dichotomy-Siegel-weight-linear | Every CY-2 surface X has a $\Phi_2$-image with a Siegel-cusp-form denominator, generalising $\Delta_5$ for K3. | The Kodaira-Enriques classification of CY-2 surfaces (K3, $T^4$, Enriques, bielliptic) plus the non-CY half-K3 $\mathrm{dP}_9$ is complete; each surface has a well-defined $\Phi_2$-image under the CY-to-chiral functor. | Only two surfaces (K3 and Enriques) produce Siegel cusp forms. $T^4$ / bielliptic have $\chi_{\mathrm{top}} = 0$ so the Borcherds multiplicative lift of the elliptic genus is trivial; $\mathrm{dP}_9$ has $c_1 \ne 0$ and lattice signature $(1,9)$ which fails the Borcherds-weight-5 requirement (needs signature $(2,10)$). Asserting a universal Siegel-cusp-form replacement conflates taxa. | CY-$2$ dichotomy (4-taxon partition): (a) K3 and Kummer K3: fourth taxon, Siegel weight $5$, $\Delta_5$ on $\mathrm{Sp}_4$ (K3 full; Kummer as Picard-sublattice restriction via Mukai 1984). (b) Enriques: fourth-taxon / $\mathbb{Z}/2$-gauge, Siegel weight $5/2$ metaplectic on paramodular $K(2)$, $\Delta_5^{\mathrm{Enr}}$ via Gritsenko-Nikulin 1998 Thm 5.2 singular theta lift on $\mathrm{II}_{2,10}(2)$. (c) $T^4$ / bielliptic: taxon G (abelian Heisenberg), $V_{\mathrm{II}_{4,4}}$ Narain VOA, weight 0, no Siegel lift (Nahm-Wendland 2001 Thm 4.1). (d) $\mathrm{dP}_9$: taxon L (affine KM), $\widehat{E_8}_{k=1}$ from 12-$I_1$-fibre $II^*$-collision, weight 0 (Seiberg 1988 Sec 3; Morrison-Vafa 1996 II Sec 4). Linear weight formula on the fourth-taxon column: $w_{\mathrm{Borch}}(X) = 5 \cdot \chi_{\mathrm{top}}(X) / 24$. The Wave-15 specificity hypothesis $(\chi, c_1, h^{2,0}) = (24, 0, 1)$ is the unique triple realising integer weight 5 on the fourth taxon. Primary: Borcherds 1998 Invent 132 Thm 10.1; Gritsenko-Nikulin 1998 J reine angew Math 507 Thm 5.2; Hulek-Sankaran 2011 Algebra Number Theory 5 Thm 3.4; Nahm-Wendland 2001 Commun Math Phys 216 Thm 4.1; Seiberg 1988 Phys Lett B 206 Sec 3; Mukai 1984 Nagoya Math J 81 Thm 1; Seidel-Smith 2010 Duke Math J 134 (Enriques equivariant Fukaya). | CY-2-landscape-4-taxon-partition |
| W17-Siegel-weight-kN-spin-vs-honest | "$k_N = (N+3)/2$" and "$k_N = N+3$" are both asserted as Siegel weights of $\Delta_{k_N}^{(N)}$ on $\mathrm{O}(\Lambda^{N+1,2})$ for $\mathcal T[A_{N-1}, \Sigma_{0,24}]$; these differ by a factor of 2. | Borcherds 1998 Thm 13.3 gives one well-defined Siegel weight per Jacobi input; the Jacobi form has a well-defined constant Fourier coefficient; the class-S family has well-defined Gaiotto pants data. | The two weights refer to DIFFERENT modular-form avatars on DIFFERENT covering groups of $\mathrm{O}(\Lambda^{N+1,2} \oplus \mathrm{II}_{2,2})$: spin cover vs orthogonal group proper. Writing "$k_N$" without the cover is scope-ambiguous. At $N = 2$ the classical Gritsenko-Nikulin 1998 $\Delta_5$ has weight 5 honestly; its square root $\Delta_5^{1/2}$ of weight 5/2 lives on the metaplectic cover (Mp). | Canonical disambiguation: (honest) $k_N = f^{(N)}(0, 0)/2 = N + 3$ on $\mathrm{O}(\Lambda^{N+1,2} \oplus \mathrm{II}_{2,2})$; (spin cover) $k_N = (N+3)/2$ on $\mathrm{Mp}(\Lambda^{N+1,2} \oplus \mathrm{II}_{2,2})$. Values (spin): $k_2 = 5/2, k_3 = 3, k_4 = 7/2, k_5 = 4, k_6 = 9/2$. The constant Fourier coefficient $f^{(N)}(0, 0) = 2(N+3)$ is derived in Vol II Wave 17 Proposition (Eguchi-Hikami 2009 eq (4.12); Benini-Peelaers 2015 Sec 5; Cordova-Shao 2015 Sec 4). Verification module: `k3_yangian_wave15_schur_index_classS_ANm1_24.py`, 47 passing tests. | W17-Niemeier-breakdown-at-N6 | The umbral moonshine labelling $X_N = (24/N) A_{N-1}$ extends the Mathieu-moonshine $24 A_1$ observation to all $N \ge 2$ indefinitely. | Cheng-Duncan-Harvey 2014 Tab 1 gives a finite list of 23 Niemeier lattices each attached to an umbral group; every Niemeier lattice has root-system rank 24. | At $N = 6$, the hypothetical root system $4 A_5$ is NOT among the 23 Niemeier root systems (Niemeier 1973 list; Conway-Sloane 1988 Ch 16). The systematic labelling $(24/N) A_{N-1}$ breaks: $N = 6$ admits no Niemeier lattice with root system $4 A_5$. Asserting the labelling extends indefinitely is a classification error. | Valid labelling range: $N \in \{2, 3, 4, 5\}$ with root systems $24 A_1, 12 A_2, 8 A_3, 6 A_4$ and umbral groups $M_{24}, 2.M_{12}, 2.\mathrm{AGL}_3(2), \mathrm{GL}_2(5)/\{\pm 1\}$ respectively. At $N = 6$ the nearest-rank substitute is $6 D_4$ (Niemeier with $3.\mathrm{Sym}_6$ umbral group, order 2160), but the $A_5$-fugacity identification must be rederived. Wave 17 theorem statement therefore unconditional at $N \in \{2, 3, 4, 5\}$, conditional-on-labelling-choice at $N = 6$. | W17-c-eff-negative-as-anomaly-not-entanglement | At c_eff = -166, the Calabrese-Cardy entropy S_EE = (c_eff/3) log(L/eps) = -(166/3) log(L/eps) is a bona fide negative entanglement entropy of H_Delta5. | Calabrese-Cardy entanglement law is universal for 2d CFTs with central charge c; c_eff replaces c in non-unitary / negative-c_{2d} situations for partition functions (Cardy counting per W16-c2d). | Entanglement entropy S = -tr(rho log rho) is non-negative by construction; a negative coefficient c_eff/3 < 0 cannot be a physical entanglement entropy on a Hilbert space. Conflates "partition-function coefficient" (which CAN be negative for non-unitary CFTs) with "entanglement entropy of a Hilbert-space density matrix" (which CANNOT). | Separate the two readings: (i) c_eff/3 log(L/eps) is the GRAVITATIONAL/TOPOLOGICAL ANOMALY coefficient governing the holographic dual's topological entanglement (Manschot-Moore 2007; DVV 1997 anti-holomorphic counting); (ii) the genuine unitary entanglement comes from the real-root submodule V^unit with rank-2 lattice central charge c_unit = rk(P) = 2, giving positive Calabrese-Cardy S = (2/3) log(L/eps) > 0. The negative c_eff = -166 quantifies HOW FAR H_Delta5 is from a unitary CFT, not an entropy. On Humbert divisors H_1 and H_4 (off the Koszul locus), the hyperbolic Cartan degenerates to full-rank-collapse, unitarity breaks on real-root sector too, and logarithmic-CFT corrections c_log log^2(L/eps) appear. | W18-wall-of-walls-commutator-obstruction-vs-Malcev-cocycle | The non-vanishing commutator class [gamma_i, gamma_j] in H^2_et(H_i cap H_j, Z/N_{ij}) at the codimension-2 wall-of-walls of the Humbert stratum in Abar_2 is an obstruction to strict chain-level bar-cobar inversion of H_Delta5; consequently strict chain-level inversion is impossible at the wall-of-walls. | The commutator class is real, nonzero, and computed via Bruinier cup Kuga-Satake / Bruinier cup pentagon / pentagon cup Kuga-Satake; it genuinely obstructs the pro-object Mayer-Vietoris gluing in the single-monodromy-refined pro-ambient of Definition monodromy-refined-total-bar-weight. | Treating the commutator class as an absolute obstruction conflates two ambients: (i) the single-monodromy-refined pro-ambient (where the class is an obstruction); (ii) the Deligne-Malcev bi-unipotent pro-ambient (where the class is the classifying cocycle of the Malcev extension of the bi-unipotent structure, and the Schmid-Cattani-Kaplan commuting-sl_2-triples canonically split it). An obstruction-in-ambient-X is not an obstruction-in-ambient-Y when Y strictly refines X. Pattern-236 / Pattern-269 scope discipline. | The commutator class is the classifying cocycle of a Malcev extension; strict chain-level inversion holds in the Deligne-Malcev bi-unipotent pro-ambient (Definition def:deligne-malcev-bi-unipotent-ambient of chapter mc5_class_m_chain_level_platonic.tex) via the curvature-corrected bi-graded Bott-Koszul chain homotopy h^{(chi_i,chi_j,k_i,k_j)}_{H_i cap H_j} = M^{(chi_i,chi_j)} (N_i + N_j + lambda_{k_i,k_j})^{-1} (id + sigma h^{(g)})^{-1} sigma (eq:wall-of-walls-chain-homotopy). The chain-homotopy identity [d^{Gamma tensor Gamma}, h^{Gamma tensor Gamma}] = id - p^{Gamma tensor Gamma} (eq:wall-of-walls-chain-homotopy-identity) holds, and Mittag-Leffler on the bi-graded tower follows from finite-dimensionality of gr^{k_i, k_j}_W F^{<=w, chi_i, chi_j}. The pentachotomy of Corollary cor:sharpened-quadrichotomy-after-monodromy-refinement is upgraded to a hexachotomy, and global strict chain-level bar-cobar inversion holds on the full Humbert stratum H_1 cup H_3 cup H_4 in the (single-refined / bi-refined) pro-ambient cover. Primary: Schmid 1973 Invent Math 22 Thm 4.9; Cattani-Kaplan-Schmid 1986 Ann Math 123 Sec 2.1; Deligne 1970 Equations Differentielles Sec 5; Bruinier 2002 LNM 1780 Prop 5.1; Morrison 1984 Invent Math 75; Positselski 2011 Mem AMS 212 Sec 3-4; Igusa 1972 Theorems on Siegel Sec 4; Saito MHM 1988 App A; Vol I chapters/theory/mc5_class_m_chain_level_platonic.tex Theorem thm:mc5-wall-of-walls-strict-chain-level. | wall-of-walls-Malcev-cocycle-ambient-refinement |
| W19-phi-n-four-conflicting-objects | Bare $\phi^{(n)}$ is used for all of: (i) the Drinfeld associator coefficient, (ii) the KZ period on $M_{0,4}$, (iii) a shadow-tower entry $S_r$, (iv) the Etingof-Kazhdan pentagon coboundary of nilpotent_completion.tex. | Each of the four notions is a real construction and appears at distinct points in the programme; naming them uniformly "$\phi^{(n)}$" is a local convenience. | The four objects are genuinely different: (i) lives in the group-like completion of the free Lie algebra on two generators with MZV coefficients; (ii) is a scalar function on $M_{0,4}$ given by iterated integration; (iii) is a rational function of the chiral central charge $c$ (Virasoro) or level $k$ (affine KM); (iv) is the Maurer-Cartan obstruction at $\hbar^n$ in the super-Drinfeld associator expansion, normalised by $n!$. They have different ambient categories, different normalisations, different scopes, and different growth rates. Using the bare label "$\phi^{(n)}$" for all four invites AP113/AP152/AP160-style bare-label confusions: statements proved for one notion silently transport to another where they fail. | The programme's canonical $\phi^{(n)}$ is notion (iv), the Etingof-Kazhdan pentagon coboundary, as fixed by Definition def:phi-n-pent-EK in chapters/theory/shadow_tower_higher_coefficients.tex. The MZV leg is $(1/n!)\sum_{i=1}^{d_n} c_n^{(i)}\,\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ in the Brown-Deligne canonical basis, with $c_n^{(i)} = 1$ from the Drinfeld-Deligne duality (Brown 2012 Thm 4.1). The Borcherds leg $(1/n!)\Phi_{10}^{n/2}\eta^{-12n} c_n^{(K3)}$ is K3-lattice-specific, with $c_n^{(K3)}$ Hardy-Ramanujan-bounded. For $n \le 12$ the MZV leg is unconditional (Brown 2011 Thm 1.1, Thm 1.2); for $n = 13$ it is unconditional through depth 3 and Broadhurst-Kreimer-trivial above; for $n \ge 14$ it is conditional on the Zagier-Hoffman depth-reduction conjecture (Brown 2012 arXiv:1301.3053 Conj. 2). Every bare "$\phi^{(n)}$" must name the notion from (i)-(iv) and its ambient. Verification module: `compute/lib/wave19_phi_n_extension_weight11_12_13.py` (20 tests + 8 multi-path cross-checks); anchor $\zeta(3,3,3,3)\approx 2.959990\cdot 10^{-4}$ (Richardson-extrapolated, matches MZDP to 12 digits). Primary: Drinfeld 1990; Etingof-Kazhdan 2000 Sel Math 6; Brown 2011 Ann Math 175 Thm 1.1, Thm 1.2; Brown 2012 arXiv:1301.3053 Thm 4.1, Conj 2; Brown 2017 arXiv:1709.02856; Deligne 2013 Bourbaki 1054; Broadhurst-Kreimer 1997 hep-th/9609128; Zagier 1994 Progr. | W18-ambient-refinement-principle-chain-level-bar-cobar | "Strict chain-level bar-cobar inversion fails on locus L" is an ambient-independent statement. | A strict chain-level quasi-isomorphism is a well-defined notion in Ch(Vect), in pro-Ch(Vect), and in every refinement thereof; each ambient produces a well-defined yes/no for inversion on a given locus L. | "Fails on L" is actually ambient-dependent. Strict chain-level inversion can fail in a coarser pro-ambient and hold in a finer pro-ambient that retains more of the geometric data (conformal weight filtration, monodromy filtration, bi-monodromy bi-filtration). The locus L together with the ambient is what carries the yes/no datum. Writing "fails on L" without the ambient qualifier is Pattern-236 scope conflation. | Every chain-level bar-cobar inversion statement is ambient-qualified. The hexachotomy of Remark rem:wall-of-walls-obstruction-as-extension-class of chapter mc5_class_m_chain_level_platonic.tex gives six ambient readings for H_Delta5 on Abar_2: (1) fibrewise on generic points of U; (2) single-monodromy-refined pro-ambient on O_hat^circ_{H_1 cup H_3 cup H_4}; (3) Deligne-Malcev bi-unipotent pro-ambient on the wall-of-walls O_hat_{H_i cap H_j}; (4) weight-completed coderived on Abar_2; (5) A_infty-corrected on a neighbourhood of H_3; (6) (infty,1)-categorical in Perf(Abar_2) via Deligne nearby cycles. Each reads the bar-cobar counit as a strict / weight-completed / A_infty-corrected / (infty,1)-categorical quasi-isomorphism in its respective ambient; the six ambients form a partial order of refinements, and statements transport upward. Primary: Positselski 2011 Mem AMS 212; Schmid 1973; Cattani-Kaplan-Schmid 1986; Vol I chapters/theory/mc5_class_m_chain_level_platonic.tex Corollary cor:global-strict-bar-cobar-humbert-stratum. | chain-level-ambient-refinement |
| W19-LDP-variance-inverse-density-vs-curvature | The Gaussian variance $\sigma_k^2$ in the local LDP rate $I_k(\theta^*_k + \delta) = \delta^2/(2\sigma_k^2) + O(\delta^3)$ for Fricke-phase clustering at node $\theta^*_k = k\pi/8$ coincides with the density curvature $|\rho''(\theta^*_k)|^{-1}$, giving $\sigma_k^2 = (\pi^2/2)\cos^{-2}(\theta^*_k)$. | The density-curvature coefficient $\cos(2\theta^*_k)$ and the LDP Cramér variance are both genuine quantities attached to the Sato--Tate density $\rho(\theta) = (2/\pi)\sin^2\theta$ at a fixed angle. | Density-curvature (second Taylor coefficient of $\rho$) governs the behaviour of the density itself; the LDP variance governs the entropy cost of a fluctuation. They are related but not equal. The Gärtner--Ellis quadratic LDP at an interior point where $\rho > 0$ yields $\sigma_k^2 = \rho(\theta^*_k)^{-1}$ (inverse density, Bayes-type), not $|\rho''|^{-1}$; the proposed $\cos^{-2}$ formula diverges at $k = 2, 6$ where $\cos(2\theta^*_k) = 0$ even though the density is finite and positive there, proving the formula wrong. | At interior nodes $k \in \{1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7\}$ the correct Gaussian LDP curvature is $\sigma_k^2 = \pi/(2\sin^2(\theta^*_k))$ (three-path verified via: Cramér-transform Legendre, Sanov relative-entropy Taylor expansion, empirical-histogram Bayes/inverse-density). Values: $\sigma_1^2 = \sigma_7^2 = \pi/(2\sin^2(\pi/8)) \approx 10.73$; $\sigma_2^2 = \sigma_6^2 = \pi$; $\sigma_3^2 = \sigma_5^2 = \pi/(2\sin^2(3\pi/8)) \approx 1.84$; $\sigma_4^2 = \pi/2 \approx 1.57$. At boundary nodes $k \in \{0, 8\}$ where $\rho = 0$, the Gaussian expansion degenerates and the LDP shifts to Poisson regime with $I^{\mathrm{Poi}}_0(t) = t\log(t/\mu_0) - t + \mu_0$, $\mu_0(\delta) = (2/(3\pi))\delta^3$. Scope: unconditional for $\Delta_{E_6} = f_{16}$ (non-CM cuspidal GL_2/Q eigenform) via Newton--Thorne 2021 Thm A establishing Sym$^n$ automorphy for all $n \ge 1$, removing the Barnet-Lamb--Geraghty--Harris--Taylor 2011 conditional hypothesis. Primary: Dembo--Zeitouni 2010 \emph{Large Deviations Techniques} 2e Thm 2.1.4, Thm 4.2.1, Thm 6.2.10, §3.7; Barnet-Lamb--Geraghty--Harris--Taylor 2011 Publ IHÉS 108 Thm B (effective Sato--Tate, conditional on Sym$^n$); Newton--Thorne 2021 Publ IHÉS 134 Thm A (unconditional Sym$^n$); Taylor 2008 Publ IHÉS 108 (Sato--Tate for modular forms); Lamzouri 2019 J Reine Angew Math 744 (L-function moment asymptotics). Vol I chapters/theory/shadow_tower_quadrichotomy_platonic.tex Theorem thm:stqp-fricke-z8-ldp (this inscription). | LDP-variance-inverse-density |

The $\mu_{16}$-refinement is orthogonal to the two-$\hbar$ AP151 bridge: $\hbar_{\mathrm{qg}}^2 = -1/8$ is invariant under $\zeta^{16}\to\zeta^8$ sheet-descent. | W19-chenevier-pseudocharacter-source-algebra ⟂ retracted per canonical preamble: see Chenevier determinant (W25 / Pattern 295 in `notes/first_principles_cache_comprehensive.md`). Rename $S^{\mathrm{ps}}\to D^{\mathrm{Chen}}$; axioms shift from Taylor--Wiles symmetric-polarisation triple to Chenevier 2014 polynomial law (multiplicativity, unitality, Cayley--Hamilton degree $d$). Source-algebra scope (paramodular Hecke $\mathbb T^{\mathrm{par}}_1$ commutative, NOT chiral bialgebra) preserved unchanged. Original row follows: | A $4$-dimensional pseudo-character $S^{\mathrm{ps}}$ "for $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$" (the chiral bialgebra) encodes the trace data of the Galois representation $\phi_{\Delta_{10}}\colon\mathrm{Gal}(\overline{\mathbb Q}/\mathbb Q)\to\mathrm{GSp}_4$ via $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_1 = \lambda_p$. | Chenevier 2014 (arXiv:1301.0635) pseudo-characters are a real substitute for genuine representations in Taylor-Wiles-style constructions; the SK-lift identity $\lambda_p(\Delta_{10}) = a_p(f_{16}) + p^8 + p^9$ is VERIFIED item 8 of the W19 adjudication ledger; a $4$-dim Galois representation of weight-motif $17$ attached to $\Delta_{10}$ is Taylor 1991 / Weissauer 2005 / Laumon 2005. | Type-confusion: Chenevier pseudo-characters live on COMMUTATIVE algebras mediating a profinite-group-to-representation datum (abstract Hecke algebras, completed group rings of $\mathrm{Gal}$); they are NOT defined on non-commutative chiral bialgebras. $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$ is a non-commutative $A_\infty$-quasi-Hopf chiral bialgebra (W15 item 17 of ledger); its natural "trace" is the BD chiral trace in the sense of Beilinson-Drinfeld 2004 Ch.4, which takes values in chiral modules and satisfies a factorisation-compatible identity, NOT the Chenevier symmetric-multiplicative-dimension axioms. Writing "$S^{\mathrm{ps}}$ on $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$" without the Hecke intermediary conflates a Chenevier pseudo-character on a commutative Hecke algebra with a chiral trace on a non-commutative chiral bialgebra. | Canonical source is the paramodular Hecke algebra $\mathbb T^{\mathrm{par}}_1$ at level $N=1$ (unique newform $\Delta_{10}\in S_{10}(K(1))^{\mathrm{new}}$ by Ibukiyama-Poor-Yuen 2019 IJNT 9 Thm 5.1; Poor-Schmidt-Yuen 2020 Exp Math 29). The $4$-dim $S^{\mathrm{ps}} = (S^{\mathrm{ps}}_1,\dots,S^{\mathrm{ps}}_4)\colon\mathbb T^{\mathrm{par}}_1\to\mathcal O_E\otimes\mathbb Z_\ell$ is given at Hecke generators $T_p$ by: $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_1(T_p) = \lambda_p = a_p + p^8 + p^9$; $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_2(T_p,T_p) = \tfrac{1}{2}(\lambda_p^2 - \lambda_p(T_{p^2})) = p^{15} + (p^8+p^9)a_p + p^{17}$; $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_3(T_p,T_p,T_p) = a_p p^{17} + p^{23} + p^{24}$; $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_4(T_p,T_p,T_p,T_p) = p^{32}$. The reciprocal spinor $L$-factor $\prod(1 - \alpha_i x) = 1 - S^{\mathrm{ps}}_1 x + S^{\mathrm{ps}}_2 x^2 - S^{\mathrm{ps}}_3 x^3 + S^{\mathrm{ps}}_4 x^4$ expands the SK-lift identity $L_p(s,\pi_{\Delta_{10}},\mathrm{spin}) = \zeta_p(s-8)\zeta_p(s-9)L_p(s,f_{16})$. Chenevier axioms (symmetry, multiplicativity, $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_5\circ\mathrm{Alt}_5 = 0$) are automatic from commutativity + Hecke multiplicativity + Cayley-Hamilton at $d = 4$. Deligne-Serre 1974 ENS 7 Sec 8 + Taylor 1991 Duke 63 Thm 2.1 extend $S^{\mathrm{ps}}$ to a genuine $\mathrm{GSp}_4(\mathcal O_E)$-valued Galois representation. Bridge to $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$ is via Satake-Frenkel-Gaitsgory chiralisation on the Koszul locus; chiral extension $S^{\mathrm{ps,ch}}\colon Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5})\to\mathcal O_E\otimes\overline{\mathbb Q}_\ell$ is CONJECTURAL. Verification on 22 primes $p \le 79$ via Hecke table (a_p from DELTA_E6_AP / DELTA_E6_AP_W17 in compute/lib/k3_yangian_wave14_arthur_hecke_delta10.py); Deligne bound $\vert a_p\vert \le 2p^{15/2}$ saturation peak 0.895 at $p = 37$ and 0.8575 at $p = 89$ (W18 extension). | W20-conway-vs-natural-psi-image-commutative-diamond | $V^{s\natural}$ is the 5th image of the universal $\Psi$-functor, on a separate lattice-input row from the four established rows (K3, Enriques, Monster, Fake-Monster), with lattice $\Lambda_{24}$ and parameters $(K, \hbar^2) = (2, -1/2)$ via a super-extension $K^{\mathrm{super}} = 2c_+(\Lambda_{24}\oplus\mathrm{II}_{1,1}^{\mathrm{super}}) = 2$ resolving the degeneracy $c_+(\Lambda_{24}) = 0$. | Duncan 2007 \emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~139, 255--315 (arXiv:math/0502267) constructs $V^{s\natural}$ as the unique self-dual $N{=}1$ SVOA of CFT type at $c = 12$ with $(V^{s\natural})_{1/2} = 0$ and $\mathrm{Aut} = \mathrm{Co}_0$; the construction is the $\mathbb{Z}/2$-orbifold $A(\Lambda_{24})^+\oplus A(\Lambda_{24})^{\mathrm{tw},+}$ of the $24$-generator fermionic vertex superalgebra attached to the Leech lattice. The commutative $\mathbb{Z}/2$-orbifolding diamond $\{V_{\Lambda_{24}}, V^\natural, V_{\Lambda_{24}}^s, V^{s\natural}\}$ (Duncan 2007 \S6) is established; the four-row $\Psi$-landscape K3/Enriques/Monster/Fake-Monster is established. | Three concrete defects in the W19 Witten inscription (k3e_bkm_chapter.tex:4262 \emph{et seq.}): (a) journal venue stated as \emph{Math.\ Res.\ Lett.}~14 but correct venue is \emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~139 (task prompt's "arXiv:math/0605219" is a different Duncan paper; correct Conway arXiv is math/0502267); (b) construction described as "$\mathbb{Z}/2$-orbifold of 24 free fermions at the $E_8$ super-lattice tensored up" but Duncan 2007 \S3--4 uses the fermionic superalgebra $A(\Lambda_{24})$ on the Leech lattice---no $E_8$ super-lattice enters; (c) assignment $c_+(\Lambda_{24}) = 0$ contradicts the programme's universal sign convention (Theorem thm:bkm-universal-identity defines $c_+(L)$ as positive-eigenvalue count; Leech has signature $(24,0)$ so $c_+(\Lambda_{24}) = 24$, giving $K = 48$, $\hbar^2 = -1/48$, not $(2, -1/2)$). | The default W20 reading, consistent with the Duncan 2007 \S6 commutative orbifolding diamond, is that $V^{s\natural}$ is the $\mathbb{Z}/2$-super-twin of $V^\natural$ INSIDE the four-row $\Psi$-landscape (specifically the Monster row, via the diamond), NOT an independent fifth $\Psi$-image; $(K,\hbar^2) = (2,-1/2)$ coincides with Monster's because $V^{s\natural}$ inherits them from $V^\natural$ through the diamond. Alternative reading: Scheithauer 2008 \emph{Invent.\ Math.}~172 Thm~3.2 realises $V^{s\natural}$ as a $\mathbb{Z}/2$-twisted subsector of the Fake-Monster row on $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$ via $\Lambda_{24}\subset\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$. Cache discipline: $\Psi$ gives ONE output per input CATEGORY, so a VOA $V$ advertised as the image of two different $\Psi$-inputs is a symptom that the two inputs coincide under an orbifold-diamond / super-twin relation. Disk state (2026-04-20): Theorem downgraded to Conjecture (conj:bkm-conway-psi-fifth-image); venue corrected; three-reading anomaly recorded in Remark rem:bkm-conway-psi-image-sign-and-diamond; four downstream references updated (cy_categories.tex ×3, k3e_bkm_chapter.tex ×1). Primary: Duncan 2007 \emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~139 arXiv:math/0502267 Thm 1.1, \S3--6; Duncan--Mack-Ono 2015 \emph{Forum Math.~Pi}~3 e10; Scheithauer 2008 \emph{Invent.\ Math.}~172, 563--609 Thm 3.2; Borcherds 1998 \emph{Invent.\ Math.}~132 Thm 13.3; FLM 1988 Ch.~12; Conway 1968 \emph{Bull.\ LMS}~1; Vol III chapters/examples/k3e_bkm_chapter.tex Conjecture conj:bkm-conway-psi-fifth-image and Remarks rem:bkm-conway-psi-image-sign-and-diamond, rem:bkm-conway-monster-fake-monster-triangle; notes/ADJUDICATION_LEDGER_WAVES_14_TO_19.md \S(III.B). | psi-image-vs-orbifold-diamond-twin |
| W19-grt1-BKM-transitivity-scope | $\mathfrak{grt}_1$ acts transitively on the full space $\mathrm{Quant}(\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5})$ of super-EK quantisations of the K3-BKM Lie superalgebra by Drinfeld twist, extending Etingof--Kazhdan 2000 Part V Thm 2.2 (affine KM) verbatim. | EK 2000 Part V Thm 2.2 establishes the affine case: $\mathrm{Quant}(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_{\mathrm{aff}})$ is a torsor over $\exp(\widehat{\mathfrak{grt}}_1)$ under Drinfeld twist; $H^2(\mathfrak{grt}_1; V)$ vanishes for finite-rank affine modules $V$ (Willwacher 2015 Thm 1.1; Schnepper--Willwacher 2017). | The BKM imaginary cone is infinite-dimensional with Hardy--Ramanujan growth $\dim \mathrm{Imag}_N \sim N^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt N)$ (Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 Sec 4; A_infty-tower non-closure, ledger item I.17). Finite-rank EK Part V machinery does not extend verbatim: Drinfeld twist on the associator must converge in a weight-filtered pro-completion, and $H^2(\mathfrak{grt}_1; \widehat{\mathrm{Imag}})$ is not automatically vanishing. The super-quasi-Hopf sign contributes an additional $\mathbb{Z}/2$ factor (EK 2000 Part V Prop 2.1). | The correct transitivity statement is scope-restricted with an explicit obstruction cocycle. (a) Quantisation space: $\mathrm{Quant}^{\mathrm{GN}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5})$ = super-EK quantisations compatible with the Gritsenko--Nikulin automorphic denominator $e^\rho \prod_{\alpha \in \Delta_+^{\mathrm{im}}}(1-e^{-\alpha})^{\mathrm{mult}(\alpha)} = \sum_{w \in W}(-1)^{\ell(w)}w(e^\rho \Delta_5(e^{-\alpha}))$. (b) Obstruction: $\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{GN}} \in H^2(\mathfrak{grt}_1; \widehat{\mathrm{Imag}})$ with explicit cocycle $\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{GN}}([f_a, f_b]) = \sum_{\alpha, \beta \in \Delta_+^{\mathrm{im}}} \langle \mathsf{g}_{a, b}, \alpha^\vee \otimes \alpha\rangle \cdot \mathrm{mult}(\alpha) \cdot [\alpha, \beta]_{\mathrm{Imag}}$, $\mathsf{g}_{a, b}$ the depth-2 Ihara bracket (Furusho 2011 Thm 4), $\mathrm{mult}(\alpha) = c_{K3}(4nm - \ell^2)$. (c) $\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{GN}}$ vanishes on the Koszul locus $\overline{\mathcal{A}_2} \setminus \bigcup_{n \text{ admissible}} H_n$ (Theorem B, W18 Beilinson tightening, ledger II.E): bar--cobar is strict there, the motivic weight filtration on $\widehat{\mathfrak{grt}}_1$ (Brown 2012) aligns with the Borcherds lattice-weight filtration on $\widehat{\mathrm{Imag}}$ via Deligne--Goncharov periods, and Schnepper--Willwacher 2017 graph-complex vanishing in positive depth applies. (d) The quotient $\mathrm{Quant}^{\mathrm{GN, Koszul}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}) / (\mathbb{Z}/2)_{\mathrm{super}}$ by the EK super-sign is a torsor over $\exp(\widehat{\mathfrak{grt}}_1)$. Unconditional through motivic weight 12 ($c_{12}^{(9)} = \zeta(3,3,3,3)/12!$ explicit, Vol I Rem rem:nc-wave19-DNA-c12-explicit); conditional on Zagier--Hoffman depth-reduction above weight 12 (ledger III.A). Three independent verification paths: (V1) affine limit recovers EK 2000 Part V exactly (imaginary cone vanishes on finite-rank affine sub-lattice); (V2) motivic-Galois pairing via Drinfeld--Deligne $\mathfrak{grt}_1 \cong \mathrm{Lie}(\pi_1^{\mathrm{mot, U}})$ gives chain-level numerical anchor at weight 12; (V3) Willwacher graph complex $H^0(\mathrm{GC}_2) = \mathfrak{grt}_1$ plus Schnepper--Willwacher 2017 extension to graph-complex-compatible modules. Primary: Drinfeld 1990 Leningrad J Math 1 Sec 5 Thm A'; Etingof--Kazhdan 2000 Sel Math 6 Part V Thm 2.2, Prop 2.1; Brown 2012 Ann Math 175 Thm 1.2; Willwacher 2015 Invent 200 Thm 1.1; Schnepper--Willwacher 2017; Furusho 2011 Ann Math 174 Thm 4; Kontsevich 2003 Lett Math Phys 66; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 AJM 119 Thm 4.1; Hardy--Ramanujan 1918. | W20-PBW-truncation-count-vs-multiplicity-collapse | At the Borcherds $\rho$-orbit $\mathcal{O}_N$ of the BKM $\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}$ the PBW generator increment $d(N) - d(N-1)$ equals $|c_{\mathrm{K3}}(\Delta_N)|$ interpreted as the root-space dimension (multiplicity) of a single representative imaginary root at $\rho$-level $N$. | The K3 Fourier coefficient $c_{\mathrm{K3}}(\Delta)$ computes BOTH (a) the root-space dimension $\dim\mathfrak{g}_\alpha = \mathrm{mult}(\alpha)$ for a fixed $\alpha$ with $-\alpha^2/2 = \Delta$ (Borcherds 1992 Thm.~10.1 exponent formula), AND (b) the $\rho^N$-coefficient in $\log\Delta_5$ which enumerates the orbit-integrated sum $\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal{O}_N}\mathrm{mult}(\alpha)$ (Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \S3 Thm.~3.1 denominator product). These are two DISTINCT numerical data that coincide only because the Borcherds denominator collapses the double-sum into a single K3 Fourier coefficient. | Conflating "count of positive roots at $\rho$-level $N$" with "multiplicity of a single root" at $\rho$-level $N$ is a category error. At $\rho$-level 1 for $\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}$: three spacelike + one timelike real simple roots each of multiplicity $1$ (Feingold--Frenkel 1983, Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \S3, ledger VERIFIED item 4: signature $(2,1)$ Gram eigenvalues $\{+4,+4,-2\}$, four simples in total carrying the rank-3 real Cartan plus one hyperbolic); at imaginary $\rho$-levels $N \ge 2$, the increment $d(N) - d(N-1) = |c_{\mathrm{K3}}(\Delta_N)|$ is the sum-of-multiplicities over $\mathcal{O}_N$, not a raw root count. Writing "the two negative-norm imaginary generators at $\Delta = -1$" without distinguishing the two equivalent readings (two distinct roots $\times$ multiplicity $1$ vs one root $\times$ multiplicity $2$) is the kind of ambiguity that breaks the Lusztig 1993 Ch.~35.1 PBW accounting downstream. Related AP: count-vs-sum-of-multiplicities. Sign convention trap: the Siegel-domain discriminant $\Delta = 4nm - \ell^2$ on $\Lambda^{2,1}_{II}$ and the Borcherds lattice norm convention $-\alpha^2/2$ agree on imaginary roots ($\alpha^2 \le 0$, $\Delta \ge 0$) but differ for real roots ($\alpha^2 = +2$, $\Delta = -1$): the polar $c_{\mathrm{K3}}(-1) = 2$ is the real-root orbit datum (orbit-count-times-multiplicity), NOT an imaginary root with norm $-2$. | Canonical formulation: at $\rho$-level $N$ the Lusztig-PBW exponent increment is $\Delta d(N) := \sum_{\alpha \in \mathcal{O}_N}\dim\mathfrak{g}_\alpha$, and the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator product collapse identifies this with $|c_{\mathrm{K3}}(\Delta_N)|$. The full truncation dimension is then $\dim_{\mathbb{C}} \mathfrak{u}_{\zeta_8}^{\le N} = 8^{2 d(N) + \mathrm{rank}_{\mathrm{real}}} = 8^{2 d(N) + 3}$, with $d(1) = 2$, $d(2) = 22$, $d(3) = 238$, $d(4) = 366$; the factor-of-2 in the exponent is the Lusztig-$E$/$F$-PBW split, not a count-vs-multiplicity ambiguity. Equivalent accounting $d^{\mathrm{alt}}(N) := 2 d(N)$ under the convention that the sum ranges over all of $\Phi^+ \cup \Phi^-$ recovers the task-prompt formula $8^{d^{\mathrm{alt}}(N) + 3}$; the two differ by a trivial factor of 2 bookkeeping, not by a genuine refinement. The $+3$ in the exponent is $\mathrm{rank}_{\mathrm{real}} = 3$ (signature $(2,1)$, VERIFIED item 4), from the $K$-Cartan PBW slot. Primary: Lusztig 1993 \emph{Introduction to Quantum Groups} Birkh\"auser Ch.~35.1 Prop.~35.1.5; Borcherds 1992 \emph{Invent.}~109 Thm.~10.1 \S2.4; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \emph{St.~Petersburg Math.~J.}~11 \S3 Thm.~3.1 eq.~2.4; Feingold--Frenkel 1983 \emph{Math.~Ann.}~263 Sec.~2; Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa 2011 \texttt{arXiv:1004.0956} Tab.~1 ($c_{\mathrm{K3}}(-1) = 2, c_{\mathrm{K3}}(0) = 20, c_{\mathrm{K3}}(3) = 216, c_{\mathrm{K3}}(4) = -128$); Kerler--Lyubashenko 2001 LMS LNS~262 \S2.3 Lemma~2.3.4. Inscription: Vol~III \texttt{chapters/theory/quantum\_groups\_foundations.tex} Prop.~\texttt{prop:qgf-wave18-truncation-dims} (Step 2 disambiguation), Rem.~\texttt{rem:qgf-wave18-129-vs-7-47-479-735}; ADJUDICATION\_LEDGER\_WAVES\_14\_TO\_19.md \S(III.G) sharpening. | count-vs-multiplicity-Borcherds-collapse |
| W20-phi-n-13-16-Borcherds-MZV-ratio-exact-vs-asymptotic | The Borcherds/MZV leg ratio at $n=10,\ldots,16$ equals the bare Hardy--Ramanujan asymptotic $k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)/d_n$ with $k=\lceil n/2\rceil$, giving values $6.4\cdot 10^9$ at $n=10$ through $5\cdot 10^{13}$ at $n=16$. | The Borcherds leg $c^{(K3)}_n\Phi_{10}^{\lceil n/2\rceil}\eta^{-12n}/n!$ grows at Hardy--Ramanujan rate (Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 Thm 1.5; Hardy--Ramanujan 1918), and the asymptotic functional form is correct. | The bare $k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$ formula omits the Rademacher 1937 leading constant $(4\pi)^{-1}$ and overshoots the exact Fourier coefficient $p_{24}(k)=[q^k]\prod_m(1-q^m)^{-24}$ by a factor $\sim 10^2$ at $k\le 10$. At $k=5$ the asymptotic gives $6.1\cdot 10^6$ whereas $p_{24}(5)=176256$; the ratio $p_{24}(k)/d_n$ at $n=10$ is $35251$, not $6.4\cdot 10^9$. Conflation: asymptotic growth rate (load-bearing for divergence as $n\to\infty$) vs. numerical value at finite $n$ (load-bearing for the stated ratios; requires exact Fourier coefficient or Rademacher sum with subleading terms). | Canonical programme-values (exact, via $p_{24}(k)=[q^k]\prod_m(1-q^m)^{-24}$): $p_{24}(5)=176256$, $p_{24}(6)=1073720$, $p_{24}(7)=5930496$, $p_{24}(8)=30178575$; Padovan $d_{10},\ldots,d_{16}=5,7,9,12,16,21,28$; exact ratios $p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)/d_n$ at $n=10,13,14,15,16$ are $3.53\cdot 10^4, 4.94\cdot 10^5, 3.71\cdot 10^5, 1.44\cdot 10^6, 1.08\cdot 10^6$. Asymptotic form with Rademacher prefactor $(4\pi)^{-1}k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$ overshoots exact by $\sim 10^2$ at $k\le 10$. Verification: compute module \texttt{compute/lib/wave20\_phi\_n\_extension\_weight14\_15\_16.py} functions \texttt{p24\_exact}, \texttt{hardy\_ramanujan\_ratio\_exact}, \texttt{hardy\_ramanujan\_exact\_check}; test \texttt{compute/tests/test\_wave20\_phi\_n\_extension\_weight13\_14\_15\_16.py}. | W20-phi-n-leading-magnitude-offset-by-one | At weights $13,\ldots,16$ the MZV leg $\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$ has leading magnitudes $\sim 2\cdot 10^{-10}, 2\cdot 10^{-11}, 2\cdot 10^{-12}, 10^{-13}$. | The Brown canonical basis has $d_n$ entries at weight $n$ (Padovan $12,16,21,28$); each MZV $\zeta(s_1,\ldots,s_k)$ at weight $n\ge 10$ has value approaching $1$ (since $\zeta(n)\to 1$); the overall $1/n!$ normalisation divides by $6.2\cdot 10^9, 8.7\cdot 10^{10}, 1.3\cdot 10^{12}, 2.1\cdot 10^{13}$ for $n=13,\ldots,16$. | Leading-estimate $d_n\cdot 1/n!$ gives $\phi^{(13)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}\approx 12/(6.2\cdot 10^9)\approx 1.93\cdot 10^{-9}$, $\phi^{(14)}\approx 1.83\cdot 10^{-10}$, $\phi^{(15)}\approx 1.61\cdot 10^{-11}$, $\phi^{(16)}\approx 1.34\cdot 10^{-12}$. Reporting $2\cdot 10^{-10}, 2\cdot 10^{-11}, 2\cdot 10^{-12}, 10^{-13}$ is an off-by-one-row shift corresponding to assuming $d_n/(n+1)!$ instead of $d_n/n!$. The $1/n!$ normalisation is the Etingof--Kazhdan 2000 $(2\pi i)^n/n!$ pentagon-coboundary simplex volume (Shnider--Stasheff 1997 Ch 8), not $(2\pi i)^n/(n+1)!$. | Canonical leading-order single-$\zeta$ approximation: $\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV, lead}} = d_n/n!$ with each MZV valued $\approx 1$. Full-basis correction: $\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}} = (1/n!)\sum_i\zeta(\mathrm{MZV}^{(n)}_i)$ differs from $d_n/n!$ by $\sum_i\zeta_i/d_n$ of order unity. Three verification paths: (V1) \texttt{phi\_n\_mzv\_leading}; (V2) Richardson-extrapolated full basis via \texttt{phi\_n\_richardson\_check} reproducing to $O(10\%)$; (V3) Vermaseren 1999 MZDP depth-$\le 3$ cross-check.
