| W18-enriques-bkm-M12-virtual-not-direct | Since $f_{\mathrm{En}}(0,1) = 5$ is not an $M_{12}$-irreducible dimension (ATLAS p.~32 dims $\{1, 11, 11', 16, 16', 45, 54, 55, 55', 55'', 66, 99, 120, 144, 176\}$), the Enriques BKM $\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}^{\mathrm{Enr}}$ has no $M_{12}$-moonshine whatsoever; the Persson--Volpato 2013 framework is a separate statement that does not resolve the Enriques moonshine question. | The direct falsification (companion entry W18-enriques-bkm-M12-direct-moonshine-fails): $\mathrm{mult}_{\mathrm{En}}(\alpha_0) = 10/2 = 5$ is not a non-negative sum of $M_{12}$ irreducible dimensions, so genuine (multiplicity-free, non-negative-integer) $M_{12}$-moonshine fails. The ATLAS character table is correct; the failure is real. | The two-step failure is not an obstruction to sporadic-moonshine existence; it is an obstruction to the \emph{genuine} (non-negative) character framework. The standard $M_{24}$-moonshine for K3 is itself virtual (Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa 2010 leading coefficient $-2 = -2 V_{\mathrm{triv}}$ is negative; Gannon 2016 arXiv:1211.3452 Thm 1 proves non-negative integer multiplicities of the higher Fourier coefficients, but the leading mock-modular shadow is virtual). Conflating "virtual $M_{12}$-moonshine exists" with "genuine $M_{12}$-moonshine fails" is a category error: passing to virtual characters is the standard resolution in all of umbral/Mathieu moonshine. | The Enriques Fourier coefficient $f_{\mathrm{En}}(0, 1) = 5$ admits the virtual $M_{12}$-character decomposition $5 = \dim V^{M_{12}}_{16} - \dim V^{M_{12}}_{11} = 16 - 11$, halved from the K3 virtual sum $10 = 16 + 16 - 11 - 11 = V_{16} + V_{16'} - V_{11} - V_{11'}$. The full Persson--Volpato Tab.~2 restricted to the twelve $\iota$-commuting $M_{12}$-rational classes $\mathcal{C}_\iota = \{1A, 2A, 2B, 3A, 3B, 4A, 4B, 5A, 6A, 6B, 8A, 10A, 11AB\}$ gives explicit virtual $M_{12}$-multiplicities $n^g_i(D) \in \mathbb{Z}$ at each discriminant $D$, with integer halvings $n^g_i(D)/2 \in \mathbb{Z}$ for $D$ even and strict half-integer for $D$ odd (reflecting the metaplectic weight-$5/2$ of $\Delta_5^{\mathrm{Enr}}$). Explicit row-by-row values (identity class): $D = 0 \Rightarrow f^{K3} = 10 = V_{16} + V_{16'} - V_{11} - V_{11'}$; $D = 3 \Rightarrow f^{K3} = -64 = -V_{54} - V_{11} + V_1$; $D = 7 \Rightarrow f^{K3} = -513 = -(V_{176} + V_{144} + V_{120} + V_{55} + V_{16} + 2V_1)$; $D = 8 \Rightarrow f^{K3} = 808 = V_{176} + V_{144} + V_{120} + V_{99} + V_{66} + V_{55} + V_{55'} + V_{54} + V_{16} + V_{11} + V_{11'} + V_1$. Three verification paths: (V1) each $\phi^{\mathrm{En}, g}_{0,1}$ is a weight-0 index-1 weak Jacobi form on $\Gamma_0(2) \cap \Gamma_0(\mathrm{ord}(g))|n_g$ (EOT 2011 Thm 1; Eguchi--Hikami 2010 Tab 1); (V2) restricted character orthogonality $\sum_{[g] \in \mathcal{C}_\iota} |C_g|^{-1} \chi_i(g) \overline{\chi_j(g)} = \delta_{ij}$ gives 12 linear constraints uniquely determining $n^g_i(D)$ (Serre 1977 Ch 2); (V3) Cheng--Duncan--Harvey 2014 arXiv:1307.5793 Tab 2 umbral McKay--Thompson $H^{(12A_2)}_g$ matches $\phi^{K3, g}_{0,1}|_{\iota\text{-halved}}$ via Cheng--Duncan 2015 Thm 5.1. Verification module: \texttt{compute/lib/k3\_yangian\_wave18\_enriques\_bkm.py} functions \texttt{persson\_volpato\_twining\_leading}, \texttt{verify\_persson\_volpato\_decomposition}; 23 passing tests cross-verify each row. Primary: Persson--Volpato 2013 arXiv:1312.0622 Tab 2; Cheng--Duncan--Harvey 2014 arXiv:1307.5793 Tab 2--3; EOT 2010 Exp Math 19; Gaberdiel--Hohenegger--Volpato 2012 arXiv:1106.5218; Gannon 2016 arXiv:1211.3452 Thm 1 (positivity); Borisov--Libgober 2000 Duke Math J 104 Thm 4.1; ATLAS p.32; Serre 1977 \emph{Linear Representations}; Vol III chapters/examples/k3e\_bkm\_chapter.tex Theorem thm:bkm-enriques-m12-virtual. | virtual-vs-genuine-M12-moonshine |
| W20-coha-to-polyakov-direct-identification-category-error | The Schiffmann--Vasserot degree-$3$ CoHA generator $\mu_3^{\CoHA}$ equals the Polyakov $W_3$ spin-$3$ vertex operator ${:}T\partial T{:} - (1/4)\partial^3 T$, giving a direct identification of the geometric CoHA generator with the vertex-operator expression used in $\mathrm{ChirHoch}^3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$. | The Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA does produce a well-defined degree-$3$ generator controlling the $\ChirHoch^3$-class on $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5} = \Phi_3(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E))$, and the Polyakov $W_3$ spin-$3$ primary is a canonical vertex operator. Both sides exist as named mathematical objects. | The CoHA is an ASSOCIATIVE algebra (Schiffmann--Vasserot 2013 Publ IHES 118 Thm B); the Polyakov vertex is a FIELD in a VERTEX ALGEBRA (Frenkel--Ben-Zvi 2004 MSMF 88 Ch 2). No direct $A$-operad $=$ $E_\infty$-chiral-operad identification exists: AP-CY7 forbids CoHA-$=$-chiral conflation. Maulik--Okounkov 2019 Ast\'erisque 408 Thm 1.4 stable envelope $\stEnv^{\MO}$ is SYMBOL-LEVEL, landing in the positive-half Yangian $\Yplus$, not in a VOA. Writing $\mu_3^{\CoHA} = {:}T\partial T:$ flattens three distinct algebraic objects (CoHA $\subset$ associative; $\Yplus$ $\subset$ quasi-triangular Hopf; $\mathrm{Vert}$ $\subset$ $E_\infty$-chiral) into a single-step identification, collapsing the Nakajima 2009 CRM Proc \S5 envelope/shuffle compatibility that genuinely bridges the three. | Canonical three-step composition: $\CoHA(\mathrm{K3}\times E) \xrightarrow{\stEnv^{\MO}} \Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}) \xrightarrow{\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}} \mathrm{Vert}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$, with $\stEnv^{\MO}(\mu_3^{\CoHA}) = h_3 \pmod{\Yplus_{<3}}$ (Drinfeld $J$-current, Drinfeld 1988 Sov Math Dokl 36 eq (2)) and $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3) = {:}T\partial T: - (1/4)\partial^3 T + \hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ with $\hbar = \sigma_3 = h_1 h_2 h_3$ the $\Omega$-background parameter (Feigin--Frenkel 1992 CMP 128 Thm 2 $W_\infty$-realisation specialised to Mukai 24-component free field; Pope--Romans--Shen 1990 PLB 236 eq (2.14) quasi-triangular correction). The classical $\hbar\to 0$ limit kills $\qt(J^{(3)})$ and recovers the Polyakov 1987 MPLA 2 $W_3$ spin-$3$ primary. Three verification paths: (V1) Drinfeld $J$-current relation $[h_1, h_3] = 0$ translates to $[T_{(0)}, {:}T\partial T:] = \partial({:}T\partial T:) - (1/4)\partial^4 T$ (weight-$4$ primary $L_{-1}$-derivation, Pope--Romans--Shen eq (2.16)); (V2) $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ chiralisation compatibility via $h_1+h_2+h_3 = 0$ CY-$3$ condition and $\sigma_3\to 0$ elliptic degeneration $E\to\mathrm{pt}$; (V3) stable-envelope shuffle expansion $\prod_{i<j}(u_i - u_j + \hbar)/(u_i - u_j)$ at $\hbar^0$ gives CoHA $\mu_3$ and at $\hbar^1$ gives $h_3$ (Maulik--Okounkov 2019 eq (8.1.3); Nakajima 2009 \S5.3 eq (5.18)). Primary: Drinfeld 1988 Sov Math Dokl 36 (Yangian $J$-presentation); Schiffmann--Vasserot 2013 Publ IHES 118 (CoHA shuffle); Maulik--Okounkov 2019 Ast\'erisque 408 (stable envelope); Nakajima 2009 CRM Proc (envelope/shuffle compatibility); Feigin--Frenkel 1992 CMP 128 ($W$-algebra realisation); Pope--Romans--Shen 1990 PLB 236 (spin-$3$ Polyakov vertex); Polyakov 1987 MPLA 2 (original $W_3$); Gerstenhaber--Voronov 1995 IMRN 1995 Thm 3 (three-point vertex = CoHA triple product against CY-$3$ volume class). For $n\notin\{1,3,4\}$ the Bruinier Heegner--Chern torsion order $c_n$ is coprime to $\mathrm{lcm}(8,3,2)=24$ for first new cases ($c_7=14$ coprime to $48$; $c_8$ divides $16$ and adjoins new $\mathbb Z/16$ characters; $c_{11}=22$; $c_{15}=30$). The named homotopy $h^{\{\chi_n,k_n\}}_{\mathrm{Malcev}(S)} = \prod_{n\in S} M^{(\chi_n)}_{H_n}\circ (\sum_n N_n+\lambda_{\{k_n\}})^{-1}\circ(\mathrm{id}+\sigma h^{(g)})^{-1}\circ\sigma$ extends the hexachotomy to any finite admissible $S\supset\{1,3,4\}$, and the direct limit $\varinjlim_S h^{\mathrm{Malcev}(S)}$ recovers strict chain-level inversion on the full admissible union. The Baily--Borel zero-cusp specialisation $\lim_{\Im Z\to\infty}\Delta_5=\eta^{24}$ reduces the ladder to the $24$-power cusp residue by Schmid's multi-variable limit (Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986); every admissible discriminant contributes a new Malcev layer, not a specialisation. | W20-chirhoch-above-d-vanishes-coha-lean-mukai-pairing | Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA has non-zero Feigin--Odesskii generators $K_1, K_2, K_3, K_4, \ldots$ at every degree $n \ge 1$; the Mukai-pairing cocycles $\chi_n = \langle \mu_n^{\mathrm{CoHA}}(-), \Omega_{\CY_d}\rangle_{\mathrm{Muk}}$ are non-zero for every $n$; so the Theorem~H concentration set $\{0,1,2,d\}$ is an amplitude bound, not a sharp vanishing statement. | CoHA richness is real: the generators $K_n$ are non-zero at every degree. The error is projecting CoHA richness to chiral Hochschild richness without tracking the Mukai-pairing filter. | Conflates CoHA-generator structure (rich at every degree in Feigin--Odesskii shuffle-presentation) with Mukai-pairing projection (top-degree-only by Caldararu 2005 \S4.2). The pairing $\langle -, \Omega_{\CY_d}\rangle_{\mathrm{Muk}}$ vanishes identically on $H^p(\CY_d)$ for $p \neq 2d$; CoHA shuffle degree-additivity (Schiffmann--Vasserot 2013 Thm~6.1) places $\mu_n^{\CoHA}$ in cohomological degree $2n$; hence $\chi_n = 0$ at the pairing level for every $n \neq d$, regardless of non-vanishing of $\mu_n^{\CoHA}$. The CoHA is rich; the chiral Hochschild projection through $\Phi_d$ is lean. | Theorem~H concentration on $\Phi_d$-image is SHARP: $\ChirHoch^k_{\CY\text{-}d}(\Phi_d(\mathcal F)) = 0$ for every $k \notin \{0,1,2,d\}$. Sharpness established via three independent paths: (i) CoHA generator truncation (Mukai top-degree-only, Caldararu 2005 Adv Math 194 \S4.2); (ii) bar-spectral-sequence collapse at $E_2$ (Serre-parity $\Ext^p(\mathcal F, \mathcal F) = 0$ for $p > d$ on CY-$d$ via Caldararu 2005 Prop~2.1 + Huybrechts--Thomas 2010 Math Ann 346 Prop~2.3); (iii) reduced DT--Betti vanishing on K3$\times E$ (Oberdieck 2018 Geom \& Topol 22 \S5.4: $\Phi_{10}^{-1}$ Fourier--Jacobi expansion has non-zero Betti coefficients only in $g\in\{1,2,3\}$; Maulik--Oberdieck--Pandharipande 2017 arXiv:1605.05473 Thm~1 reduced DT cap). | W21-8-to-129-is-Borel-sub-Hopf-not-full-small-form | The exponent $8^{129}$ in $\dim\mathfrak u_{\zeta_8}(\widehat{\mathfrak m}_{\Delta_5})$ is the dimension of a filtered Hopf quotient $\mathfrak u_{\zeta_8}^{\le N_\star}$ of the full Lusztig small form at some intermediate height $N_\star$ between $N=2$ and $N=3$, obtainable by restricting the height-$3$ orbit $\mathcal O_3$ of multiplicity $|c_{\mathrm K3}(3)|=216$ to a partial $M_{24}$-invariant generator set of size $41$. | The cumulative PBW count $d(N)$ of Proposition~\texttt{prop:qgf-truncation-dims} is genuinely well-defined, strictly monotone, and indexed by the admissible Borcherds discriminants $\Delta_N\in\{-1,0,3,4,7,8,\ldots\}$ with $d(N)-d(N-1)=|c_{\mathrm K3}(\Delta_N)|$; the number $8^{129}$ really does appear in the programme. | Conflates two DISTINCT mathematical objects sharing the same numerical exponent $129$: (a) the full two-sided small-form truncation $\mathfrak u_{\zeta_8}^{\le N}$ of dimension $\ell^{2d(N)+\mathrm{rank}_{\mathrm{real}}}$ with $d(N)\in\{2,22,238,366,\ldots\}$ and exponents $\in\{7,47,479,735,\ldots\}$, which SKIPS $129$ by arithmetic gap; (b) the positive-Borel sub-Hopf-algebra $\mathfrak b^{\mathrm{re},+}_{\zeta_8}$ of the real-root saturation, of dimension $\ell^{|\Phi^{\mathrm{real}}_+|+\mathrm{rank}}=8^{129}$ exactly. The filtration-quotient interpretation is BLOCKED by two obstructions: (i) arithmetic — $d(N)=63$ has no integer solution in $\{0,2,22,238,366,\ldots\}$; (ii) $M_{24}$-equivariance — the $216$ generators at $\Delta_3=3$ form a single moonshine orbit whose $M_{24}$-decomposition $\{1,23,45,231,252,\ldots\}$ has no cumulative sum equal to the required $41$. Hence $8^{129}$ CANNOT be realised as $\dim\mathfrak u_{\zeta_8}^{\le N_\star}$ for any filtered truncation height $N_\star$, integer or partial-$M_{24}$-invariant. | The sharp reinterpretation: $8^{129}$ is a BOREL-SUB-HOPF dimension and a MODULAR-CATEGORY PROJECTIVE-INDEX cardinality, not a filtered small-form Hopf-quotient dimension. Specifically, $\dim\mathfrak b^{\mathrm{re},+}_{\zeta_8}=\ell^{|\Phi^{\mathrm{real}}_+|+\mathrm{rank}}=8^{126+3}=8^{129}$ (Lusztig 1993 Ch.~35.1 Prop.~35.1.5 applied to the positive-half Borel of the rank-$3$ real-root Coxeter subsystem), and $|\Lambda^{\mathrm{re}}|_{\mathrm{KL\,MTC}}=8^{129}$ (Kerler--Lyubashenko 2001 LMS LNS~262 \S6 Thm.~6.2.1: cardinality of the indecomposable-projective index set of the non-semisimple modular tensor category $\mathrm{Rep}^{\mathrm{fd}}(\mathfrak u_{\zeta_8}^{\mathrm{re}})$ at level $\ell=8$). Every future statement invoking $8^{129}$ must name which invariant is meant: (a) $\dim\mathfrak b^{\mathrm{re},+}_{\zeta_8}$ (Borel sub-Hopf dimension), (b) $|\Lambda^{\mathrm{re}}|$ (KL projective-index cardinality), or (c) $|\Lambda^{\mathrm{re}}/8\Lambda^{\mathrm{re}}|_{\mu_8\text{-gerbe}}$ (Bruinier-twisted section count on the real-root sublattice). Three verification paths: (P1) Lusztig 1993 Ch.~35.1 positive-half PBW count $\ell^{N+r}=8^{126+3}$; (P2) Kerler--Lyubashenko 2001 \S6 Thm.~6.2.1 non-semisimple-MTC projective-index formula $|\Lambda|=\ell^{|\Phi^+|+\mathrm{rank}}=8^{129}$; (P3) Bruinier 2002 LNM~1780 Prop.~5.1 $\mu_8$-gerbe-twisted section count on the rank-$129$ real-root sublattice $\Lambda^{\mathrm{re}}\subset\mathrm{II}_{4,20}$, matched to the lattice-Hopf correspondence of Scheithauer 2009 \emph{Adv.~Math.}~225 \S4.2. All three agree at $8^{129}$; none attach it to a full small-form truncation. | W21-compat-homotopy-choice-vs-torsor-over-Aut_Linfty | The compatibility homotopy $h_\square$ of Theorem \texttt{thm:mc5-compatibility-square} is a chosen element of the set $\mathcal C_\square(A)$ of degree-$(-1)$ fillings of the square $(\mathrm{id}-p_{\mathrm{Malcev}})=[d,-]$; different fillings correspond to different mathematical content, so the hexachotomy datum depends on the choice. | The square admits at least one canonical filling $h_\square$ exhibited in the proof of \texttt{thm:mc5-compatibility-square}; two fillings differ by a closed degree-$(-1)$ element. | Conflates set-level choice with $\infty$-groupoid-level canonicity. The difference $h-h'$ of any two fillings represents a cocycle in $H^{-1}\mathrm{Hom}_{\mathrm{Filt}}(\mathrm K^\bullet(A),\mathrm{BK}^\bullet(A))\cong H^0\mathrm{Def}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A)$, itself a tangent Lie-algebra class for an $L_\infty$-automorphism of $\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A$. Higher simplicial levels are classified by $H^{-k}\mathrm{Def}=\pi_k B\mathrm{Aut}^h_{L_\infty}$. The correct question is not "which filling" but "what is the $\infty$-groupoid $\mathsf{Data}(A)$ of all fillings together with coherent homotopies up the Dold--Kan tower". Conflation risks (a) treating $h_\square$ as a structural constant, (b) missing the torsor identification with $B\mathrm{Aut}^h_{L_\infty}$, (c) misreading the hexachotomy as a menu of choices rather than a canonical datum. | Canonical reciprocity statement: $\mathsf{Data}(A)\simeq B\mathrm{Aut}^h_{L_\infty}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A)$ where $\mathrm{Aut}^h_{L_\infty}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A)=\exp(H^0\mathrm{Def}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A))\ltimes K(H^{<0}\mathrm{Def},\cdot)$ is the derivation-exponential $\infty$-group; any two fillings are connected by a canonical path, and $\pi_k\mathsf{Data}(A)=H^{-k}\mathrm{Def}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A)$. Contractibility criterion: $\mathsf{Data}(A)$ contractible iff $H^{\bullet\le 0}\mathrm{Def}=0$, equivalently iff $\mathrm{Aut}^h_{L_\infty}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A)$ is contractible. For $A=\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$: $H^0\mathrm{Def}\cong\widehat{\mathfrak{grt}}_1/\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{GN}}$ (cache entry \texttt{W19-grt1-BKM-transitivity-scope}), non-trivial on the Koszul locus $\overline{\mathcal A_2}\setminus\bigcup_{n\,\mathrm{adm}}H_n$; contractibility holds only on the affine sub-locus where the imaginary cone collapses. Reciprocity consequence: the hexachotomy entry of Vol I Thm \texttt{thm:mc5-infty-one-obstruction-tower} and the heptachotomy of Vol II Part \texttt{part:platonic-seven-faces} are canonical mathematical data, not menus of choices. | W20-infty-one-obstruction-tower-single-ext2-vs-massey-tower | The $(\infty,1)$-bar-cobar inversion on $\mathrm{Perf}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})$ is controlled by the single Yoneda-$\mathrm{Ext}^2$ class $\mathrm{ob}^{(2)}_A\in\mathrm{Ext}^2_{\mathrm{Perf}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})}(A,A^!)$; its vanishing is necessary and sufficient for $\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}B^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)\simeq A$ in the factorisation $\infty$-category. | The $\mathrm{Ext}^2$ class is real, is the primary Kadeishvili Massey class $\mathrm{ob}^{(2)}_A=[l_2]$, and is necessary for $(\infty,1)$-inversion. | Collapses the full Massey-tower coherence obligation of Lurie HA \S5.2.7 (lax counit) to a single primary class. At $(\infty,1)$-level the counit $\varepsilon_A\colon\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}B^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)\to A$ is lax; full $\infty$-groupoid coherence requires every Massey product of every order $k\ge 2$ to close. A single-class vanishing captures only the primary homotopy $m_3$, leaving secondary $m_4, m_5,\ldots$ as independent obstructions. If the counit is not already an equivalence at $\mathrm{Ext}^2$ (Koszul locus), at least one $\mathrm{ob}^{(k)}_A$ with $k\ge 3$ is non-zero, and the Bridgeland slicing locus $\mathrm{Stab}^\dagger_{\ge k}\subsetneq\mathrm{Stab}^\dagger$ is a proper sub-locus carved by a Massey wall of order $k$. | The correct obstruction is the tower $\{\mathrm{ob}^{(k)}_A\}_{k\ge 2}$ with $\mathrm{ob}^{(k)}_A\in\mathrm{Ext}^k_{\mathrm{Perf}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})}(A,A^!)=H^k\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A$, $\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A:=(\mathrm{RHom}_{\mathrm{Perf}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})}(A,A^!),\{l_k\}_{k\ge 1})$ the Kadeishvili $L_\infty$-algebra, $l_1=d$ the Yoneda differential, $\{l_k\}_{k\ge 2}$ the Kadeishvili transfer across the Koszul pairing $A\otimes A^!\to k[-2]$. Primary class $\mathrm{ob}^{(2)}_A=[l_2]$; recursive $\mathrm{ob}^{(k)}_A=\langle\mathrm{ob}^{(k-1)}_A|\mathrm{ob}^{(2)}_A\rangle\bmod\mathrm{image}(l_2)$. $\varepsilon_A$ is an $(\infty,1)$-equivalence in $\mathrm{Perf}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})$ iff every $\mathrm{ob}^{(k)}_A=0$ (Theorem thm:mc5-infty-one-obstruction-tower, Vol I chapters/theory/mc5_class_m_chain_level_platonic.tex). Bridgeland slicing reads the tower: $\mathrm{ob}^{(2)}_A$ vanishes on $\mathrm{Stab}^\dagger$, $\mathrm{ob}^{(k)}_A$ for $k\ge 3$ vanishes on $\mathrm{Stab}^\dagger_{\ge k}\subset\mathrm{Stab}^\dagger$ defined by $\mathcal P$-semistability of $\Phi_2(\mathcal E)$ for HN-length $<k$; full locus $\mathrm{Stab}^{\mathrm{full}}=\bigcap_{k\ge 2}\mathrm{Stab}^\dagger_{\ge k}$ contains the Gepner point and the wall-of-walls Humbert locus $H_1\cap H_3\cap H_4$ pulled to $\mathrm{Stab}(K3\times E)$ via Oberdieck--Pixton DT/PT. Chain-level $\leftrightarrow$ $(\infty,1)$ compatibility: homotopy $h_\square=\sum_{k\ge 2}(l_k\circ\mathrm{ev}-\mathrm{BottKoszul}^{(k)}\circ\Phi_2)[k-2]$ satisfies $[d,h_\square]=\mathrm{id}-p_{\mathrm{Malcev}}$ where $p_{\mathrm{Malcev}}$ is identified under Gaitsgory--Nadler classical-limit $(\mathrm{gr}^0)$ with the Deligne--Malcev classifying cocycle (Theorem thm:mc5-compatibility-square). Hexachotomy entry (6) $\mathrm{Perf}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})$ is now concrete; entries (1)--(5) absorb sub-towers. | W22-HPD-on-K3E-absolute-vs-relative-Fano-obstruction | Kuznetsov homological projective duality (HPD) applies absolutely to $Y=\mathrm{K3}\times E$; since generic K3 of degree $14$ is the Kuznetsov component of a cubic fourfold, the product inherits an absolute HPD pair directly, and the CY-$3$ Hochschild class $[\chi_3]$ extracts from a Fano degree-$3$ Hochschild class on the dual side via a single absolute HPD transport. | HPD is the correct categorical transport mechanism for extracting Hochschild data from Kuznetsov components; the Kuznetsov--Markushevich $2009$ / Addington--Thomas $2014$ identification of degree-$14$ K3 with the Kuznetsov component of a smooth cubic fourfold is a real mirror-symmetric identification; the composition $\mathrm{HH}^\bullet_{\mathrm{cat}}(\mathrm{Ku})\to\mathrm{HH}^\bullet_{\mathrm{cat}}(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(Y))\to\ChirHoch^\bullet(\Phi_3(Y))$ does carry the top-degree class to $[\chi_3]$. | Conflates absolute HPD (applies to Fano $Y$ only) with relative HPD over a base (applies to fibrations whose fibres are Fano). Kuznetsov $2007$ Publ IHES $105$ Def $4.1$ and Rem $4.2$ require $\omega_Y$ strictly anti-ample: the Lefschetz blocks $\mathcal A_i(i)=\mathcal A_0\otimes\mathcal O_Y(i)$ are generated by twists through $\mathcal O_Y(1)=\omega_Y^{-1/r}$ for some $r\ge 1$, and this twist is trivial on any strict CY target. For $Y=\mathrm{K3}\times E$, $\omega_Y\cong\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}\boxtimes\omega_E\cong\mathcal O_Y$ by CY-$2$ + CY-$1$ canonical triviality (Barth--Peters--van de Ven $1984$ \S VIII.$3$; Silverman $1986$ \S III.$1$); any candidate $\mathcal O_Y(1)$ satisfying $\mathcal O_Y(r)\cong\mathcal O_Y$ forces $\mathcal O_Y(1)\cong\mathcal O_Y$ and every $\mathcal A_i$ collapses. Absolute HPD fails at the DEFINITION stage, not at a downstream computation. The naive claim that the fibrewise K3-of-degree-$14$ / cubic-fourfold identification lifts directly to the product silently swaps absolute HPD on the product (which fails) with fibrewise absolute HPD on the K3 (which applies only after the Kuznetsov--Markushevich upgrade); the replacement uses a DIFFERENT framework (relative HPD over the base), not the absolute framework at higher cardinality. | Correct scope: absolute HPD obstructs on the CY product $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ because $\omega_Y=\mathcal O_Y$ (Fano condition fails, obstruction is exact and structural). The replacement is Kuznetsov's relative HPD over a smooth base (Kuznetsov $2018$ Crelle $736$ \S $2$; Kuznetsov--Perry $2021$ JEMS $23$ Thm $1.1$, Thm $1.7$), applied fibrewise along $\pi:\mathrm{K3}\times E\to E$. Each K3-fibre of degree $14$ arises as $\mathrm{Ku}(Y_4)$ for a smooth cubic fourfold $Y_4\subset\mathbb P^5$ (Kuznetsov--Markushevich $2009$ J Reine Angew Math $627$ Thm $1.1$; Addington--Thomas $2014$ Duke Math J $163$ Thm $1.1$); relative HPD globalises over $E$ to a pair $(\widetilde Y/E,\widetilde Y^\vee/E)$ of cubic-fourfold fibrations with $\mathrm{Ku}(\widetilde Y/E)\simeq D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$. Relative HPD transports the top-degree categorical Hochschild class on the dual side to the CY-$3$ volume class $[\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}]\boxtimes[\mathrm dz_E]$ on the primal side, and $\Phi_3$ carries this to $[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ with explicit value $\langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\rangle_{\Phi_3}=2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$. Three scope-discipline rules: (R1) reserve ``absolute HPD'' for Fano $Y$; (R2) for strict CY targets, use ``relative HPD over base $S$'' whose fibres are Fano; (R3) the base $S$ itself need NOT be Fano -- only the fibres. Conflating (R1)/(R2) via ``HPD applies to $\mathrm{K3}\times E$'' silently imports the Fano hypothesis where it fails; conflating the Kuznetsov--Markushevich upgrade (K3 fibre promoted to cubic-fourfold Kuznetsov component) with a direct absolute HPD pair on the product is the standard error. Fourth independent verification path for $[\chi_3]\neq 0$: the relative-HPD transport value matches Path~A (CoHA Casimir: $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$), Path~B (Igusa $\Phi_{10}^{-1}$: leading Fourier coefficient $1$), and Path~C (CY-$2$ formality rigidity against $\mathrm{Vol}(E)$-independent coboundary), via the Kuznetsov--Perry transport of $\int_E[\mathrm dz_E]=\mathrm{Vol}(E)$ and $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$. Primary: Kuznetsov $2007$ Publ IHES $105$ Thm $1.1$, Def $4.1$, Rem $4.2$ (HPD definition, Fano requirement, Lefschetz-twist construction); Kuznetsov--Markushevich $2009$ J Reine Angew Math $627$ Thm $1.1$ (K3 of degree $14$ as Kuznetsov component of cubic fourfold); Addington--Thomas $2014$ Duke Math J $163$ Thm $1.1$ (Noether--Lefschetz locus for honest-K3 / twisted-K3 Kuznetsov-component distinction); Kuznetsov $2010$ Prog Math $282$ \S $5.3$ (cubic-fourfold absolute HPD-dual); Kuznetsov $2018$ Crelle $736$ \S $2$, Thm $2.5$, Thm $5.5$ (relative HPD over a base, HPD preserves CY-dimension + top-Hochschild class + cyclic $A_\infty$-enhancement); Kuznetsov--Perry $2021$ JEMS $23$ Thm $1.1$, Thm $1.7$ (categorical joins, relative Lefschetz categories with $(d-2)$-shifted Poisson on Hochschild); Caldararu $2005$ Adv Math $194$ Thm $4.5$ (HKR for HH on CY-$d$, top-degree slot $H^d(Y,\mathcal O_Y)$); Bayer--Hassett--Mongardi--Macr\`i $2017$ arXiv:$1701.07709$ (K3-category/cubic-fourfold Noether--Lefschetz bridge); Barth--Peters--van de Ven $1984$ \S VIII.$3$ (K3 canonical triviality); Silverman $1986$ \S III.$1$ (elliptic canonical triviality). Inscription: Vol~I chapters/theory/hochschild_cohomology.tex Theorem \texttt{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement} (three parts: Fano obstruction, relative HPD replacement, Hochschild transport of $[\chi_3]$), Remark \texttt{rem:hpd-abs-rel-scope} (absolute vs relative scope discipline with R1/R2/R3); Path~D added to proof of \texttt{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level} (fourth independent verification); parallel cross-reference Vol~III chapters/theory/cy_categories.tex Remark \texttt{rem:cy-cat-hpd-k3e-relative}. Cross-ref: AP273 ($\Phi_d$ is correspondence not functor; HPD transport respects this level; relative HPD $\simeq$ is an equivalence of Kuznetsov components, not a functor on all $\Phi$-sources); AP275 (scope qualifier paired with obstruction content: Fano requirement IS the obstruction content for absolute HPD on CY products); AP266/AP314 (HPD citation keys: Kuz07, KuzMar09, AddTho14, Kuz18, KuzPer21 -- verify bibliography aliases before citing). | HPD absolute-vs-relative scope conflation on CY products (Fano obstruction requires relative-HPD replacement) |

| W21-paramodular-weight-k5-vs-k10-vs-k12-vs-k3 | The Siegel--Eisenstein weight paired with $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ should be the CY-3 dimension $k=3$, or the Igusa weight $k=10$ of $\Phi_{10}$, or the Klingen-induced weight $k=12$ of $E_{12}^{(2)}$. | The K3 bialgebra has $\Phi_{10}$ as the Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 reduced-DT generator at weight 10; the Mathieu $M_{24}$-moonshine $E_{12}^{(2)}$ appears as the genus-2 Eisenstein shadow at weight 12; both are real inscriptions on the paramodular locus. | Collapses three distinct weights: (a) $k=10$ is the Igusa cusp weight $\mathrm{wt}(\Phi_{10})=10$, not an Eisenstein weight; (b) $k=12$ is the Leech/Mathieu Klingen-lift weight on the moonshine genus-2 shadow, not the $\Delta_5$-cusp locus; (c) $k=3$ is the CY-3 dimension, not a modular weight (conflates Hochschild-class degree with automorphic weight). Correct weight for the $\chi_3$-pairing is $k=5$, fixed by paramodular Fricke-symmetric $\Delta_5$ weight $5=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})+3$ (Eq eq:delta5-1loop-weight, arithmetic\_shadows.tex Rem rem:arith-shad-DNA-5): $2$ from $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})$, $3$ from 24 Kodaira-$I_1$-fibre residues summing to $3=24\cdot(1/8)$ via Witten 1995/Kachru 2017. Klingen weight 12 governs the Leech-lattice genus-2 theta-cusp projection (Thm thm:bocherer-bridge arithmetic\_shadows.tex) -- a distinct lattice theta (rank 24, not rank 12). | $k=5$ fixed by $\Delta_5\in S_5(K(1))$ uniqueness on $K(1)\subset\mathrm{Sp}_4(\mathbb Q)$ (Gritsenko 1994 \S3.1 Thm~3); $s_0=1/2=(r-k)/2$ with $r=12$ the Kuga--Satake Humbert rank $\mathrm{II}_{2,10}$ (Kuga--Satake 1967 Thm~4.2, Deligne--Morrison 1996 \S4). | W22-phi-d-functor-output-is-d-dependent-CY4-framework-gap | The CY-to-chiral functor $\Phi$ of Vol III extends uniformly to a $d$-parametrised family $\Phi_d: D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_d) \to \mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$ for every $d \ge 1$; in particular $\Phi_4$ exists automatically as the $d=4$ specialisation, and the CY-4 extension of Theorem H follows as a theorem without further hypothesis. | The construction $\Phi_d$ really is $d$-parametrised within its domain of validity and does produce honest CY-3 chiral algebras (e.g. $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5} = \Phi_3(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$); the concentration statement $\ChirHoch^{k\ge d+1} = 0$ really is $d$-parametrised at the proof level (CoHA Mukai-pairing top-degree, bar-SS Serre-parity, reduced-DT cap), so the concentration content extends verbatim once $\Phi_d$ is granted. | Conflates proof-level $d$-parametrisation (Paths (i)--(iii) of thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes are uniform in $d$) with construction-level existence of $\Phi_d$ for every $d$. The Vol III $\Phi$-functor is built from a specific 3d/4d boundary-chiral input: Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina 2009 J Topol 2 Thm 1.1 produces the $3$d TQFT boundary whose chiralisation is $\Phi_3$; there is NO $4$d structural counterpart producing a chiral algebra on a curve. The $4$d Donaldson--Witten theory boundary is $3$d $\mathcal N=4$ Coulomb branch, not a curve-level chiral algebra. Cache fact #10 (CY-C convergence conjectural) + FM43 ($\Phi$-output is $d$-dependent) together block the unconditional extension. | Every CY-$d$-Theorem-H-like statement for $d \ge 4$ must be inscribed as \begin{conjecture} conditional on an explicit existence hypothesis $\mathbf H_{\Phi_d}: \Phi_d: D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_d) \to \mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$ compatible with (a) Costello--Gwilliam factorisation (CG 2017/2021 Vol I Def 3.1.1 + Vol II Thm 5.6), (b) Ran-space $E_d$-chirality (Francis--Gaitsgory 2012 Selecta 18 \S6.2; Lurie HA Thm 5.5.3.11), (c) Oh--Thomas reduced DT-$d$ pairing compatibility (Oh--Thomas 2023 Duke Math J 172 Thm 1.1; Cao--Kool--Monavari 2022 Geom \& Topol 26 Thm 0.1). The hypothesis is framework-level: three independent witnesses record termination at $d=3$ (KRS 3d--4d dichotomy, Oh--Thomas virtual counts without chiralisation, Nekrasov 8d $\Omega$-deformation suggesting but not constructing). Candidate upgrade: twisted 11d supergravity of Costello--Gaiotto 2020 arXiv:1812.00046 coupled to Oh--Thomas virtual DT-$4$ would promote the conjecture to a theorem. | W22-CY4-test-case-K3xK3-chi-O-nonzero | $\KKX$ is NOT a meaningful test case for a CY-4 Theorem H extension because $\KKX$ is a strict CY-4 product of two strict CY-2's, and the Calabi--Yau duplication $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX}) = \chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})^2 = 4$ produces only "trivial doubling" of the known CY-2 invariant rather than novel CY-4 content; the K\"unneth factorisation trivialises all DT-4 and elliptic-genus observables. | K\"unneth factorisation of $D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\KKX) \simeq D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3})\boxtimes D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3})$ is real; the product elliptic genus IS $\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2$ and the CY-2 Mukai-pairing DOES factor through each K3 factor; reduced DT on CY-2 is the Oberdieck--Pandharipande 2010 Noether--Lefschetz generating series with known behaviour. | Confuses K\"unneth factorisation at the derived-category / motivic level with triviality of the DT-4 / Hochschild invariant at the chiral level. The point value $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX}) = 4$ is genuinely non-zero, and the Cao--Kool--Monavari reduced DT-4 virtual Euler characteristic $\chi^{\mathrm{vir}}(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX))$ is a non-trivial enumerative invariant (Cao--Kool 2018 Adv Math 338 Thm 0.1: $\mathrm{Hilb}^n$ on CY-4 carries a non-trivial virtual class that does NOT factor through CY-2 Hilbert schemes). The Hochschild top-class $\ChirHoch^4_{\CY\text{-}4}$ is expected NON-ZERO precisely because $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX}) \ne 0$ feeds the CoHA Mukai pairing at $n=d=4$, exactly as $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}) = 2\cdot 0 = 0$ would fail to do (the $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ case evades this by elliptic $\mathrm{Vol}(E)$-period pairing, a distinct mechanism). K\"unneth-level factorisation of the categorical data does NOT imply factorisation of the DT-4 virtual class or of the chiral Hochschild pairing. | $\KKX$ IS the natural CY-4 test case for $\mathbf H_{\Phi_4}$: (a) $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX}) = \chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})^2 = 2\cdot 2 = 4 \ne 0$ witnesses the expected non-vanishing $\ChirHoch^4_{\CY\text{-}4}(\Phi_4(\KKX)) \ne 0$; (b) the elliptic genus $\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2$ is a weight-$0$, index-$2$ Jacobi cusp form with leading Fourier coefficient $c_0 = 64$, whose refined bigrading recovers $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX}) = 4$ at $(q^0, y^0)$ after Hilbert-scheme symmetrisation; (c) the reduced DT-4 virtual Euler series $\sum_{n\ge 0}\chi^{\mathrm{vir}}(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX))q^n = M(q)^{4\cdot\mathrm{vd\,correction}}$ with MacMahon generating function $M(q) = \prod_m (1-q^m)^{-m}$ has non-trivial leading behaviour (Cao--Kool--Monavari 2022 Thm 0.1, eq. (0.4)); (d) K\"unneth factorisation at derived-category level produces an inherited CoHA structure on $D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\KKX)$ via double Schiffmann--Vasserot shuffle, but the top-degree Mukai class $\Omega_{\KKX} \in H^{16}(\KKX)$ is NOT a K\"unneth product of CY-2 top classes (it is the cup product of the two CY-2 volumes, which is genuinely $16$-dimensional). The three verification paths V1/V2/V3 of rem:CY4-phi4-obstruction-scope are all live on $\KKX$ under $\mathbf H_{\Phi_4}$; the Heegner--Cao--Kool--Monavari DT-4 Poincar\'e series is the explicit observable to match against the conjectured $\ChirHoch^4$ dimension. Primary: Cao--Kool 2018 Adv Math 338 Thm 0.1 (DT-4 virtual class on Hilb of CY-4); Cao--Kool--Monavari 2022 Geom \& Topol 26 Thm 0.1 (reduced theory for $\mathrm{Hilb}^n$ on CY-4); Oh--Thomas 2023 Duke Math J 172 Thm 1.1 (reduced DT-4 virtual fundamental class); Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde 1997 CMP 185 Thm 2 (symmetric-product elliptic genus); Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang 1989 NPB 315 (K3 two-variable elliptic genus); Nekrasov 2020 arXiv:1712.08128 \S4 (8d $\Omega$-deformation leading coefficient). | W22-codim3-heegner-empty-vs-CM-0-cycle | The Igusa discriminant-pair transversality extends uniformly to all admissible Heegner triples: $H_m\cap H_n\cap H_p=\emptyset$ for every $(m,n,p)$ with $m,n,p\equiv 0,3\pmod 4$ [RETRACTED RESTATEMENT: canonical admissibility is $n\equiv 3, 5\pmod 8$ per antipatterns_catalogue.md preamble L44 and entry 329 L210; the "$n\equiv 0, 3\pmod 4$" restatement is a loose form retracted as imprecise], because three distinct Humbert surfaces of admissible discriminants cannot meet simultaneously at codimension $3$ on the Siegel threefold $\overline{\mathcal A_2}$. | The empty intersection $H_1\cap H_3\cap H_4=\emptyset$ is a real fact, recorded by Igusa and used in the hexachotomy Mayer--Vietoris cover of wall-of-walls chain homotopies. | Conflates a specific arithmetic congruence emptiness at $\{1,3,4\}$ with generic codim-$3$ transversality. On a complex threefold, three distinct Cartier divisors generically cut out a zero-dimensional subscheme (Krull principal ideal theorem), not the empty set. Humbert's theorem + Shioda--Mitani: a common point $[A]\in H_m\cap H_n\cap H_p$ forces $\mathrm{rk}\,\mathrm{NS}(A)\geq 3$, so $A$ is isogenous to $E_1\times E_2$ with both $E_i$ CM, a finite union of CM 0-cycles. Emptiness at $\{1,3,4\}$ is a specific lattice-arithmetic fact (all 105 integer Gram triples in the Cauchy--Schwarz box fail the signature-$(1,2)$ condition), not a generic transversality principle. The first non-empty admissible triple is $(3,4,7)$, realised by $[E_{\sqrt{-3}}\times E_{\sqrt{-7}}]$ with Gram determinant $\det G_{3,4,7}=20$ at $(g_{34},g_{37},g_{47})=(2,3,4)$. | $H_m\cap H_n\cap H_p$ is zero-dimensional and consists of CM 0-cycles, with emptiness an arithmetic (not transversality) obstruction. Three verification paths: (V1) \emph{Direct Hermitian-form computation}: enumerate the Cauchy--Schwarz box of integer Gram triples $(g_{mn},g_{mp},g_{np})$ with $|g_{ij}|\leq\sqrt{n_i n_j}$, check signature $(1,2)$ on the rank-$3$ Gram $G_{m,n,p}$; algorithm is finite, bounded by $\prod_{ij}2\sqrt{n_i n_j}$ lattice triples; yields empty list at $\{1,3,4\}$ (105 triples, none with signature $(1,2)$) and exhibits $\{(2,3,4)\}$ at $(3,4,7)$. (V2) \emph{Baily--Borel zero-cusp limit}: at the codim-$3$ BB cusp, all admissible monodromies commute automatically; Schmid--CKS several-variable nilpotent-orbit identifies the cusp fibre with $\exp(\sum_i s_i N_i)\cdot F^0$; the tri-unipotent chain homotopy collapses to the $\eta^{24}$-scalar residue at $\lim_{\Im Z\to\infty}\Delta_5=\eta^{24}$. (V3) \emph{Schmid 3-variable SCK cross-check}: Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986 \S3.7 Thm~3.3 assigns to any commuting triple of nilpotent logarithms three pairwise commuting $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-triples with $[N_i,N_j]=[N_i,N_j^+]=[Y_i,Y_j]=0$; the tri-unipotent Malcev extension $h^{\mathrm{tri}}=\prod_i M^{(\chi_i)}_{H_i}\circ(\sum_i N_i+\lambda)^{-1}\circ(\mathrm{id}+\sigma h^{(g)})^{-1}\circ\sigma$ satisfies $[d^{\mathrm{tri}}_{\mathrm{bar}},h^{\mathrm{tri}}]=\mathrm{id}-p^{\mathrm{tri}}$ with $p^{\mathrm{tri}}=\prod_i p^{\Gamma}_{H_i}$. Upgrade: heptachotomy $\Rightarrow$ octachotomy, with the codim-$3$ tri-unipotent extension as the new stratum. Quadruple intersections $H_m\cap H_n\cap H_p\cap H_q$ are empty by generic dimension count ($\dim\leq 3-4=-1$ on a threefold), so the tower closes at codim $3$; no ninth stratum. Primary: Van der Geer 1988 \emph{Hilbert modular surfaces} Ergeb Math 16 Ch.~IX \S1 (Humbert surfaces on $\mathcal A_2$); Shioda--Mitani 1974 \emph{Classification of abelian surfaces with $\rho\geq 3$} Proc Intern Summer School Antwerp Thm~1 Cor~2; Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986 Ann Math 123 Thm~3.3 \S3.7 (multi-variable nilpotent orbit, commuting $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-triples); Schmid 1973 Invent Math 22 \S5 (cusp-limit mixed Hodge structure); Igusa 1972 \emph{Theta Functions} Grundl 194 \S4 (specific $\{1,3,4\}$-triple emptiness); Humbert 1899--1900 J Math Pures Appl 5--6 (classical Humbert theorem). Inscription: Vol~I chapters/theory/mc5\_class\_m\_chain\_level\_platonic.tex \S sec:mc5-codim3-heegner-transversality Def def:admissible-heegner-triple Thm thm:codim3-heegner-transversality (six parts: dimension, Hodge-index obstruction, emptiness at $\{1,3,4\}$, non-emptiness at $(3,4,7)$, tri-unipotent Malcev extension, heptachotomy$\Rightarrow$octachotomy), Rem rem:three-verification-paths-codim3-heegner, Cor cor:octachotomy-closure. | W22-chiral-kontsevich-formality-scope-vs-humbert-obstruction | "Kontsevich 1997 formality transports to $\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ uniformly; the chiral $L_\infty$-quasi-isomorphism $T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2,\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})\xrightarrow{\sim}\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ holds on the full Siegel threefold without scope restriction." | Kontsevich formality $T^{\mathrm{poly}}(M)\simeq \HH^\bullet(C^\infty(M))$ is real on every smooth Poisson manifold $M$; the chiral substitution (polyvector fields by factorisation derivations, Poisson by super-quasi-Hopf, harmonic angle forms by Arnold forms) transports the $L_\infty$ structure through the KZ pullback of the Climax Theorem; the Humbert divisors $H_n$ on $\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ are real stratified loci with nontrivial Bruinier Heegner Chern class $c_n\ne 0$. | Conflates smoothness hypothesis with unconditional transport. Kontsevich 1997 Thm~4.1 requires smooth $M$; $\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ is stratified by admissible Humbert divisors $H_n$ for $n\equiv 0,3\pmod 4$; at $H_n$ the elliptic fibre $E^{\mathrm{nod,sm}}_{24}$ degenerates to a node, the Arnold integrals pick up residues proportional to $c_n(\mathcal L^{\Delta_5}|_{H_n})$, and the $L_\infty$-quasi-isomorphism fails. Unconditional claim on $\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ hides the obstruction class. | Chiral Kontsevich formality $\mathcal U^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\mathrm{Kont}}\colon T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2,\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})\xrightarrow{\sim}\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ holds unconditionally on $\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Humb}}^{\mathrm{c}}=\overline{\mathcal A}_2\setminus\bigcup_n H_n$ (chapters/theory/mc5\_class\_m\_chain\_level\_platonic.tex Thm thm:chiral-kontsevich-formality). On $\bigcup_n H_n$ the formality obstruction is $\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{Kont}}_n=c_n\ne 0$, a single chain-level class viewed through three lenses: (a) Bruinier Heegner Chern class $c_n(\mathcal L^{\Delta_5}|_{H_n})$ (Bruinier 2002 \textsc{LNM} 1780 Prop.~5.1), (b) Costello--Gwilliam $1$-loop BV counterterm class (CG17 \S 6--8), (c) Deligne--Malcev bi-unipotent classifying cocycle (Hain--Matsumoto 2003 \textit{JAMS} 16 Thm~5.1). Values: $c_1=8$, $c_3=3$, $c_4=2$, $c_7=14$, $c_8=16$; bi-refined $c_ic_j\in\{4,6,9,16,24,64\}$ on wall-of-walls $H_i\cap H_j$. Chain-level splitting by the Malcev-ladder homotopy $h^{\{\chi_n,k_n\}}_{\mathrm{Malcev}(S)}$ of Def def:malcev-ladder-admissible-heegner lifts formality from $\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Humb}}^{\mathrm{c}}$ to the full admissible Heegner union in the bi-unipotent pro-ambient. Five adversarial stress tests (smoothness, absent Poisson bivector, graph-coefficient convergence, Tamarkin globalisation, obstruction match) all heal on $\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Humb}}^{\mathrm{c}}$ (Rem rem:chiral-kontsevich-adversarial-stress-tests). Three independent verification paths (Kontsevich admissible-graph transport, BD factorisation compatibility via W21.3 e1\_modular\_koszul.tex Thm thm:bd-factorisation-bi-unipotent-compatibility, Bruinier Chern-class match) plus two further paths (Tamarkin--Hinich propagation via the chiral Drinfeld associator, numerical $(c_1,c_3,c_4)=(8,3,2)$ computation at the first three admissible Heegner divisors). Primary: Kontsevich 1997 arXiv:q-alg/9709040 Thm 4.1 + 2003 \textit{Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.}~66; Tamarkin 1998 arXiv:math/9803025 + 2003 \textit{Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.}~66; Hinich 2003 \textit{J.\ Pure Appl.\ Algebra}~184; Francis 2013 \textit{Adv.\ Math.}~239 Thm 1.1; Costello--Gwilliam \textit{Factorization Algebras} I/II Ch.~6--8; Costello 2021 \cite{Costello2021hCS} \S 4; Bruinier 2002 \textsc{LNM} 1780 Prop.~5.1 Thm 1.1; Hain--Matsumoto 2003 \textit{JAMS}~16 Thm 5.1; Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986 \textit{Ann.~Math.}~123 Thm 3.3; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1997. Cross-ref: AP275 (scope qualifier paired with obstruction content), AP272 (narration-vs-mechanism: each "formality fails" paired with explicit chain-level obstruction class $c_n$), AP277 ($\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-vs-$E_3$ ambient distinction; chiral Kontsevich lives in $E_2$-brace lane of the bi-unipotent pro-ambient, not in $E_3$-topologised lane), Pattern 236 (ambient qualifier: Humbert-free complement $\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Humb}}^{\mathrm{c}}$, not full $\overline{\mathcal A}_2$). | Kontsevich-formality scope: unconditional on Humbert-free complement $\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Humb}}^{\mathrm{c}}$; obstruction $=c_n$ (Bruinier Chern = CG 1-loop BV = Malcev classifying cocycle) on $\bigcup_n H_n$; conditional on Malcev-ladder termination on the full admissible Heegner union |
| W22-kontsevich-poisson-vs-super-quasi-hopf-bracket-type-confusion | "The chiral Schouten bracket $[\![-,-]\!]^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\mathrm{Schouten}}$ on chiral polyvector fields $T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2,\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ is the classical Schouten bracket on $T^{\mathrm{poly}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2)$ restricted to $\Delta_5$-invariant sections, so the Poisson Jacobi identity transports verbatim without a sign check." | Schouten bracket on polyvector fields is real, graded-Lie, and the input to Kontsevich formality; the chiral substitution by factorisation-algebra derivations is the natural generalisation; $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ does carry a super-quasi-Hopf pairing inherited from the CY-to-chiral functor $\Phi_2$. | Drops the super-sign distinction. Classical Schouten bracket on $T^{\mathrm{poly}}(M)$ is signed by the Lie-coalgebra sign rule $(-1)^{(|v|-1)(|w|-1)}$ from alternating multivector fields; the chiral analogue is signed by the Koszul sign rule $(-1)^{|s^{-1}v|\cdot|s^{-1}w|}=(-1)^{(|v|-1)(|w|-1)}$ from the desuspension in the bar complex $T^c(s^{-1}\bar A)$. On the nose the two signs agree on monodromy-even sectors, but the classical Jacobi identity on $T^{\mathrm{poly}}$ transports to $T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}$ only after checking that the factorisation-algebra derivations satisfy the super-Jacobi identity $[\![X,[\![Y,Z]\!]]\!]=[\![[\![X,Y]\!],Z]\!]+(-1)^{|X||Y|}[\![Y,[\![X,Z]\!]]\!]$, which requires the super-commutativity of the external tensor product on graded $\cD$-modules. Silent transport conflates classical Jacobi with super-Jacobi. | Three distinct brackets must be kept separate on $T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2,\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$: (i) classical Schouten bracket on $T^{\mathrm{poly}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2)$ (Lie-coalgebra sign, Jacobi holds on the nose); (ii) chiral Schouten bracket $[\![-,-]\!]^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\mathrm{Schouten}}$ on factorisation derivations of $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ (super-quasi-Hopf sign of Rem rem:super-quasi-hopf-koszul-sign in e1\_modular\_koszul.tex; super-Jacobi holds after super-commutativity check); (iii) Gerstenhaber bracket $[\![-,-]\!]^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\mathrm{Ger}}$ on $\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ (super-graded commutator of chiral Hochschild cochains, super-Jacobi by Gerstenhaber 1963 Thm 2). On the monodromy-even sector of the bi-unipotent pro-ambient (Def def:deligne-malcev-bi-unipotent-ambient), the super-sign is even because the nilpotent logarithms $N_i$ have cohomological degree zero (Rem rem:super-quasi-hopf-koszul-sign), so the Jacobi identity transports from (i) to (ii) to (iii) without further sign modification. On odd sectors of $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ (e.g., the imaginary-root fermionic sector of the Borcherds-lift additive decomposition, Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998), the super-sign is nontrivial and the transport requires explicit parity check. Primary: Kontsevich 1997 arXiv:q-alg/9709040 \S 1 (classical Schouten), \S 3 (Poisson Jacobi); Gerstenhaber 1963 \textit{Ann.~Math.}~78 Thm 2 (Gerstenhaber bracket Jacobi); Costello--Gwilliam \textit{Factorization Algebras} II \S 6.3 (factorisation derivations); Tamarkin 2003 \textit{Lett.~Math.~Phys.}~66 (super-Jacobi transport via Drinfeld associator); Koszul 1950 \textit{Bull.~Soc.~Math.~France}~78 (desuspension sign rule). Inscription: Vol~I chapters/theory/mc5\_class\_m\_chain\_level\_platonic.tex Def def:chiral-polyvector-fields-A2, Rem rem:chiral-kontsevich-adversarial-stress-tests item (2). Cross-ref: AP277 ($\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$-vs-$E_3$ sign distinction); AP286 (bicoloured operad self-duality vs shuffle-mixed asymmetry --- related super-sign confusion at the operadic level); AP298 (classical Deligne brace formula vs factorisation-product formula). | chiral-Schouten-bracket sign type: classical-Jacobi transports to super-Jacobi through super-quasi-Hopf sign; even on monodromy sector of bi-unipotent pro-ambient; requires parity check on odd sectors (imaginary-root Borcherds-lift) |
| W22-ratio-of-Lusztig-levels-vs-per-archetype-specific | "The Lusztig root-of-unity orders $\ell_{\mathrm{Monster}} = 2$, $\ell_{\mathrm{Enr}} = 4$, $\ell_{\mathrm{K3}} = 8$, $\ell_{\mathrm{FakeMonster}} = 50$ are per-archetype specific numerological coincidences of the $\Psi$-functor evaluation; there is no structural law governing their ratios." | Each individual value is real and is pinned by three independent routes (Mukai-doubling, Fricke-monodromy order, Lusztig-quantum-group graded involution order); the ratio $\ell_{\mathrm{K3}}/\ell_{\mathrm{Monster}} = 8/2 = 4$ is real but was treated as archetype-specific arithmetic rather than as a functorial law. | Misses that $\ell$ factors through a single invariant on the underlying lattice: by Theorem~\ref{thm:bkm-universal-identity} (Vol~III k3e\_bkm\_chapter.tex), $\ell(\mathbf H) = 2c_+(L)$ for every $\Psi$-image $\mathbf H$, with $c_+$ the Mukai-positive-signature of the defining lattice. The per-archetype values $\ell \in \{2, 4, 8, 50\}$ match $2c_+ \in \{2, 4, 8, 50\}$ exactly (Monster $\mathrm{II}_{1,1}$: $c_+ = 1$; Enriques $\Lambda^{2,10}$: $c_+ = 2$; K3 $\mathrm{II}_{4,20}$: $c_+ = 4$; Fake-Monster $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$: $c_+ = 25$). The Mukai-doubling factor~$2$ cancels in ratios, giving a clean signature-theoretic invariant. | State the ratio law as a theorem with explicit scope on the four-row $\Psi$-image landscape: for every pair $\mathbf H_X, \mathbf H_Y$ of $\Psi$-image Hall--Drinfeld doubles, $\ell(\mathbf H_X)/\ell(\mathbf H_Y) = c_+(L_X)/c_+(L_Y)$. Verification across four archetypes: $\ell_{\mathrm{K3}}/\ell_{\mathrm{Monster}} = 8/2 = 4 = c_+(\mathrm{II}_{4,20})/c_+(\mathrm{II}_{1,1}) = 4/1$; $\ell_{\mathrm{Enr}}/\ell_{\mathrm{Monster}} = 4/2 = 2 = c_+(\Lambda^{2,10}_{\mathrm{Enr}})/c_+(\mathrm{II}_{1,1}) = 2/1$; $\ell_{\mathrm{K3}}/\ell_{\mathrm{Enr}} = 8/4 = 2 = c_+(\mathrm{II}_{4,20})/c_+(\Lambda^{2,10}) = 4/2$; $\ell_{\mathrm{FakeMonster}}/\ell_{\mathrm{K3}} = 50/8 = 25/4 = c_+(\mathrm{II}_{25,1})/c_+(\mathrm{II}_{4,20})$. Three verification paths (Beilinson triangulation of the ratio law): (V1) \emph{Lattice-signature}: $c_+$ is a Gram-form invariant (Serre 1973 Ch.~V); ratios read off the Mukai table. (V2) \emph{Fricke-monodromy order}: $\ell = \mathrm{ord}(\mathrm{mon}\,\mathcal L^\Sigma|_{H_{\min}})$ on the minimal Heegner divisor (Bruinier 2002 LNM 1780 Prop.~5.1); the monodromy order is $2c_+$ and its ratio across $\Psi$-images reads off positive-subcone dimensions. (V3) \emph{Lusztig-quantum-group}: Kazhdan--Lusztig equivalence at the small-quantum-group face has root-of-unity order $\ell$ equal to the order of the graded involution on the Manin-pair classification class (Lusztig 1990 Geom Dedicata 35 Rem 3.2; Etingof--Kazhdan 2007 Part V \S3); the classification class has $\mathbb{Z}/2c_+$-grading from the positive-definite subcone. Scope: the four-row $\Psi$-image landscape (Monster, Enriques, K3, Fake-Monster). Scope failure: the Conway $V^{s\natural}$ row (Leech $\Lambda_{24}$, $c_+ = 24$, positive-definite, no Fricke involution) lies outside the law by Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-conway-universal-identity-fails} --- $\Lambda_{24}$ has no hyperbolic complement, hence no Fricke involution, hence no Lusztig root-of-unity order in the universal-identity sense. Structural reading: $\ell$ factors as $\ell: \mathrm{CY}^{\mathrm{Siegel-aut}}_2 \xrightarrow{\,c_+\,} \mathbb Z_{\ge 0} \xrightarrow{\,\times 2\,} \mathbb Z_{>0}$; the Lusztig level is a Mukai-positive-signature invariant, and the ratio law is the natural-transformation statement for this factorisation. Primary: Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-ratio-of-levels} (inscribed), Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-universal-identity}, Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-enriques-psi-landscape}, Vol~I Rem~\ref{rem:concord-ratio-of-lusztig-levels} (concordance.tex constitutional entry); Serre 1973 \emph{A Course in Arithmetic} Ch.~V (signature invariant); Bruinier 2002 LNM 1780 Prop.~5.1 (Heegner-Chern reciprocity); Lusztig 1990 \emph{Geom.\ Dedicata}~35 Rem.~3.2 (root-of-unity order); Etingof--Kazhdan 2007 Part V \S3 (super-quasi-Hopf Manin-pair quantisation); Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 Prop.~5.1 (Enriques lattice embedding); Mukai 1984 \emph{Invent.\ Math.}~77 (paramodular signature $c_+(\mathrm{II}_{4,20}) = 4$); Borcherds 1990 Invent Math 99 (Fake-Monster); Borcherds 1992 Invent Math 109 (Monster); Borcherds 1998 Invent Math 132 Thm 13.3 (all four Borcherds lifts); Scheithauer 2008 (super-Fricke for $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$). Cross-ref: Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-universal-identity} (universal three-faces identity, the source); Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-enriques-psi-landscape} ($\Psi$-landscape row-by-row evaluation); Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-conway-universal-identity-fails} (Leech scope failure); Vol~III Rem~\ref{rem:bkm-ratio-of-levels-triangulation} (three-path triangulation); cache #W22 AP-307 scope note (Monster lies outside CY-3 fibre coincidence, consistent with universal $\ell = 2c_+$). | ratio-of-Lusztig-levels law: $\ell(\mathbf H_X)/\ell(\mathbf H_Y) = c_+(L_X)/c_+(L_Y)$ on the four-row $\Psi$-image landscape; $\ell = 2c_+$ factors Lusztig through Mukai-positive-signature; Mukai-doubling cancels in ratios; Leech $V^{s\natural}$ row outside scope (positive-definite, no Fricke) |
| W22-chiral-kontsevich-obstruction-class-is-wall-of-walls-only-vs-per-wall-global-sheaf | "The chiral Kontsevich formality obstruction is defined only on wall-of-walls intersections $H_i\cap H_j$ as the bi-refined class $c_ic_j$; there is no single-wall obstruction class on each admissible Humbert divisor $H_n$ separately." | The bi-refined class $c_ic_j$ on wall-of-walls is real (three-way presentation agreement), is the Theorem~D class $\kappa\cdot\lambda_2|_{H_i\cap H_j}$ at genus two, and does control the chain-level splitting on each wall-of-walls in the bi-unipotent pro-ambient. | Stops short of the globalised obstruction-sheaf statement. Collapsing to wall-of-walls-only obstacles hides the single-admissible-discriminant obstruction and prevents the Malcev-ladder rung identification $\obKont_n=[\mathrm{gr}_n^{\mathrm{Malcev}}]$. | Chiral Kontsevich formality obstructions live on three strata simultaneously: (1) per-wall $\obKont_n\in H^3(H_n,\mathrm{Sym}^2\Tpolych|_{H_n})=c_n=[\mathrm{gr}_n^{\mathrm{Malcev}}]$ the Malcev-ladder $n$-th rung classifying cocycle (Thm thm:chiral-kontsevich-formality-unified (b), Def def:global-kontsevich-obstruction-sheaf); (2) wall-of-walls bi-refined $\obKont_{ij}=c_ic_j\in H^3(H_i\cap H_j,\ldots)=[\mathrm{gr}_{i,j}^{\mathrm{Malcev}}]$ the bi-unipotent pro-ambient classifying cocycle (Thm thm:wall-of-walls-obstruction, Rem rem:wall-of-walls-obstruction-as-extension-class); (3) global obstruction sheaf $\obKont\in H^3(\overline{\mathcal A}_2,\mathrm{Sym}^2\Tpolych)$ assembled by locally-finite pushforward $\sum_n\iota_{n,*}\obKont_n$ (Def def:global-kontsevich-obstruction-sheaf). Chain-level splitting $h^{\{\chi_n,k_n\}}_{\mathrm{Malcev}(\{n\})}$ of the single-admissible-discriminant restriction satisfies $[d^{\Gamma},h]=\mathrm{id}-p^{\Gamma}_{H_n}$. Five ingredients assembled in one statement: (I) Kontsevich admissible-graph $L_\infty$-formula (Kontsevich 1997 arXiv:q-alg/9709040 Thm 4.1, globalised via Tamarkin 1998 arXiv:math/9803025); (II) Costello--Gwilliam factorisation polyvector fields (CG17 \S 6.3 factorisation-derivation model); (III) Francis--Gaitsgory BD chiralisation (Francis 2013 Adv Math 239 Thm 1.1 factorisation-operad formality induces $\ChirHoch$-formality); (IV) W21.3 bi-unipotent factorisation compatibility (e1\_modular\_koszul.tex Thm thm:bd-factorisation-bi-unipotent-compatibility); (V) W21.1 Malcev ladder cocycle (mc5\_class\_m\_chain\_level\_platonic.tex Def def:malcev-ladder-admissible-heegner). $\Uadm=\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Humb}}^{\mathrm{c}}=\overline{\mathcal A}_2\setminus\bigcup_n H_n$ is the maximal open of bar--cobar strictness (Lem lem:uadm-is-koszul-locus-bar-cobar); the unified statement is Thm thm:chiral-kontsevich-formality-unified. The true closed form for this seed is the residue of its generating series at z = 1/rho, NOT the reciprocal of rho^2 + 2 (the latter is for a different seed / variant). | Correct Binet constant for seed (1, 0, 1, 1) / Brown 2011 enumeration: C ~ 0.3106288403 = (residue of generating series at z=1/rho); module should have `padovan_asymptotic(n) = C * rho^n` with C computed from the matching linear combination of the three roots of x^3 - x - 1 evaluated at the initial data (d_1, d_2, d_3). | 310-W23-chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait-shadow-finite-zero-vs-infinite-depth-W3Zam | Every standard archetype (Heisenberg $\mathsf G$, affine Kac-Moody $\mathsf L$, $\beta\gamma$ $\mathsf C$, Virasoro $\mathsf M$, BKM crown $\mathbf B$) admits a non-trivial $\ChirHoch^3$ class given by the Zamolodchikov $W_3$-extension generator ${:}T\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3 T$, plus a Yangian quantum tail $\hbar\cdot\mathrm{qt}(J^{(3)})$ on the crown. | The Zamolodchikov $W_3$-extension generator $W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}={:}T\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3 T$ IS the chain-level Hochschild $3$-cocycle on the rows carrying it ($\mathsf M$ and $\mathbf B$); the Polyakov W18 cocycle $\chi_3^{\mathbf B}=W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}+\hbar\cdot\mathrm{qt}(J^{(3)})$ on the crown row is the $\hbar$-deformed lift under the CoHA$\to Y^+\to$ VOA dictionary; the shadow-tower depth $r_{\max}(\cA)\in\{2,3,4,\infty\}$ IS the discriminating invariant separating finite-depth from infinite-depth rows. | Conflates the common skeleton reading with the actual chain-level non-vanishing. Rows $\mathsf G,\mathsf L,\mathsf C$ have $r_{\max}<\infty$ and generic averaged $\kappa^!=-\kappa$, forcing $[\chi_3^{\cA}]=0$ through archetype-specific coboundary primitives; Theorem H's ambient-curve concentration $\{0,1,2\}$ forbids degree-$3$ on the shadow-finite rows. The non-zero rows are exactly $\mathsf M$ (Virasoro, ambient-curve scope, $\kappa+\kappa^!=13$) and $\mathbf B$ (BKM crown, CY-$3$-enlarged ambient, $\kappa+\kappa^!=8$), both at $r_{\max}=\infty$. | Five-archetype portrait of $\ChirHoch^3$ with row-specific verdict + three verification paths per row: (a) Row $\mathsf G$ ($\mathcal H_k$, $k\ne 0$): $[\chi_3^{\mathcal H}]=0$ via shadow-tower truncation at $r_{\max}=2$ (no $S_3$); Arnold-form charge-neutrality (U(1)-conservation kills $\langle aaa\rangle$); Koszul self-identification $\mathcal H_k^!=\mathcal H_{-k}$ with polynomial Hochschild cohomology in amplitude $\{0,1,2\}$. Primitive $\beta_2^{\mathcal H}(a_1,a_2;z_1,z_2)=(z_1-z_2)^{-2}\langle a_1,a_2\rangle_k\cdot\partial/\partial z_1$. (b) Row $\mathsf L$ ($V_k(\mathfrak g)$, $k+h^\vee\ne 0$): $[\chi_3^{V_k}]=0$ via Gelfand--Fuks loop-algebra cohomology projecting to zero in the quotient by $\mathcal Z(\widehat{\mathfrak g})$ (Frenkel--Ben-Zvi 2004 Thm 7.1.1); BD $\mathcal W$-symmetry forces degree-3 zero outside Arakawa 2007 admissible loci; Positselski dualisation $V_k^!=V_{-k-2h^\vee}$ (Arakawa 2017 JAMS 30 Thm 9.1.4) keeps amplitude $\{0,1,2\}$. Primitive $\beta_2^{\mathrm{GF}}=(1/2(k+h^\vee)){:}J^a J_a{:}\partial/\partial z$ (Sugawara descent). (c) Row $\mathsf C$ ($\beta\gamma_\lambda$, $\lambda\ne 1/2$): $[\chi_3^{\beta\gamma}]=0$ via $bc$-ghost coboundary (fermionic triples $\partial$-exact on free spinor rep; Friedan--Martinec--Shenker 1986 NPB 271 \S4); fermion-number Arnold factorisation (3-pt function factors through single $\eta_{12}-\eta_{23}$); free-field amplitude $\{0,1,2\}$. Primitive $\beta_2^{\mathrm{ghost}}=-{:}\beta\gamma{:}(z)\partial/\partial z$. (d) Row $\mathsf M$ ($\mathrm{Vir}_c$, $c\notin\{c_{p,q}\}$): $[\chi_3^{\mathrm{Vir}}]=\mathbb C\cdot[W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}]$ with $W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}={:}T\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3 T$ (weight-5 quasi-primary, Zamolodchikov 1985 TMP 65 eq (2.6)); three paths: Zamolodchikov W3 non-exactness via $[W_3,W_3]\ne 0$ (Bouwknegt--Schoutens 1993 PR 223 \S3.2); Gelfand--Fuks one-dimensional $H^3_{\mathrm{GF}}(\mathfrak{vect}(S^1))$ (Gelfand--Fuks 1970; Feigin 1988 RMS 43 Thm 1.2); shadow-tower pinning $S_3=2$ and Zamolodchikov normalisation $\langle\Lambda|\Lambda\rangle=c(5c+22)/10$ with $\Lambda={:}TT{:}-(3/10)\partial^2 T$. (e) Row $\mathbf B$ (BKM crown $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}=\Phi_3(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$): $[\chi_3^{\mathbf B}]=\mathbb C\cdot[{:}T\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3 T+\hbar\cdot\mathrm{qt}(J^{(3)})]$ on CY-3-enlarged ambient $X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$; four verification paths (triangle-cycle, DT/$\Phi_{10}^{-1}$, CoHA Casimir, Siegel--Eisenstein central-$L$ residue) pin $\langle[\chi_3^{\mathbf B}],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\rangle_{\Phi_3}=2\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi i)^3=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Res}_{s=1/2}[E_5^{(2)}(Z,s)]|_{K(1)}$. Unified classical limit $\chi_3^{\mathbf B}|_{\hbar=0,\mathrm{K3}=\mathrm{pt}}=\chi_3^{\mathrm{Vir}}=W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}$ shows $\mathsf M$ and $\mathbf B$ share the Virasoro skeleton; the Yangian quantum tail $\hbar\cdot\mathrm{qt}(J^{(3)})$ is the BKM-specific Planck-order addition from the K3$\times E$ Mukai pairing. Structural law: $[\chi_3^{\cA}]\ne 0 \Leftrightarrow r_{\max}(\cA)=\infty$; the shadow-finite rows refuse the weight-$5$ quasi-primary content. Primary: Zamolodchikov 1985 \emph{Theor Math Phys} 65 eq (2.6) ($W_3$-extension generator); Gelfand--Fuks 1970 \emph{Funct Anal Appl} 4 (loop-algebra $H^3$); Feigin 1988 \emph{Russ Math Surv} 43 Thm 1.2 ($H^3_{\mathrm{GF}}(\mathfrak{vect}(S^1))$ one-dim); Frenkel--Ben-Zvi 2004 \emph{VA and AG Curves} Thm 7.1.1 (Sugawara class quotient); Beilinson--Drinfeld \emph{Chiral Algebras} \S3.6 ($\mathcal W$-symmetry); Arakawa 2017 JAMS 30 Thm 9.1.4 (affine Positselski); Bouwknegt--Schoutens 1993 \emph{Phys Rep} 223 \S3.2 (W3 OPE non-exactness); Friedan--Martinec--Shenker 1986 NPB 271 \S4 ($bc$-ghost); Kac 1998 \emph{VAB} \S2.5 (Heisenberg 3-pt vanishing); Feigin--Frenkel 1988 CMP 117 (critical-level reflection); Schiffmann--Vasserot 2013 \emph{Publ IHES} 118 Thm B (CoHA degree-3 generator); Maulik--Okounkov 2019 \emph{Ast\'erisque} 408 Thm 1.4 (stable envelope); Oberdieck 2018 \emph{Geom \& Topol} 22 \S5 (DT--$\Phi_{10}^{-1}$). | 427 | The classical Feigin--Tsygan identification $\HCLie^\bullet(\mathfrak{gl}_\infty(A))\cong\HH^\bullet(A)$ (Feigin--Tsygan 1987 LNM 1289 Thm 3.1) transports verbatim to chiral bialgebras such as $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$, so the cyclic-cohomology derivation of $[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ is obtained by substituting "chiral" for "associative" in the classical theorem. | The classical FT identification is real for associative $A$; $\ChirHoch^\bullet$ does admit a cyclic/mixed-complex enhancement on the Koszul locus; Connes 1985 Publ IHES 62 mixed-complex axioms and SBI do transport through Francis--Gaitsgory factorisation formality to the chiral setting; the CY-$3$ trace class really is a Feigin--Tsygan cyclic class in the appropriate chiral ambient. | Conflates FIVE distinct steps into one transport: (a) the classical FT theorem hypothesises $A$ associative; $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ is an $E_1$-chiral super-quasi-Hopf bialgebra, NOT associative; (b) Connes $B$-operator requires $b^2=0,\,B^2=0,\,[b,B]=0$ as a mixed complex, but $\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}=\partial^{\mathrm{face}}+\partial^{\mathrm{conf}}$ carries no a priori cyclic rotation; (c) SBI exact sequence $\HC^{n-2}\to\HC^n\to\HH^n\to\HC^{n-1}$ needs the invertibility of $S$, which fails without Kontsevich-formality spectral-sequence collapse; (d) CoHA $[\chi_3]$ and cyclic-side $[\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY-3}}]$ use different chain-level models (polyvector sector vs $\glinf$-Lie-cyclic sector); (e) numerical evaluation $2\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi i)^3$ is not automatic from the isomorphism --- it requires explicit Serre-dual generator computation with Mukai factor $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$, elliptic period $\int_E[\omega_E]=\mathrm{Vol}(E)$, and three Arnold forms contributing $(2\pi i)^3$. Each step has its own obstruction and its own primary source. Conflating any two collapses the fifth verification path into a tautology. | The chiral Feigin--Tsygan theorem (Thm thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan in hochschild\_cohomology.tex) is not the classical FT theorem with a scope qualifier; it is a distinct five-step proof. Each step must be inscribed separately: (1) replace $\mathfrak{gl}_\infty(A)$ by $\mathfrak{gl}_\infty(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ in the Francis--Gaitsgory (FG12 Selecta 18 \S6.2) $\infty$-operadic ambient (Arnold-homotopy commutative target); (2) supply the $S^1$-action on the factorisation trace (FG12 \S6.3 construction; Kapranov 1999 Compos Math 115 \S3 for Arnold-cochain cyclic compatibility) as the chiral Connes operator $B^{\mathrm{ch}}$, with $[\partial^{\mathrm{ch}},B^{\mathrm{ch}}]=0$ on $\Uadm$; (3) restrict SBI to the Koszul locus where $S$ is invertible by Kontsevich (Kon03 LMP 66) formality collapse of $\partial^{\mathrm{conf}}$-spectral-sequence pages (FG12 \S6.4); (4) match cFT image with CoHA class via Kontsevich admissible-graph integral (Tamarkin--Hinich globalisation, DolTamTsy09 LMP 90); (5) evaluate on Serre-dual generator to produce $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi i)^3$. Three cyclic theories coexist: ordinary $\HC^\bullet_{\mathrm{alg}}$ on discrete algebras (Connes85), topological $\mathrm{TC}/\mathrm{TP}$ on ring spectra (B\"okstedt--Hsiang--Madsen 1993 Invent Math 111), chiral $\HC^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}$ on chiral algebras (this theorem); each has its own mixed-complex axioms, its own SBI, its own target. Scope: the chiral cyclic structure exists on the Koszul locus $\Uadm=\overline{\mathcal A}_2\setminus\bigcup_n H_n$; off $\Uadm$ the obstruction is $\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{Kont}}_n=c_n\ne 0$ the Bruinier Heegner Chern class (cache \#174, \#176). The fifth verification path (Path E: cyclic Feigin--Tsygan) is epistemically disjoint from Path A (CoHA Casimir), Path B (Igusa $\Phi_{10}^{-1}$), Path C (elliptic-volume rigidity), Path D (relative HPD). Primary: Feigin--Tsygan 1987 LNM 1289 Thm 3.1 (classical FT for associative $A$); Connes 1985 Publ IHES 62 Def II.1 (mixed complex axioms); Loday 1998 Grundlehren 301 Ch.~2 (mixed complex), Ch.~10 Thm 10.2.4 (Loday--Quillen); Francis--Gaitsgory 2012 Selecta 18 \S6.2--6.4 (factorisation $\infty$-operadic cyclic structure); Kontsevich 2003 LMP 66 Thm 1.1 (formality); Tamarkin 2003 LMP 66 + Hinich 2003 JPAA 184 (globalisation); Dolgushev--Tamarkin--Tsygan 2009 LMP 90 (Hochschild formality applications); B\"okstedt--Hsiang--Madsen 1993 Invent Math 111 (TC / TP); Mukai 1987 \emph{Symposium on algebraic geometry} Thm 1.5 ($\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$); Caldararu 2005 Adv Math 194 \S4.2 (CY-$d$ Serre duality). Cross-ref: AP277 (SC bicoloured vs $E_3$ single-coloured); AP296 (THH vs classical HH); AP297 (Theorem-H theory erasure); cache \#174 (chiral Kontsevich formality scope vs Humbert obstruction); cache \#176 (per-wall vs global obstruction sheaf); Rem rem:cft-chiral-vs-ordinary of hochschild\_cohomology.tex. | chiral vs ordinary cyclic homology: Feigin--Tsygan transport to chiral bialgebras requires FIVE-step proof (non-associative target, Connes lift via FG12 $S^1$-action, SBI on Koszul locus, CoHA matching via Kontsevich formality, explicit Serre-dual numerical evaluation), NOT a verbatim substitution; three cyclic theories (ordinary / topological / chiral) remain distinct |
| W23-universal-k-tower-malcev-closure-siegel-radical-dim-genus-ladder | The bi-unipotent ladder on $\overline{\mathcal A_2}$, the tri-unipotent extension at codim $3$, and the codim-$4$ emptiness are three separate theorems about three separate phenomena on $\overline{\mathcal A_2}$, specific to genus $2$; higher-genus behaviour requires its own separate treatment. | There IS a universal $k$-tower Malcev closure structure parametrised by $(g,k)$: for each codim-$k$ admissible Heegner intersection on $\overline{\mathcal A_g}$, either empty (Hodge-index signature $(1,k-1)$ unrealisable on the rank-$g(g+1)/2$ Shioda--Mitani lattice) or supports a $k$-unipotent Malcev extension with commuting $\mathfrak{sl}_2^{\oplus k}$-triple (CKS multivariable nilpotent orbit); the closure index is genus-parametric. | Conflates three successive frames of one ladder with three unrelated theorems. The unifying invariant is $k_{\max}(g)=\dim U^{\mathrm{Sieg}}_g=\dim\mathrm{Sym}^2(\mathbb Q^g)=g(g+1)/2=\dim\overline{\mathcal A_g}$, the dimension of the abelian unipotent radical of the Siegel parabolic $P^{\mathrm{Sieg}}\subset\mathrm{Sp}_{2g}$. The bi-unipotent/tri-unipotent/codim-$4$-emptiness triad on $\overline{\mathcal A_2}$ is the genus-$2$ specialisation ($k_{\max}(2)=3$) of a single $(g,k)$-parametric statement; the Hodge signature $(1,k-1)$ is the universal existence criterion; the $k$-unipotent chain homotopy formula is the universal object. Treating each codim level as a separate theorem loses the genus ladder $\kmax(1)=1,\kmax(2)=3,\kmax(3)=6,\kmax(4)=10,\ldots$ and obscures the identity $k_{\max}(g)=\dim\overline{\mathcal A_g}$. | Universal theorem: for $(g,k)$ with $k\ge 1$, an admissible Heegner $k$-tuple $(n_1,\ldots,n_k)$ on $\overline{\mathcal A_g}$ has intersection $\bigcap_i H_{n_i}$ either empty (if $k>\kmax(g)=g(g+1)/2$ or if signature $(1,k-1)$ unrealised on $\Lambda_{n_1,\ldots,n_k}\hookrightarrow G^{\mathrm{SM}}_D$) or a CM subscheme of codim $k$ supporting the $k$-unipotent Malcev extension with commuting $\mathfrak{sl}_2^{\oplus k}$-triple $\{(N_i,N_i^+,Y_i)\}_{i=1}^k$; chain homotopy $h^{\{\chi_i,k_i\}}_{\mathrm{k\text{-}uni}}=\prod_i M^{(\chi_i)}_{H_{n_i}}\circ(\sum_i N_i+\lambda_{\{k_i\}}\mathrm{id})^{-1}\circ(\mathrm{id}+\sigma h^{(g)})^{-1}\circ\sigma$ satisfies $[d^{\mathrm{k\text{-}uni}}_{\mathrm{bar}},h^{\mathrm{k\text{-}uni}}]=\mathrm{id}-\prod_i p^{\Gamma}_{H_{n_i}}$. Three verification paths: (V1) \emph{Hodge-index genus-by-genus enumeration}: Sylvester signature $(1,k-1)\Leftrightarrow\det G>0,\,\det G_{k-1}<0,\ldots$ on Cauchy--Schwarz box $\prod_{i<j}\{|g_{ij}|\le\sqrt{n_in_j}\}$; discriminant-square condition $\det G^{\mathrm{SM}}_D/\det G_{n_1,\ldots,n_k}\in\mathbb Q_{>0}^{\times 2}$ via primitive embedding into $\mathrm{NS}(E^g_{CM})$; finite arithmetic check per $(n_1,\ldots,n_k)$; at $k>g(g+1)/2$ no realisation on the rank-$g(g+1)/2$ Shioda--Mitani lattice. (V2) \emph{Baily--Borel rank stratification}: Siegel parabolic $P^{\mathrm{Sieg}}\subset\mathrm{Sp}_{2g}$ has abelian unipotent radical $U^{\mathrm{Sieg}}_g\simeq\mathrm{Sym}^2(\mathbb Q^g)$ of $\mathbb Q$-dim $g(g+1)/2$; Schmid 1973 \S 5 Thm 5.13 assigns each admissible $H_r$ a nilpotent $N_r\in U^{\mathrm{Sieg}}_g$; CKS 1986 Cor 3.13 identifies primitive component with $[\mathrm{obs}^{\mathrm{strict}}_{H_r}]$; closure index is the vector-space dim of the ambient. (V3) \emph{CKS multi-variable nilpotent orbit}: Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986 Thm 3.3 constructs the $n$-variable nilpotent orbit for pairwise commuting nilpotents on polarised $\mathbb Q$-Hodge structures; applied to $n=k$ admissible monodromies, orbit exists iff pairwise commute in $U^{\mathrm{Sieg}}_g$, capped by $\dim U^{\mathrm{Sieg}}_g=g(g+1)/2$. Paths epistemically disjoint: (V1) Sylvester--Shioda--Mitani arithmetic, (V2) Baily--Borel--Schmid geometry, (V3) CKS nilpotent-orbit Hodge theory. Genus ladder: $\kmax(1)=1,\kmax(2)=3,\kmax(3)=6,\kmax(4)=10,\kmax(5)=15$; first genus with $\kmax\ge 4$ is $g=3$; first with $\kmax\ge 10$ is $g=4$. The octachotomy of the chain-level ambient tower on $\overline{\mathcal A_2}$ generalises to a $(\kmax(g)+5)$-chotomy on $\overline{\mathcal A_g}$: $\kmax(g)$ codim-stratified $k$-unipotent Malcev extensions plus five universal ambients (Koszul locus, admissible-union ladder, Baily--Borel cusp, weight-completed coderived, $A_\infty$-correction near $H_3$). Primary inputs: Van der Geer 1988 \emph{Hilbert Modular Surfaces} Ch.~IX \S 1 (Humbert); Shioda--Mitani 1974 \emph{Classification of algebraic varieties and compact complex manifolds} \S 1 (generalisation to $E^g$); Schmid 1973 \emph{Invent Math} 22 \S 5 Thm 5.13 (nilpotent orbit); Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986 \emph{Ann Math} 123 Thm 3.3, \S 3.7, Cor 3.13 (multi-variable SCK); Bruinier 2002 \emph{LNM} 1780 Thm 3.22; Kudla--Rapoport 2000 \emph{Ann Sci ENS} 33 \S 3. Inscribed: Vol I chapters/theory/mc5\_class\_m\_chain\_level\_platonic.tex \S subsec:universal-k-tower-malcev-closure, Thm thm:universal-k-tower-malcev-closure (parts (a)--(e): closure index, Hodge-index criterion, $k$-unipotent Malcev extension, universal emptiness at $k>\kmax(g)$, genus ladder), Rem rem:three-verification-paths-universal-k-tower, Rem rem:closure-index-universal-invariant. | W23.4-g4-schottky-vs-NL-divisor-class-distinction | The Schottky locus $\SchFour\subset\AbarFour$ is absorbed into the Noether--Lefschetz stratification of the Malcev ladder (equivalently, the Schottky--Jung quartic $J^{(4)}$ is a rational combination of Humbert/Heegner Chern classes on $\AbarFour$). | The Schottky locus and Noether--Lefschetz divisors are both codimension-$1$ Cartier divisors on $\AbarFour$, and both support $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-unipotent local monodromy of Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid type, so a rung of the Malcev ladder does indeed exist on each. | Conflates coincidence of codimension with coincidence of class. The Schottky class $[\SchFour]=8\lambda\in\mathrm{Pic}(\AbarFour)\otimes\mathbb Q$ (van~der~Geer--Katsura 2003) is independent of the NL-classes $[\NLdivFour_\Delta]=\Delta\lambda-\sum_D c_{\Delta,D}[\partial_D]$ in the Picard group, because NL carries non-trivial toroidal-boundary corrections and Schottky does not (Schottky--Jung relations are pure theta-null identities). The Schottky monodromy $N^{\mathrm{Sch}}$ is geometrically half-integer theta-characteristic transport, not a Heegner unipotent; it commutes with NL-unipotents on mixed intersections only through the Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid completion of an \emph{independent} commuting pair. | Genus-$4$ Malcev ladder requires a \emph{separate} bi-unipotent structure $(N^{\mathrm{Sch}},N^{\mathrm{NL}}_\Delta)$ on $\SchFour\cap\NLdivFour_\Delta$ with its own $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-triple, not a reduction of an NL-doublet. The $g=4$ twenty-stratum tower of Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hgmk-abar4-bar-cobar-scope}} / Corollary~\textup{\ref{cor:hgmk-abar4-twenty-stratum}} inscribes the Schottky block as its own stratum class. Three verification paths: (V1) direct Gram signature at codim-$1$ Schottky: Jacobian $\partial J^{(4)}/\partial Z$ gives rank-$1$ normal bundle section, signature $(1,0)$, matching mono-unipotent rung; (V2) Faltings--Chai toroidal cusp limit: Schottky limits to codim-$1$ face of the rank-$3$ cusp $\partial_3$ with Siegel Eisenstein weight-$8$ section normalising the scalar homotopy; (V3) Schottky--Jung reciprocity (Welters 1984, Donagi 1987): $\theta$-characteristic reciprocity gives explicit coboundary primitive $\gamma_1^{\mathrm{Sch}}(Z)=\sum_\sigma\mathrm{sign}(\sigma)\theta[m_0+\sigma](Z,0)^2$. Primary: Igusa 1981 Am J Math 103 (Schottky quartic on $\AbarFour$ irreducible); van~Geemen 1984 Invent Math 78 Thm 0.1 (Schottky--Jung quartic for $g=4$); Welters 1984 Compositio 49 (Schottky--Jung reciprocity); Donagi 1987 Bull AMS 16 (Schottky--Jung relations); Grushevsky 2012 (survey of Schottky problem for $g\leq 5$); van~der~Geer--Katsura 2003 (Schottky class $=8\lambda$ vs NL classes, independent in Picard); Faltings--Chai 1990 Ch.~II, Thm.~5.2 (rank-stratified Satake boundary $\partial_r$, $0\leq r\leq g$); Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986 Ann Math 123 Thm 3.3 (multi-variable $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-orbit for commuting unipotents); Hain 1997 (Malcev completion of $\pi_1(\mathcal A_g)$); Arbarello 1987 (Torelli for $g=4$ injective on open dense). Genus-scaling extension: stratum count $N_g=1+g(g+1)/2+B^{\mathrm{Sch}}(g)+1+g+2$ with $B^{\mathrm{Sch}}(2)=B^{\mathrm{Sch}}(3)=0$ (Torelli codim $0$); $B^{\mathrm{Sch}}(4)=2$ (Schottky quartic + mixed Schottky-NL block); $B^{\mathrm{Sch}}(5)=4$ (Andreotti--Mayer stratification introduces two additional blocks at codim $2$). Predicts $N_2=8,\ N_3=13,\ N_4=20,\ N_5=28$ -- cubic-like growth tracked by the Satake-boundary count $g+1$ and the Andreotti--Mayer codimension $\max(0,g-3)$. | 428 | If the BKM crown $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ carries an explicit non-vanishing $\chi_3 \in \mathrm{ChirHoch}^3$ (Polyakov 2020: ${:}T\partial T{:} - (1/4)\partial^3 T + \hbar\cdot\mathrm{qt}(J^{(3)})$), then by the universal-formality philosophy every archetype G / L / C / M / B admits a non-trivial top-degree Hochschild class of the same shape. | There is a universal degree-$3$ template: the Polyakov cocycle ${:}T\partial T{:} - (1/4)\partial^3 T$ is genuinely the Zamolodchikov $W_3$-extension of Virasoro and survives chain-level closure modulo derivatives; this is the $\hbar \to 0$ limit of the BKM Polyakov cocycle; the universal-template observation is correct. | Uniform non-vanishing across G / L / C / M / B collapses the shadow-tower-depth hierarchy $r_{\max} \in \{2, 3, 4, \infty, \infty\}$ into a single row. Heisenberg ($r_{\max}=2$) has no $S_3$ — every degree-$3$ class is a derivative of $S_{\le 2}$-content, hence $\partial$-exact. Affine KM at $k + h^\vee \ne 0$ ($r_{\max}=3$) has a Gelfand-Fuks sub-primary at $S_3$, but the chain-level closure routes through Kac--Moody invariant-theoretic reductions which kill the degree-$3$ class on the ambient-curve scope. $\beta\gamma$ at $\lambda \ne 1/2$ ($r_{\max}=4$) has four shadow coefficients but ghost-field parity forces $\chi_3^{\beta\gamma} = \partial\beta_2^{\mathrm{ghost}}$ exact. Only class M (Virasoro, $r_{\max} = \infty$) and class B (BKM crown $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$, $r_{\max} = \infty$) support a non-trivial $\chi_3$: the $W_3$-extension module has genuine infinite-depth content tied to the $:T\partial T: - (1/4)\partial^3 T$ composite. The two non-vanishing rows coincide up to the quantum tail $\hbar\cdot\mathrm{qt}(J^{(3)})$: class M is the $\hbar \to 0$ limit of class B. Depth-$\infty$ classification is the discriminator. Three verification paths per row: (V1) shadow-tower truncation, (V2) Arnold-form charge / parity argument, (V3) Koszul self-identification or archetype-specific cross-check (e.g. Wakimoto bosonisation for class L, BRST decoupling for class C, $W_3$-extension module for class M, $\Phi_3$-CY-$3$ enlargement for class B). | 430 | The Auslander--Reiten translate on a 2-morphism category in an $(\infty, 2)$-setting is the classical Dlab--Ringel reflection functor, transported verbatim. | There is a genuine Auslander--Reiten translate visible on stable $\infty$-categories; Dyckerhoff--Kapranov supply the Serre-spherical formalism. | On a stable $(\infty, 2)$-category with Serre functor $\mathbb{S}$, the AR-translate is $\tau_{\mathrm{AR}} = \mathbb{S} \circ [-1]$ acting on 2-morphisms (not 1-morphisms), with the AR-triangle $\tau_{\mathrm{AR}}(\eta) \to E(\eta) \to \eta \to \Sigma\tau_{\mathrm{AR}}(\eta)$. The $[-2]$-Serre-shift arising from K3-CY$_2$ gives $\tau_{\mathrm{AR}} = [-3]$ on $\Def(\mathfrak{g}^{\infty,1}_A)$-cohomology, not $[-1]$. Dlab--Ringel reflection assumes finite-dimensional representation theory, so importing it verbatim into the chiral setting is a type error. | Every AR-triangle statement in the programme must: (i) name the ambient stable $\infty$-category; (ii) name the Serre autoequivalence (here $\mathbb{S}_{(\infty,2)} = [2]$ on $\Perf(\AbarTwo)$, descending to $[-2]$ on $\Def(\mathfrak{g}^{\infty,1}_A)$-cohomology); (iii) compute $\tau_{\mathrm{AR}} = \mathbb{S} \circ [-1]$ explicitly; (iv) cite Dyckerhoff--Kapranov $\S 6.4$ Serre-spherical framework, not Dlab--Ringel. | 431 | [W22.6 HK-restricted Phi_4] The CY-$4$ chiralisation hypothesis $\mathbf H_{\PhiFour}$ is uniformly obstructed on every smooth projective CY-$4$ by the Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina 3d/4d dichotomy; $\ChirHoch^4$ on any CY-$4$ (including $\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}$) therefore must wait for an $8$d-chiral boundary construction. | The generic obstruction is real on CY-$4$s without a distinguished transverse circle: Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina 2009 J Topol 2 Thm 1.1 feeds $\Phi_3$ a 3d topological boundary; Oh--Thomas 2023 Duke 172 Thm 1.1 produces virtual counts but not a chiralisation; Nekrasov 2020 arXiv:1712.08128 \S 4 defines an 8d partition function without a factorisation $E_4$-algebra on a curve; $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}})=4\ne 0$ is the expected top-class weight. | Confuses \emph{generic} CY-$4$ obstruction with \emph{every} CY-$4$. The meridian $S^1_{\mathrm{tw}}\subset\mathbb P^1_{\mathrm{tw}}$ is a Killing circle for the holomorphic symplectic pairing; reducing the 4d target along $S^1_{\mathrm{tw}}$ lands in a 3d $\mathcal N=4$ sigma model, the Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina input to $\Phi_3$.
