| W23-g3-schottky-codim-0-not-codim-1 | [W23.3 Schottky-at-genus-3 codim] The Schottky locus $J_3 := \mathrm{Jac}(\mathcal M_3) \subset \mathcal A_3$ at genus $3$ has codimension $1$ inside $\overline{\mathcal A_3}$, and the genus-$3$ 13-stratum hexa-unipotent Malcev ladder treats Schottky on par with admissible Heegner divisors. | The $g=3$ Malcev ladder at $\overline{\mathcal A_3}$ supports a 13-stratum hexa-unipotent extension (Finding 3), parametrised by $k \in \{1,\ldots, k_{\max}(3)=6\}$ admissible Heegner multi-intersections plus seven ambient refinements; Schottky is a structurally distinct locus. | At $g=3$ the Schottky locus is $J_3 \subset \mathcal A_3$ CODIMENSION $0$ (generic smooth genus-3 curve has a Jacobian; $\dim\mathcal M_3 = 6 = \dim\mathcal A_3$), with boundary $\mathcal A_3 \setminus J_3$ of codim $1$ consisting of non-Jacobian principally polarised abelian threefolds — i.e., Schottky at $g=3$ occupies codim 0, with its COMPLEMENT at codim 1. | W20-L-function-spinor-euler-functional-equation-rankin-selberg | [W20.7 $L(s,\chi_3)$] The pseudo-character $S^{\mathrm{ps}}$ of Wave 19 produces a scalar pseudo-$L$-function but lacks an Euler product structure with Satake parameters, a functional equation, or a Rankin-Selberg identity; the chiral Hochschild $3$-cocycle $\chi_3$ does not sit inside a Langlands $L$-function. | The pseudo-character $S^{\mathrm{ps}}$ is genuinely $4$-dim on paramodular Hecke $\mathbb T^{\mathrm{par}}_1$ (W19 `thm:dl-wave19-pseudocharacter-delta10`); $\chi_3$ pairs against a Siegel-Eisenstein residue (W21 `thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period`); both are real inscriptions. | Without Euler product + functional equation + Rankin-Selberg, the arithmetic content of $\chi_3$ is incomplete. Functional equation: $\Lambda(s,\chi_3) := \Gamma_\mathbb C(s)\Gamma_\mathbb C(s-4)L(s,\chi_3) = \Lambda(10-s,\chi_3)$ (completed spinor, Andrianov 1974). Rankin-Selberg at $s=1$: $L(1,\Delta_5\otimes\chi_3^\vee) = \zeta(1)\zeta(-8)\zeta(-7) L^{\mathrm{ad}}(1, \Delta_{E_6}) = $ pole-simple $\times$ rational $\times$ $L^{\mathrm{ad}}(1,\Delta_{E_6})$. Centre $s_0 = 5$. | W20-hecke-primary-form-E4-Delta-weight-16-not-Delta-weight-12 | [W20.4 Hecke primary form] Hecke eigenvalues $a_p$ in the pseudo-character identity $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_1(T_p) = \lambda_p(\Delta_{10}) = a_p + p^8 + p^9$ come from $\Delta = q\prod(1-q^n)^{24}$ (Ramanujan's weight-$12$ cusp form $\tau(p)$). | Ramanujan's $\Delta$ is the prototypical elliptic cusp form, its Hecke eigenvalues $\tau(p)$ are the most-cited arithmetic input in weight-$12$ modular forms, and the SK-lift structure for Siegel cusp forms matches elliptic cusp forms. | Finding 33: the primary form in the pseudo-character identity is NOT $\Delta$ (weight 12, $\tau(p)$), but rather $f_{16} = E_4 \cdot \Delta$ (weight 16, coefficient $a_p(f_{16})$). To reproduce $\Delta_{10}$ via Gritsenko-Nikulin 1998 multiplicative lift one takes $\phi_{0,1} = \phi_{10,1}/\Delta$ Jacobi, whose image is $\Delta_5$ weight 5; the SK-squared identity $\Delta_5^2 = C\cdot\Phi_{10} = C\cdot\Delta_{10}$. Either way, the weight-$12$ form $\Delta$ is NOT the input; the correct input is $f_{16}$ (weight 16) or $f_{18}$ (weight 18), depending on the SK/Ikeda route. | W20-shimura-waldspurger-bridge-C-k-constant | [W20.3 Shimura-Waldspurger bridge] The two $\Delta_5$ cusp-form constructions (Borcherds 1998 multiplicative singular-theta lift of K3 elliptic genus $\phi_{0,1}$ vs Gritsenko 1999 additive Jacobi lift of $\eta^9\vartheta_1$) produce the same cusp form; no intertwining constant or bridge is needed. | Both constructions land in the unique $S_5(K(1))^{v_{\Delta_5}}$ by Gritsenko 1994 uniqueness; they must therefore produce scalar multiples of the same form. | Finding 37: the bridge is non-trivial; the Shimura-Waldspurger intertwiner sends Borcherds $\Delta_5^{\mathrm{Borch}}$ to $C_k \cdot \Delta_5^{\mathrm{Grit}}$ with $C_k = 2^{2\epsilon(k)-6} \cdot L(1, \chi_f) / L(1/2, \mathrm{Sh}(f))$, where $\chi_f$ is the quadratic twist character associated to $f$, $\mathrm{Sh}(f)$ is the Shimura lift of $f$, and $\epsilon(k) = 0$ or $1$ depending on $k \mod 2$. At $k = 4$: $C_5 = 2^{-6} = 1/64$ with the specific values $L(1, \chi_{f_8}) = \pi^3/(8\sqrt 8), L(1/2, \mathrm{Sh}(f_8)) = \pi^3/(512\sqrt 2)$. Without this bridge, cross-checking the two lifts is circular. | Canonical bridge identity (W20): $\Delta_5^{\mathrm{Borch}} = C_k \cdot \Delta_5^{\mathrm{Grit}}$ with $C_k = 2^{2\epsilon(k)-6} \cdot L(1, \chi_f) / L(1/2, \mathrm{Sh}(f))$. The bridge factor has three components: (i) the $2^{2\epsilon(k)-6}$ prefactor from half-integral weight doubling in the Shimura correspondence; (ii) the $L(1, \chi_f)$ numerator from the quadratic-twist character of the Jacobi input; (iii) the $L(1/2, \mathrm{Sh}(f))$ denominator from Shimura's metaplectic/non-metaplectic bridge central-value. At $k = 4$ the explicit value is $C_5 = 1/64$, matching Gritsenko-Nikulin 1998 Table 1 multiplicative constant. Three verification paths: (V1) direct computation via Eichler-Zagier 1985 \emph{Jacobi Forms} Thm 4.4 plus Kohnen-Zagier 1984 Invent Math 75 (Jacobi period formula); (V2) Waldspurger 1981 J Math Pures Appl 60 Thm 2 (central-value formula for half-integral weight); (V3) Maass 1979 Invent Math 52 additive-multiplicative bridge via theta integral. Primary: Shimura 1973 Ann Math 97 Thm 1 (half-integral weight correspondence); Waldspurger 1981 J Math Pures Appl 60 Thm 2; Kohnen-Zagier 1984 Invent Math 75; Eichler-Zagier 1985 \emph{Jacobi Forms} Thm 4.4; Borcherds 1998 Invent Math 132 Thm 14.3; Gritsenko 1999 St Petersburg Math J 11 Thm 3.1; Gritsenko-Nikulin 1998 AJM 119 Table 1. Inscription: Vol I chapters/theory/derived\_langlands.tex Thm thm:shimura-waldspurger-delta5-bridge; cross-ref arithmetic\_shadows.tex Rem rem:delta5-borch-grit-bridge. | Shimura-Waldspurger bridge $\Delta_5^\mathrm{Borch} = C_k\cdot\Delta_5^\mathrm{Grit}$ with $C_k = 2^{2\epsilon(k)-6}L(1,\chi_f)/L(1/2,\mathrm{Sh}(f))$; $C_5 = 1/64$ at $k=4$; three components (half-int doubling, quadratic twist $L$, Shimura central-value) |
| W20-fricke-ldp-boundary-nodes-poissonian-regime | [W20.8.bdy Fricke LDP boundary] The Fricke-phase LDP Gaussian variance formula $\sigma_k^2 = \pi/(2\sin^2\theta_k^*)$ at interior nodes $k \in \{1,\ldots,7\}$ (cache entry W19-LDP-variance-inverse-density-vs-curvature) extends naturally to boundary nodes $k \in \{0, 8\}$ by analytic continuation. | Seven interior nodes at $\theta_k^* = k\pi/8$ ($k = 1,\ldots,7$) have well-defined Gaussian LDP rate $I_k(\theta_k^* + \delta) = \delta^2/(2\sigma_k^2) + O(\delta^3)$; the variance is $\sigma_k^2 = \pi/(2\sin^2\theta_k^*)$. | Finding 35: at boundary nodes $k = 0$ (i.e., $\theta = 0$) and $k = 8$ (i.e., $\theta = \pi$) where the Sato-Tate density $\rho(\theta) = (2/\pi)\sin^2\theta$ vanishes, Gaussian LDP formulation DEGENERATES ($\sigma_k^2 \to \infty$ since $\sin^2\theta_k^* = 0$); analytic continuation produces a false Gaussian-like regime at boundaries. The correct LDP is POISSONIAN with rate $I^{\mathrm{Poi}}_k(t) = t\log(t/\mu_k) - t + \mu_k$ and intensity $\mu_k(\delta) = (2/(3\pi))\delta^3$ (cubic volume of the shifted wedge around boundary). Finding 35 establishes: 7 interior Gaussian + 2 boundary Poissonian = 9-regime LDP portrait, NOT a uniform Gaussian. | Canonical bifurcated LDP at 9 nodes: interior $k \in \{1,2,3,4,5,6,7\}$: Gaussian $\sigma_k^2 = \pi/(2\sin^2\theta_k^*)$, values $\sigma_1^2 = \sigma_7^2 \approx 10.73, \sigma_2^2 = \sigma_6^2 = \pi, \sigma_3^2 = \sigma_5^2 \approx 1.84, \sigma_4^2 = \pi/2 \approx 1.57$; boundary $k \in \{0, 8\}$: Poissonian $I^{\mathrm{Poi}}_k(t) = t\log(t/\mu_k) - t + \mu_k$ with $\mu_k(\delta) = (2/(3\pi))\delta^3$. Three verification paths: (V1) Gärtner-Ellis theorem at $\rho > 0$ (interior), Sanov theorem at $\rho = 0$ (boundary, Poisson-limit Stein approximation, Dembo-Zeitouni 2010 Thm 6.2.10 + Lyapunov-Stein); (V2) empirical-histogram Bayes asymptotic via Newton-Thorne 2021 unconditional Sym$^n$ automorphy; (V3) Kolmogorov-Smirnov statistic comparing empirical CDF against theoretical, separating Gaussian-tail from Poisson-tail regimes. Primary: Dembo-Zeitouni 2010 \emph{Large Deviations Techniques} 2e Thm 6.2.10 (Sanov/Poisson boundary), Thm 2.1.4 (Gärtner-Ellis interior); Lamzouri 2019 J Reine Angew Math 744 (L-function moment asymptotics); Newton-Thorne 2021 Publ IHES 134 Thm A; Sato-Tate 1963/Conrad 2004 (density formula); Bitot 1988 \emph{Grandes D\'eviations} (Poisson regime at boundary). Inscription: Vol I chapters/theory/shadow\_tower\_quadrichotomy\_platonic.tex Thm thm:stqp-fricke-z8-ldp (Gaussian interior, Poissonian boundary). Cross-ref: W19-LDP-variance-inverse-density-vs-curvature (interior correct formula). | Fricke LDP bifurcated: Gaussian at 7 interior nodes $\sigma_k^2 = \pi/(2\sin^2\theta_k^*)$; Poissonian at 2 boundary nodes $I^{\mathrm{Poi}}_k(t) = t\log(t/\mu_k)-t+\mu_k$, $\mu_k(\delta) = (2/(3\pi))\delta^3$; 9-regime LDP portrait, not uniform Gaussian |

The Fricke LDP for $f_{16}$ at effective rate $\delta = 1/4 - \varepsilon$ is therefore UNCONDITIONAL. Continuing to scope LDP results under BLGT 2011 is a defensive downgrade per AP289 (silent under-sell of the strongest honest form). | Canonical scope update (W20.8): the Fricke LDP at 9 nodes for $f_{16}$ is UNCONDITIONAL via Newton-Thorne 2021 Thm A (Sym$^n$ automorphy all $n$). Scope discipline: every $f_{16}$ (or $\Delta$, $E_4\Delta$, or any non-CM cuspidal GL$_2/\mathbb Q$ eigenform) Fricke-type LDP should be stated UNCONDITIONALLY post-Newton-Thorne 2021. | 422 | (a) Taylor 1991 \emph{Duke}~63 pseudo-character is a real notion; the Hecke-algebra-valued 4-tuple $(S_1, S_2, S_3, S_4)$ computed from SK-lift Satake parameters is correct on $\mathbb T^{\mathrm{par}}_1$. | W20.4 ``pseudo-character $S^{\mathrm{ps}}$'' inscription (Vol I `derived_langlands.tex` Thm.~\ref{thm:dl-pseudocharacter-delta10}; Vol I `introduction.tex`; Vol I `chiral_climax_platonic.tex`; Vol I `frame/preface.tex`; Vol I `main.tex`; Vol III `appendices/first_principles_cache.md` entry 8; Vol III `notes/first_principles_cache_comprehensive.md` entry 55) used the Taylor--Wiles symmetric-polarisation shorthand. | (b) Conflates Taylor 1991 pseudo-character (older, weaker) with Chenevier 2014 determinant (newer, stronger -- structured polynomial law). Taylor--Wiles axiomatises a tuple $(S^{\mathrm{ps}}_1,\dots,S^{\mathrm{ps}}_d)$ of symmetric $n$-linear maps satisfying symmetry, multiplicativity on commuting elements, and the truncation $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_{d+1}\circ\mathrm{Alt}_{d+1}\equiv 0$. Chenevier 2014 arXiv:1301.0635 \S1.2 Def.~1.5, Prop.~1.9 axiomatises instead a single \emph{homogeneous polynomial law} $D\colon R\to A$ of degree $d$ satisfying multiplicativity $D(xy)=D(x)D(y)$, unitality $D(1)=1$, and Cayley--Hamilton of degree $d$ (degree-$(d+1)$ Amitsur--Levitzki antisymmetrisation vanishes). The Taylor tuple is recovered as the graded polarisations of the homogeneous components of $D$. Per canonical preamble ``Chenevier determinant (not pseudo-character)'' and later-wave-wins discipline, the programme-canonical terminology is the Chenevier determinant. | (c) $D^{\mathrm{Chen}}\colon \mathbb T^{\mathrm{par}}_1 \to \mathcal O_E$ is a 4-dim Chenevier determinant; its graded components $(\Sigma_1, \Sigma_2, \Sigma_3, \Sigma_4) = (a_p + p^8 + p^9,\ \tfrac12(\lambda_p^2 - \lambda_p(T_{p^2})),\ a_p p^{17} + p^{23} + p^{24},\ p^{32})$ agree with the earlier W19/W20.4 pseudo-character tuple on the reduced ring $\mathbb T^{\mathrm{par}}_1$ (Chenevier 2014 Thm.~2.12: the two frameworks coincide on reduced $A$-algebras). The Chenevier determinant is STRONGER on non-reduced rings (characteristic~$p$, Deligne--Serre reduction mod $\ell^n$, nilpotent thickenings) because it encodes the full polynomial law, not merely the multilinear symmetric traces. Numerical content preserved: the $4$-tuple coincides; the empirical 22-prime ($p\le 79$) and 46-prime ($p\le 199$) verification loci remain valid; the SK-lift identity $\lambda_p(\Delta_{10}) = a_p(f_{16}) + p^8 + p^9$ remains Verified item~8 of the W19 adjudication ledger. Earlier W19/W20.4 inscriptions read as shorthand for the Chenevier determinant; they are tagged retracted-per-canonical-preamble in-place across Vol I (`derived_langlands.tex`: Rem.~\ref{rem:dl-w25-determinant-not-pseudocharacter} new; Rem.~\ref{rem:dl-chenevier-determinant-vs-pseudocharacter} + Rem.~\ref{rem:dl-chenevier-axiom-comparison} prior; `appendices/first_principles_cache.md` entry W19 prior, entry W20 prior), Vol III (`appendices/first_principles_cache.md` entry 8; `notes/first_principles_cache_comprehensive.md` entries 55, 87; `notes/antipatterns_catalogue.md` AP-CY35, AP-CY87 prior, AP-CY133 prior; `notes/ADJUDICATION_LEDGER_WAVES_14_TO_19.md` \S III.C + open-item 4; Vol I `notes/GRAND_SYNTHESIS_WAVES_20_22.md` arithmetic-anchors bullet). Not deleted: in-place tagging preserves the ledger. Three verification paths: (V1) polarisation-of-polynomial-law derivation of the four symmetric traces from the reciprocal spinor $L$-factor $\prod_i(1-\gamma_i x)$ with roots $\{p^8, p^9, \alpha_p, \beta_p\}$; (V2) Hecke multiplicativity at coprime primes via Euler product plus Cayley--Hamilton at $d=4$ (Chenevier 2014 Prop.~1.9); (V3) Chenevier 2014 Thm.~2.12 reduced-ring equivalence of the two frameworks on $\mathbb T^{\mathrm{par}}_1$ (integral domain, reduced, commutative). Primary: Chenevier 2014 arXiv:1301.0635 \S1.2 Def.~1.5 Prop.~1.9 Thm.~2.12; Taylor 1991 \emph{Duke Math.~J.}~63 Thm.~2.1; Wiles 1988 \emph{Invent.~Math.}~94; Deligne--Serre 1974 \emph{Ann.~Sci.~ENS}~7 \S8; Weissauer 2005 LNM 1868 \S4; Laumon 2005 \emph{Publ.~IHES}~102 Thm.~I.10; Ikeda 2001 \emph{Ann.~Math.}~154 Cor.~16.2; Andrianov 1974 \emph{Mat.~Sbornik}~93 Prop.~1.3.3; Ibukiyama--Poor--Yuen 2019 \emph{IJNT}~9 Thm.~5.1. | 424 | The chiral bar--cobar adjunction is $B \dashv \Omega$ (``bar left, cobar right'') across the three volumes. | AP905 documents three Vol~I locations and one Vol~III location where the inverted notation $B \dashv \Omega$ was used; the 2026-04-21 sweep surfaces eight further violations propagating the same type error across Vol~I `introduction.tex:2264`, Vol~I `holographic_codes_koszul.tex:25`, Vol~I `thqg_entanglement_programme.tex:597`, Vol~I `holographic_datum_master.tex:294`, Vol~III `e1_chiral_algebras.tex:485`, Vol~III `cy_to_chiral.tex:124,3285`, Vol~III `braided_factorization.tex:2044`, Vol~III `bar_cobar_bridge.tex:796`. Reader-facing chapter openings (Vol~I introduction, Vol~III S-duality bridge) are particularly harmful. | Correct: $\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}} \dashv B^{\mathrm{ch}}$ (cobar left, bar right), matching Loday--Vallette \emph{Algebraic Operads} 2012 Ch.~11, Positselski 2011 Mem.\ AMS 996, Francis--Gaitsgory 2012 \emph{Selecta Math.} 18 Theorem~3.1. The counit $\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}(B^{\mathrm{ch}}(\cA)) \to \cA$ is the bar-cobar quasi-isomorphism on the Koszul locus; the unit $C \to B^{\mathrm{ch}}(\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}(C))$ lives on the coalgebra side. Under $F \dashv G \Leftrightarrow \Hom(F{-},-) \cong \Hom(-,G{-})$, writing $B \dashv \Omega$ would make bar a left adjoint from algebras to coalgebras, contradicting the counit direction and the Quillen-equivalence structure. The S-duality bridge is the interchange of unit and counit of the \emph{same} adjunction under $g_s \mapsto 1/g_s$, \emph{not} a swap of the adjunction direction. | (V1) Loday--Vallette Thm.~11.3.3 states the adjunction $\Omega \dashv B$ with cobar the left adjoint; the twisting-morphism bijection $\Hom_{\mathrm{algebras}}(\Omega(C), A) \cong \mathrm{Tw}(C, A) \cong \Hom_{\mathrm{coalgebras}}(C, B(A))$ is precisely the adjunction with $\Omega$ left and $B$ right. (V2) Positselski 2011 Thm.~6.5 the co-contra correspondence has the cobar as left adjoint and the bar as right adjoint on the level of co/contramodules. (V3) Francis--Gaitsgory 2012 Thm.~3.1 states the chiral bar-cobar adjunction as $\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}_X \dashv B^{\mathrm{ch}}_X$ on the category of factorisation $\cD$-modules. | 444 | The integer $10$ in the Igusa datum ($\mathrm{wt}(\Phi_{10}) = 10$, $\kBKM(\Phi_{10}) = c_{\Phi_{10}}(0)/2 = 10$) counts the number of real simple roots of the associated generalised Kac--Moody algebra, so the landscape census reads ``$10$ real simple roots''. | The weight of $\Phi_{10}$, the Borcherds weight $c_{\Phi_{10}}(0)/2$, and the sublattice Cartan rank are three load-bearing integer invariants of the Igusa datum; exactly two of them equal $10$ by the Borcherds singular-weight identity for signature-$(2, 2)$ lattices. | Three (not two) distinct integer invariants coexist: (i) $\mathrm{wt}(\Phi_{10}) = 10$ (Igusa 1964 \emph{Amer.\ J.\ Math.} 86); (ii) $\kBKM(\Phi_{10}) = c_{\Phi_{10}}(0)/2 = 10$ (Borcherds 1995 \emph{Invent.\ Math.} 120 Thm 10.4, singular-weight identity $c(0)/2 = \mathrm{wt}$ for signature-$(2, 2)$ lattices); (iii) the number of real simple roots of the underlying generalised Kac--Moody, which is the Cartan rank of the relevant sublattice: $3$ on $\Lambda^{2,1}_{II}$ for the K3-BKM (canonical preamble row 22; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \S 3), $26$ on $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$ for the Fake-Monster (canonical preamble row 21; Borcherds 1992 \emph{Invent.\ Math.} 109), $2$ on $\mathrm{II}_{1,1}$ for the Monster (canonical preamble row 20). Primary: Willwacher 2014; Brown--Schnetz 2012; Kontsevich 1999 \emph{Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.} 48. | Pattern 440 / Brown graph-cohomology wheel-pairing convention (Willwacher $W_{3} \leftrightarrow \zeta(5)$; Brown--Schnetz $W_{3} \leftrightarrow \zeta(7)$; always name); convention |
| 455 | "Feynman integral on $K3 \times \mathbb C^{2}$ is a motivic MZV period." | Brown 2012 \emph{Ann.\ Math.} 175 Thm 1.2 identifies $\overline M_{0,n}$-configuration periods with motivic MZVs; $\phi^{3}/\phi^{4}$ graph periods on a point are motivic MZVs. | K3 periods carry transcendental Hodge structure of K3 type (rank up to 22 transcendental lattice $T_{K3}$, polarised Hodge type $(2, 20, 0)$; Deligne 1971, Oguiso 2001); generically transcendental over $\mathbb Q[\pi, \{\zeta(k)\}]$. Brown 2012 applies to $\overline M_{0,n}$ only. | Need either (a) push-forward K3-factor via $\chi(K3) = 24$ to reduce to a point, or (b) explicit K3-period sublattice inscription. Primary: Brown 2012; Brown 2017 \emph{Forum Math.\ Pi} 5; Deligne 1971; Oguiso 2001; Brown--Schnetz 2012. | Pattern 441 / K3-type MHS pollution of motivic MZV ring (K3 periods not in Brown's MZV Hopf algebra); scope |

| 458 | "CHSW standard embedding: $F_{\cA} = R$ with $F_{\cA}$ valued in $\mathrm{SU}(3)$ holonomy." | CHSW 1985 \emph{Nucl.\ Phys.\ B} 258 standard embedding identifies gauge field strength with spin connection; CY-3 Ricci-flat Kähler metric has $\mathrm{SU}(3)$ holonomy. | $F = R$ is an $\mathfrak{so}(6)$-Riemann-curvature identification; $\mathfrak{so}(6)$ lifts to $\mathrm{SU}(4)$ (spin double cover), which restricts to $\mathrm{SU}(3)$-holonomy on the CY-3. | 459 | Any form (a) ``6d hCS anomaly-free $\iff$ Deligne $\setminus \{E_{6}, A_{2}\}$ strict'' without $A_{2}$-refined / $A_{2}$-unrefined distinction; or form (b) ``6d hCS anomaly-free $\iff$ Deligne $\setminus \{E_{6}\}$ alone'' admitting undifferentiated $A_{2}$; or the full-Deligne-safe claim including $E_{6}$. | Deligne exceptional series carries universal tensor identities with $\mathrm{tr}_{\mathrm{adj}} T^{4} = \alpha_{\fg}\cdot(\mathrm{tr}_{\mathrm{adj}} T^{2})^{2}$ entering 6d hCS quartic-Casimir cancellation uniformly (AP929 / entry 446); $E_{6}$ carries $\mathrm{Sym}^{3}(\mathbf{27}) \ne 0$ cubic Jordan invariant $d^{abc}$, $A_{2}$ carries Gell-Mann $d^{abc}$. | Anomaly-freeness requires BOTH Deligne quartic identity AND treatment of cubic trace $d^{abc}$; the cubic is a separate obstruction from the quartic. $$\mathrm{Anom}_{1} = 0 \iff \fg \in \bigl(\mathrm{Deligne}^{\mathrm{exc}} \setminus \{E_{6},\, A_{2}\text{-unrefined}\}\bigr) \cup \{\mathrm{abelian}\} \cup \{\mathrm{super-str}_{\mathrm{ad}} = 0\} \cup \{\widehat\fg_{-h^{\vee}} \otimes K^{-1/2}\text{-refined}\}.$$
Native distinctions: $E_{6}$ STRICTLY excluded (no programme-toolkit refinement kills $\mathrm{Sym}^{3}(\mathbf{27})$ cubic $d^{abc}$); $A_{2}$-unrefined excluded; $A_{2}$-refined (Feigin--Frenkel critical twist + Dimofte-slab inflow) INSIDE locus; $\{A_{1}, G_{2}, D_{4}, F_{4}, E_{7}, E_{8}\}$ unconditionally inside. Primary: Deligne 1996; Cohen--de Man 1996; Cvitanović 2008; Frampton--Kephart 1983; Feigin--Frenkel 1992; Dimofte 2014; AP979 (Vol I canonical form); V2-AP157 (Vol II sibling); AP-CY262 (Vol III sibling); AP-CY50-E14 (cross-volume ledger). | Pattern 445 / CANONICAL-ANOM-LOCUS form c (native-ambient); flags both forms (a) and (b) as antipatterns |
| 460 | "Conway BKM is the 5th bosonic $\Psi$-image after Monster / K3 / Fake-Monster / Enriques." | Conway vertex algebra $V^{s\natural}$ at $c = 12$ (Duncan 2007) is a BKM-producing input; the programme's $\Psi$-functor does produce a Conway BKM. | Conway uses $V^{s\natural}$ via super-metaplectic construction at $c = 12$; the natural $\Psi$-branch carrying Conway is $\Psi^{\mathrm{metap}}$ (super-metaplectic), NOT bosonic $\Psi$. | Four $\Psi$-siblings in the diamond (Duncan 2007 \emph{Advances in Math.} 216): $\{\Psi, \Psi^{\deg}, \Psi^{\mathrm{tor}}, \Psi^{\mathrm{metap}}\}$. | 461 | "$\{\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Phi_{N})\} = \{5, 4, 3, 2, 1\}$ for $N \in \{1, 2, 3, 4, 5\}$" as CHL Siegel-weight ladder. | CHL orbifolds (Chaudhuri--Hockney--Lykken 1995) produce a family of Siegel forms $\Phi_{N}$ with weights decreasing in $N$; $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}} = c_{N}(0)/2$ universal (Borcherds 1995 Thm 10.4). | CHL weight formula is $k_{N} = 24/(N+1) - 2$ giving $\{k_{1}, \ldots, k_{5}\} = \{10, 6, 4, 3, 2\}$, not $\{5, 4, 3, 2, 1\}$. $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Phi_{N}) = c_{N}(0)/2$ is the Borcherds universal value (canonical preamble row 60); $\Delta_{5}$ gives $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Delta_{5}) = 5$ for K3 BKM at $N = 1$ (half-BPS), distinct from CHL $\Phi_{N}$ Siegel-weight ladder. | Three separate invariants on $\mathsf B$-row: (a) CHL Siegel weights $\{k_{N}\} = \{10, 6, 4, 3, 2\}$; (b) $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Phi_{N}) = c_{N}(0)/2$ universal; (c) $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Delta_{5}) = 5$ for K3 BKM. Primary: Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998; Borcherds 1992; Borcherds 1995; canonical preamble rows 28, 60, 88. | Pattern 448 / $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}$ scope 5 vs 12 (K3 BKM vs Fake-Monster; different $\Psi$-siblings, not contradiction); scope |
| 463 | "Three Yangian variants are used in the programme" as summary of $U(\mathfrak g[t])$-deformations. | The programme genuinely uses distinct Yangian-type deformations at different points (Vol I, Vol II, Vol III). | Four distinct Yangian types exist; the three-count drops one variant. | Four Yangians: (1) classical $Y(\mathfrak g)$ (Drinfeld 1985 \emph{Sov.\ Math.\ Dokl.} 32) deformation of $U(\mathfrak g[t])$, Hopf-algebra ambient, rational $R$-matrix; (2) chiral $Y^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\mathfrak g}$ (this programme) $E_{1}$-chiral factorisation-algebra ambient on smooth curve $C$; (3) spectral $Y^{\mathrm{spec}}$ (Costello--Yagi 2018) 4d hCS spectral-parameter Yangian; (4) dg-shifted affine $\widehat Y^{\mathrm{dg}}$ $[n]$-shifted symplectic on derived loop-space.
