## Session antipatterns — manuscript hygiene (2026-04-22)

Fifty-five manuscript-hygiene antipatterns caught in the Vol III
2026-04-22 session and generalised to Vol I prose. Governing principle:
the manuscript is self-complete, self-coherent, self-consistent; the
current version stands for itself and only itself. No references to
previous versions, intermediate ansätze, earlier drafts, retracted
values, or drafting-history commentary. When a mathematical retraction
is genuinely informative, state the failed argument and its Gap/Flaw as
mathematics, not as drafting record.

| Pattern | Forbidden form | Canonical replacement | Mathematical reason |
|---|---|---|---|
| CGCLEAN-1 | `Wave 14 established...`, `Wave-20 calculation gives...` | `Theorem~C establishes...`, `The calculation below gives...` | Wave $N$ is an agent-swarm session label; manuscript prose states mathematics, not workflow. |
| CGCLEAN-2 | `per AP-CY56`, `avoiding AP113` | Replace AP index by the mathematical content it encodes (e.g. `with each $\kappa$ subscripted`) | AP codes index a private catalogue; they cannot be followed by the reader. |
| CGCLEAN-3 | `per FM24`, `FM42 sweep` | Inscribe the formula-mechanical content directly | FM codes index the formula-mechanical sub-catalogue; same hygiene issue as CGCLEAN-2. |
| CGCLEAN-4 | `by HZ-7 subscript discipline` | `with $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}$ named explicitly` | HZ labels index a programme-internal discipline checklist; the reader needs the checklist's output, not its name. |
| CGCLEAN-5 | `Strand S_3 resolved...` | `Theorem~C resolves...` | DNA-strand labels name agent-orchestration threads. |
| CGCLEAN-6 | `CG-rectify pass 4 established...` | `The calculation establishes...` | Pass-count labels labour, not content. |
| CGCLEAN-7 | `cache entry 175 forces $\delta^{(n)}=\lfloor n/2\rfloor+1$` | `The Yetter-Drinfeld Schauenburg bracket has weight $\lfloor n/2\rfloor+1$` | Cache indices are bookkeeping; inscribe the confusion's resolution directly. |
| CGCLEAN-8 | `Verdict: proved`, `Wave 18 spec closed`, `witnessing the adjunction` | `Theorem~B is proved:`, `\begin{proof}...\end{proof}` | Agent-pipeline state vocabulary; theorems are proved / conjectural / open, not in pipeline states. |
| CGCLEAN-9 | `the programme-canonical $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$` | `the canonical $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$` | "canonical" alone suffices; the "programme-" prefix is elevation-tag inflation. "The Borcherds programme" (as a named research programme) remains legitimate. |
| CGCLEAN-10 | `anchor T20`, `type-error registry T7` | Inscribe the underlying mathematical content | T-codes index a type-error registry; not reader-facing. |
| CGCLEAN-11 | `the narrative counterpart of Theorem~A`, `narrative arc of Chapter~5` | `Theorem~A extends as follows`, delete "narrative arc" entirely | Narrative is a property of stories; mathematics has statements, constructions, and proofs. |
| CGCLEAN-12 | `the story of $r(z)$`, `the saga of $\{b_k, B^{(2)}\}$`, `the $\kappa$-odyssey` | `The $r$-matrix $r(z)$ is characterised by...`, direct mathematical statement | Rhetorical inflation narrates the authors' experience. |
| CGCLEAN-13 | `the Platonic ideal of Theorem~D`, `Platonic-form construction` | `Theorem~D`, `the construction` | Platonic vocabulary is elevation bookkeeping (from the `chriss-ginzburg-rectify` target ideal); the object stands without the tag. Legitimate exception: Plato/*Timaeus* citation. |
| CGCLEAN-14 | `the Platonic Theorem~A` | `Theorem~A` | Same as CGCLEAN-13 applied to theorem names. |
| CGCLEAN-15 | `This chapter's function is to establish...`, `The role of this chapter is...` | Delete; open with a definition or theorem | Narrating the chapter's purpose rather than executing it; violates CG "show don't tell". |
| CGCLEAN-16 | `we now turn to`, `having established`, `let us now`, `this brings us to` | State what the next section constructs directly | Signposts replace the CG three-sentence section boundary with empty narrative. |
| CGCLEAN-17 | `in the present work`, `the author`, `our programme`, `we have argued`, `it is worth noting` | `Theorem~A establishes`, `the construction extends`, `$X=Y$ because...` | Authorial self-reference; elite mathematical writing names constructions, not authors. |
| CGCLEAN-18 | `This chapter closes the ... programme` meta-paragraphs | Delete; the last theorem speaks | Same failure mode as CGCLEAN-15 at programme scope. |
| CGCLEAN-19 | `the opening paragraphs of this preface` | Delete | Self-reference to document structure inside the document is circular. |
| CGCLEAN-20 | `Earlier in the volume`, `at earlier drafts`, `in an earlier version` | `\ref{thm:...}` citation in the current manuscript, or delete | Violates self-complete principle; the current manuscript is the only version the reader sees. |
| CGCLEAN-21 | `notably`, `crucially`, `remarkably`, `interestingly`, `importantly` | Delete the adverb; restate with load-bearing mathematics | Empty emphasis; if the importance is real, the mathematics shows it. |
| CGCLEAN-22 | `Furthermore,`, `Moreover,`, `Additionally,` as sentence openers | Begin the sentence directly | Filler conjunctions; LLM / AI-prose tells. |
| CGCLEAN-23 | `this preface's role is to...` | Delete | As CGCLEAN-15 at preface scope. |
| CGCLEAN-24 | Section-opening paragraph narrating content before stating it | Delete the narration; begin with the first theorem | The reader gets the content twice, once as narration, once as theorem. |
| CGCLEAN-25 | `in this paper`, `in this volume`, `throughout this work` as organising devices | `Theorem~X`, direct reference | Authorial-intent meta-language. |
| CGCLEAN-26 | `retracted`, `retraction`, `retracted ansatz`, `now retracted`, `the retracted value` | State the failed argument and its Gap/Flaw as mathematics, or delete | Violates self-complete principle. Exemption: `homological retraction` / `deformation retract` / `retracts onto` are topological / algebraic terms. |
| CGCLEAN-27 | `superseded`, `supersedes` | State the current identity | As CGCLEAN-26. |
| CGCLEAN-28 | `earlier draft`, `previous version`, `intermediate ansatz`, `prior derivation` | Delete; state current content | Explicit drafting-history reference. |
| CGCLEAN-29 | `previously conjectural`, `previously open`, `previously unresolved`, `previously obstructing` | `Theorem~C establishes...` | Temporal qualifier "previously"; the reader needs current status. |
| CGCLEAN-30 | `now resolved`, `now proved`, `now corrected` | `resolved`, `proved`, `corrected` | Drop the "now" temporal qualifier. |
| CGCLEAN-31 | `double-retraction`, `Three successive evaluations`, `History of the claim` | Delete; state current formulation | Retraction-of-retraction chronicle; doubly violates CGCLEAN-26. |
| CGCLEAN-32 | `drafting record`, `drafting trajectory` | Delete | Drafting metadata. |
| CGCLEAN-33 | `\ClaimStatusRetracted` on a theorem block | Delete block or rewrite with `\ClaimStatusProved` / `\ClaimStatusConjectured` | Retracted-status tag belongs in `notes/` catalogue, not reader-facing claim surface. |
| CGCLEAN-34 | `(2026-04-17)`, `(Etingof 2026-04-19)` inline | `\cite{Etingof_personal_communication}` or delete | Drafting-date metadata inline in manuscript. |
| CGCLEAN-35 | `\index{retraction!...}` | Delete the index entry | Retraction-tagged index exposes bookkeeping in published index. |
| CGCLEAN-36 | `(now retracted)`, `(retracted)`, `(now corrected)` parenthetical | Delete; restate with current formulation | Parenthetical retraction annotation. |
| CGCLEAN-37 | `as previously believed`, `as previously stated`, `as previously thought`, `as previously claimed` | Delete | Prior-belief reference. |
| CGCLEAN-38 | `originally claimed`, `the original argument` | Delete; current argument is the argument | Original-version reference. |
| CGCLEAN-39 | `pre-rectification`, `post-rectification` | Delete | Rectification-temporal divider. |
| CGCLEAN-40 | `drafting version 3`, `session 42 inscription` | Delete | Versioning tag. |
| CGCLEAN-41 | `\texttt{notes/antipatterns\_catalogue.md}` cited from prose | Migrate content to `appendices/`, cite `\ref{app:...}`, or inline the mathematics | `notes/` is internal; reader cannot access. |
| CGCLEAN-42 | `/Users/raeez/chiral-bar-cobar/...` absolute path in `.tex` | `\input{chapters/...}` relative path or `\ref{ch:...}` | Nonportable filesystem path. |
| CGCLEAN-43 | `% TODO: librarian verification`, `% FIXME`, `% XXX` | Complete the task, or remove the annotated content | Todo markers are drafting metadata. |
| CGCLEAN-44 | `% ALIAS`, `% LEGACY ALIAS`, `both keys used in prose`, `consolidate in future revision` | Consolidate to one bibkey, delete the alias, update `\cite{}` sites | Bibliography-hygiene metadata. |
| CGCLEAN-45 | `% Source: NEW CHAPTER (see notes/...)` | Delete the provenance line | Provenance comments encode drafting history. |
| CGCLEAN-46 | `\texttt{compute/lib/k3\_yangian\_wave14\_arthur\_hecke\_delta10.py}` cited from prose | Rename engine to drop `_wave14_` stem, re-cite | Wave-stem in filename propagates into published prose. |
| CGCLEAN-47 | `def wave14\_compute\_tau(...)` function name | Rename to describe computation (e.g. `compute_tau_at_prime`) | Wave-tag in function name at compute-code level. |
| CGCLEAN-48 | `\begin{warning}...\end{warning}` in prose | Delete; rewrite adjacent prose so default reading is non-confused | CG standard sharpens rather than warns. |
| CGCLEAN-49 | `do not confuse`, `don't be fooled`, `beware`, `be careful`, `we must be careful` | Delete; state the distinction as mathematics (e.g. `$X \ne Y$`) | Hedge vocabulary warns of a trap the prose lays. |
| CGCLEAN-50 | `scope-restricted to`, `scope-qualified to` (when decorative) | State the hypothesis once, cleanly, with `\hypref{...}` citation | Gratuitous scope inflation; legitimate hypothesis statements stay once, cleanly. |
| CGCLEAN-51 | `Verdict: proved`, `Verdict: open`, `Verdict: conditional` | `Conclusion:`, `\begin{proof}...\end{proof}`, `The question remains open.` | Adjudication-pipeline label. |
| CGCLEAN-52 | Chapter filenames `*_platonic.tex`, labels `ch:*-platonic`, `sec:*-platonic` | `git mv` rename; programme-wide `\ref{ch:X-platonic}` $\to$ `\ref{ch:X}` sweep | Platonic-tag migrates bookkeeping into build system identifiers; `\ref`s become load-bearing citations. |
| CGCLEAN-53 | `\label{thm:kappa-additivity-wave14}` | Rename to `\label{thm:kappa-additivity}`; cross-volume `\ref` sweep | Wave-tagged label persists across sessions as permanent identifier. |
| CGCLEAN-54 | `\index{compute module!...}`, `\index{cache!...}`, `\index{retraction!...}` | Delete the index entry | Bookkeeping-flavoured index entry exposes internal structure. |
| CGCLEAN-55 | `Five attack-heal calibrations`, `Reconstitution if the cancellation fails`, `Inversion of the programme perspective`, `History of the claim`, `Gold-standard HZ-IV disjoint verification`, `Three successive evaluations appear in the drafting record` | Inscribe the mathematical content the labour produced (e.g., enumerate the five verification paths directly) | Labour-activity inscribed as manuscript content; activity is real but belongs in `notes/`. |

**Operating rule.** Every reader-facing `.tex` inscription is swept
against CGCLEAN-1 through CGCLEAN-55 at the PostToolUse hook. A pattern
fires when its regex signature matches and none of the documented
legitimate contexts ("Borcherds programme"; "homological retraction"
/ "deformation retract" / "retracts onto"; "Platonic chord" in a music
section; Plato/Timaeus citation) applies. False positives are healed
by expanding the hook's exclusion list; true positives are healed by
the canonical replacement in the table above. Companion entries live
in `notes/antipatterns_catalogue.md` Session antipatterns section
(2026-04-22) and `notes/first_principles_cache_comprehensive.md` with
per-pattern 5-step DETECT / LOCALISE / MATH-CHECK / REPAIR / VERIFY
protocols.

## Wave 11--19 constructive synthesis append (2026-04-22)

Twelve constructive cache entries (C1--C12) inscribed below. Each entry names a load-bearing
positive structure from the Vol III Wave 11--19 synthesis, lensed into Vol I's five-theorem
core (A bar--cobar, B chiral Positselski, C derived-centre complementarity, D obstruction-tower
universality, H Hochschild concentration) and the G/L/C/M/B landscape-census archetype table.
Each entry states the structure precisely, cites primary source, and gives a Vol I-scope
detection heuristic.

| Tag | Constructive Statement (Vol I lens) | Primary Source | Detection Heuristic |
|---|---|---|---|
| C1 | **Two-stage factorisation of $\Phi$.** $\Phi_d = \mathrm{Sp}_{\Sigma_{d-1}, C} \circ \Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_d$: Stage~1 a canonical $E_d$-holomorphic factorisation algebra on the CY target; Stage~2 specialisation to a chiral algebra on curve $C$ via $\int_{\Sigma_{d-1}}$. Vol I lens: Stage~1 is the CY-side internal to the Koszul Reflection of Theorem B (chiral Positselski); the Stage-1 canonicality via Kontsevich--Tamarkin formality supplies the strict Koszul dualisation $\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_d \dashv (\Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_d)^!$ on which chiral Positselski depends. | Costello--Gwilliam \emph{Factorization Algebras in QFT} Vol 2 Ch 7; Kontsevich 1999 formality; Tamarkin 2003 \emph{Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.} 66; Vol III \texttt{chapters/theory/cy\_to\_chiral.tex} Thm \texttt{thm:phi-two-stage-factorisation}. | Invoke whenever a Vol I chiral algebra is identified as the shadow of a CY$_d$ category. The Vol I bar-cobar Theorem A reads the Stage-2 specialisation; Theorem B reads the Stage-1 canonicality. |
| C2 | **Universal positive-geometry grammar.** $Y^+(X) = H^\bullet_{\mathrm{eq}}(\mathcal{M}^+_{\mathrm{eff}}(X), \phi_W)$; $G(X) = D(Y^+(X))$ is the Drinfeld double of the positive half. Four equivariance strata (toric $T^d$ / reduced $\mathbb C^\times +\mathrm{Aut}$ / orbifold inertia / lattice-polarised period) fix the precise equivariant cohomology. Vol I lens: $Y^+(X)$ supplies the canonical presentation for G/L/C/M/B landscape archetypes whose landscape census is tabulated in \texttt{chapters/examples/landscape\_census.tex}. $D(Y^+(X))$ is the ambient Hopf-like envelope from which the Koszul-self-dual subcategory underlying Theorem B is cut out. | Schiffmann--Vasserot 2017 \emph{Publ.\ IHES} 129; Kontsevich--Soibelman 2011 arXiv:1006.2706; Maulik--Okounkov 2012 arXiv:1211.1287; Vol III \texttt{chapters/theory/positive\_geometry\_grammar.tex}. | Invoke when the five-archetype landscape census requires a uniform presentation. Each archetype sits on a fixed equivariance stratum; the stratum fixes which row of the G/L/C/M/B table applies. |
| C3 | **Universal Borcherds weight identity.** $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Phi_N) = c_N(0)/2$ for $N \in \{1, 2, 3, 4, 6\}$, eight Gritsenko--Cl\'ery forms with weights $(5, 2, 1, 1, 1/2, 1, 1/4, 0)$ and $c_N(0) \in \{10, 4, 2, 2, 1, 2, 1/2, 0\}$. Vol I lens: the landscape census uses subscripted $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}$ with Borcherds 1995 primary, populating the B-row of the G/L/C/M/B + B landmark table with $\kappa + \kappa^! = 8$ at $N = 1$. Every bare $\kappa$ in Vol I prose is AP5 / AP113 violation. | Borcherds 1995 \emph{Invent.\ Math.} 120; Gritsenko 1999 \emph{Abh.\ Math.\ Sem.\ Hamburg} 69; Gritsenko--Cl\'ery 2011; Lorgat 2020 (explicit Borcherds lift); Vol III \texttt{chapters/examples/cy\_d\_kappa\_stratification.tex} Thm \texttt{thm:borcherds-weight-kappa-BKM-universal}. | Invoke whenever $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}$ enters the Vol I landscape-census tabulation. Always cite the $\Phi_N$-denominator convention (AP5 / canonical preamble row). |
| C4 | **Three-factor universal trace identity.** $\mathrm{tr}_{\mathrm{ghost}}(Q_{\mathrm{BRST}}^2) = \mathrm{tr}_{\mathrm{Pentagon}} = \omega_{\mathrm{Borcherds}} = c_N(0)/2$. Vol I lens: the ghost factor is the Vol I BRST ghost-trace, attached to the semi-infinite cohomology diagonal of the affine KM envelope at non-critical level; at $N = 1$ the common value $5$ coincides with the Vol I B-row Koszul self-duality ceiling exponent $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Phi_{10}) + \kappa^! = 8$ minus ghost shift $3$. The identity lives on the Koszul-self-dual subcategory cut out by Theorem B. | Borcherds 1995 \emph{Invent.\ Math.} 120; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \emph{Duke} 94; Vol III \texttt{chapters/theory/universal\_trace.tex} Thm \texttt{thm:three-factor-universal-trace}. | Invoke when a Vol I BRST-ghost numerical witness matches a Vol III Borcherds weight; these are not coincidences but the single universal trace on the Koszul-self-dual subcategory. |
| C5 | **$6$D holomorphic Chern--Simons as $E_3$-algebra at level 3.** $\mathrm{Obs}^{\mathrm{cl}}_{\mathrm{hCS}_6} \in E_3$-alg$(\mathrm{Ch}(\mathrm{Dolb}))$; BV anomaly vanishes on $\mathbb C^3$ and on $K3 \times E$. Non-abelian 5D hCS on $\mathbb R \times \mathbb C^2$ quantises to the Yangian VOA $Y^{\mathrm{VOA}}(\mathfrak g)$ to all orders in $\hbar$ for simply-laced $\mathfrak g$. Vol I lens: 5D/6D hCS appears in the Vol I BV--BRST chapters as the chain-level source of the Yangian envelope; the Stage-1 factorisation algebra of C1 is implemented explicitly by hCS at $d = 3$. | Costello 2013 arXiv:1303.2632; Costello--Gaiotto 2021 arXiv:2108.01379; Costello--Li 2016 arXiv:1605.09930; Vol III \texttt{chapters/theory/six\_d\_hcs.tex}. | Invoke whenever a Vol I Yangian construction references BV-quantised hCS. The all-orders result for simply-laced $\mathfrak g$ is load-bearing for the Vol I L-row affine KM landscape. |
| C6 | **Three-tier hierarchy on the seven faces of $r_{\mathrm{CY}}$.** (i) CY-datum intrinsics; (ii) Stage-1 invariants; (iii) $(\Sigma_{d-1}, C)$-specialisations. MO $R$-matrix $R^{\mathrm{MO}}(u) = \mathrm{Res}_{u = u_\star} \phi^+_{\mathrm{UV}}(u)$ is Tier-(iii). Vol I lens: the tier-split organises the Vol I landscape census — intrinsic datum, Stage-1 factorisation invariant, specialised curve output — along the same three tiers; the Theorem D obstruction-tower universality index $r_{\max}(A)$ is a Tier-(iii) specialisation invariant. | Maulik--Okounkov 2012 arXiv:1211.1287; Kontsevich--Soibelman 2008/2011; Costello--Gwilliam \emph{FA} Vol 2; Vol III \texttt{chapters/theory/seven\_faces.tex}. | Invoke when the Vol I landscape census or Theorem D tower needs a tier-discipline. ``Spectral parameter'' is tier-(iii); ``CY structure'' is tier-(i); confusing the two silently shifts the ambient of a Theorem-D bound. |
| C7 | **Dimensional sibling catalogue.** Three Borcherds automorphic BKMs: (a) Borcherds Monster at $d = 3$, Cartan rank 26, $\Phi_{12}$; (b) Igusa cusp form BKM at $d = 3$, Cartan rank 3, $\Phi_{10} = \Delta_5^2$; (c) Fake Monster at $d = 5$, Cartan rank 26, $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$. Three dimensionally stratified BKMs with three distinct Cartans; no subalgebra inclusions. Vol I lens: Vol I's Monster-related chapters belong to the $d = 3$ Borcherds Monster slot; the B-row of the landscape census populates with the $d = 3$ Igusa BKM via $\Phi_{10}$. The $d = 5$ Fake Monster is a Vol II concern (top-form at $d = 5$). | Borcherds 1990, 1992, 1995 \emph{Invent.\ Math.} 109--120; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \emph{Duke} 94; SPLAG Ch.\ 24; Vol III \texttt{chapters/examples/dimensional\_siblings.tex}. | Invoke whenever Vol I prose names ``Monster / K3-BKM / Fake Monster'' in one paragraph. Always fix the $d$-index; rank 26 vs 3 vs 26 $\Rightarrow$ no inclusions. |
| C8 | **Serre-equivariant quasi-NCCR for $K3 \times E$.** No global NCCR exists on $K3 \times E$ (five BKR-style obstructions: $\omega$ not reflexive-tilting; derived McKay requires finite $\mathrm{Aut}$; HPD self-dual incompatible with product polarisation; Mukai vanishing fails off $K3$ factor; no global CY-3 symmetric obstruction theory). A Serre-equivariant quasi-NCCR substitutes: locally-defined tilting object equivariant under $\mathbb S = [3]$, glued via factorisation pushforward. Vol I lens: relevant to Vol I insofar as the $K3 \times E$ chiral bialgebra $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ is the B-row landmark; the quasi-NCCR is the technical architecture for the Vol III Čech descent that feeds the Vol I B-row. | Van den Bergh 2004 \emph{Duke} 122; Bridgeland--King--Reid 2001 \emph{J.\ AMS} 14; Szendr\H{o}i 2008 \emph{Sel.\ Math.} 14; Vol III \texttt{chapters/examples/k3\_times\_e\_quasi\_nccr.tex}. | Invoke if a Vol I reader asks why the usual NCCR machinery does not globally apply to the B-row landmark $K3 \times E$ host. |
| C9 | **Gaiotto curve correction.** $N = 1$ CHL class-$\mathcal S$ theory: $\mathcal T[A_1, \Sigma_{0, 24}]$ with 24 maximal regular $\mathfrak{su}(2)$ punctures on genus-0. Origin: 24 $I_1$ fibres of $K3 \times T^2$. Anomaly formula $c_{4d} = 107/6$ (all-max-regular corrected), $c_{2d} = -214$. Vol I lens: Vol I's class-$\mathcal S$-adjacent chapters (when invoking class-$\mathcal S$ for Vol I landscape row content) must use $\Sigma_{0, 24}$, not a compact genus-2 curve; the correction propagates to any Vol I citation of the $c_{4d}$ value. | Chacaltana--Distler 2010 arXiv:1008.5203; BLPR 2015 \emph{CMP} 336 eq.\ 2.27; Sen 1995 \emph{Nucl.\ Phys.\ B} 450; Vol III \texttt{chapters/examples/gaiotto\_n1\_chl.tex}. | Invoke whenever a Vol I class-$\mathcal S$ Riemann surface is identified as the bridge to a Borcherds automorphic form. The compact genus-2 identification is retracted. |
| C10 | **Heisenberg--Mukai $\eta^{-48}$ identity.** For $K3 \times E$ the elliptic-genus-like Fourier coefficient identity is $\eta^{-48}$-based: sequence $(1, 48, 1176, 19456, \dots) = $ q-expansion of $\eta^{-48}$ to all orders. Origin: 48-dim K3 Heisenberg twist via Mukai's cohomology isometry, $c_+(\mathrm{Mukai}) \cdot c_+(\mathrm{Heis}_{K3}) = 4 \cdot 12 = 48$. Vol I lens: any Vol I Fourier-coefficient match against $(1, 48, 1176, 19456)$ must be read through Heisenberg--Mukai, not Virasoro minimal model; the Vol I M-row Virasoro landscape is a different ambient. | Mukai 1987 \emph{Nagoya Math.\ J.} 108; Borcherds 1992 \emph{Invent.\ Math.} 109; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \emph{Duke} 94; Vol III \texttt{chapters/examples/heisenberg\_mukai.tex}. | Invoke when the character sequence $(1, 48, 1176, 19456, \dots)$ appears in Vol I analysis. Heisenberg--Mukai, not Virasoro. |
| C11 | **$V_{24}$ as iterated DS reduction.** $V_{24} = H^0_{\mathrm{DS}}(L_{-2 + 1/22}(\mathfrak{sl}_2)^{\otimes 22})$. Vol I lens: $V_{24}$ appears in Vol I landscape examples of moonshine-adjacent VOAs; the iterated-DS presentation links its central charge $c = 24$ to the transverse K3 SCFT rank $22$ via admissible-level Drinfeld--Sokolov. The 22 copies realise $22 = b_2(K3) - 2 = \mathrm{rk}(\mathrm{II}_{2,18})$. | Arakawa--Frenkel--Kazhdan 2020; Arakawa 2015 \emph{JRAM} 711; Kac--Roan--Wakimoto 2003 \emph{CMP} 241; Frenkel--Ben-Zvi 2004 Ch.\ 15; Vol III \texttt{chapters/examples/v24\_ds\_reduction.tex}. | Invoke whenever $V_{24}$ appears in a Vol I landscape example. The Vol I DS-reduction apparatus (principal $\mathcal W$-algebras) extends through admissible-level DS to $V_{24}$. |
| C12 | **$F_3$ Feingold--Frenkel real-root subalgebra.** Rank-3 Feingold--Frenkel hyperbolic Kac--Moody $F_3$ is the real-root subalgebra of $\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$, Cartan matrix $2\delta_{ij} - 2$; appears in $\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}$ via $R$-matrix wall-crossing at the three $\mathbb Z/2$ walls of the $K3$ K\"ahler moduli space. Vol I lens: relevant to Vol I insofar as the B-row landmark $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ carries $F_3$ as its real-root Vol I chiral-side shadow; imaginary-root completion requires Feigin--Frenkel screening operators, Vol I's standard screening-operator mechanism. | Feingold--Frenkel 1983 \emph{Math.\ Ann.} 263; Feigin--Frenkel 1990 \emph{Phys.\ Lett.\ B} 246; Feigin--Frenkel 1992 \emph{CMP} 128; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \emph{Duke} 94; Vol III \texttt{chapters/examples/feingold\_frenkel\_f3.tex}. | Invoke when the Cartan matrix $2\delta_{ij} - 2$ appears in Vol I analysis of the B-row landmark. Real-root $F_3$ is the visible part; imaginary-root screening operators are the hidden part carrying BKM multiplicities. |
| C13 | **3d gravity $= 1/\Phi_{10}$ directly; 6d hCS related by Borcherds singular theta lift, not residue.** The Dijkgraaf--Verlinde--Verlinde 1997 identification gives $Z_{\mathrm{3dQG}}^{\mathrm{AdS}_3\times K3}(Z) = 1/\Phi_{10}(Z)$ as a direct equality, not as a residue extraction. The Costello 6d hCS all-loop effective action $\bigl(\Phi_{10}(Z)/(\eta(\tau)^{24}\eta(\tau')^{24})\bigr)^{\hbar\cdot c_{K3}(Z)}$ is the Borcherds multiplicative lift of the K3 elliptic-genus generator; the 3d-gravity object emerges as the leading large-$\hbar$ saddle-point asymptotic via the singular-theta correspondence, NOT via a residue $\mathrm{Res}_{\Phi_{10}=0}$ (which is ill-typed since the residue of $c/f$ at $f=0$ is $c$, not $c/f$). Vol I lens: any Vol I Theorem-D obstruction-tower statement referencing the $K3\times T^2$ DVV identity must quote the Borcherds singular theta lift, never a self-referential residue. | Dijkgraaf--Verlinde--Verlinde 1997 \emph{Nucl.\ Phys.\ B} 484; Borcherds 1998 \emph{Invent.\ Math.} 132; Harvey--Moore 1996 \emph{Nucl.\ Phys.\ B} 463; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \emph{Duke} 94; Vol II \texttt{chapters/connections/thqg\_perturbative\_finiteness.tex} Thm \texttt{thm:hcs-all-loop-resummation}. | Invoke whenever $1/\Phi_{10}$ is derived from 6d hCS effective action. The passage is saddle-point plus singular theta, not residue. If the chapter says ``residue'', it is wrong. |
| C14 | **Both $\eta(\tau)^{24}$ and $\eta(\tau')^{24}$ are required on the Siegel period.** On the Siegel upper half space $\mathfrak H_2$ with period $Z = \begin{pmatrix}\tau & z \\ z & \tau'\end{pmatrix}$, the Igusa cusp form $\Phi_{10}(Z)$ has bimodular weight $(12, 12)$ under $\mathrm{Sp}_4(\mathbb Z)$. The diagonal restriction factors as $\Phi_{10}(Z)\vert_{z = 0} = z^2 \cdot \eta(\tau)^{24} \cdot \eta(\tau')^{24} \cdot \mathcal J(\tau, \tau')$ (Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998, Dijkgraaf--Verlinde--Verlinde 1997). The bimodular-weight-zero object on $\mathfrak H_2 \setminus \{z = 0\}$ is $\Phi_{10}(Z)/(\eta(\tau)^{24}\eta(\tau')^{24})$; a single $\eta^{24}$ leaves a residual weight $(0, 12)$ or $(12, 0)$ and is NOT modular-invariant under the full $\mathrm{Sp}_4(\mathbb Z)$. Vol I lens: any Vol I Heegner-Chern-class witness (B-row landmark) quoting the Costello 6d hCS effective action on $K3 \times T^2$ must use the two-$\eta^{24}$ denominator; single-$\eta^{24}$ shorthands of the Hall-pentagon / Chern-class character belong to a different context and should not be conflated with the Siegel bimodular-weight cancellation. | Dijkgraaf--Verlinde--Verlinde 1997 \emph{Nucl.\ Phys.\ B} 484 \S4; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \emph{Duke} 94 Thm 2.1; Eichler--Zagier 1985 \S9; Vol II \texttt{chapters/connections/thqg\_perturbative\_finiteness.tex} equation \texttt{eq:hcs-all-loop-resummation}. | Invoke whenever a putative bimodular-weight-zero object on $\mathfrak H_2$ divides by only one $\eta^{24}$. Check the Siegel period convention; the two modular parameters $\tau, \tau'$ each carry weight 12 on $\Phi_{10}$ and each needs its own $\eta^{24}$ denominator. |
| C15 | **6d hCS on $\C^3$: $E_6$ at Dolbeault level, reducing to $E_3$ via $\Omega^{0,\bullet}(\C)\simeq\C$; not three commuting $E_1$'s.** The translation-equivariant factorisation algebra $\Fobs^q_{\mathrm{hCS}}$ on $X = \C^3 = \R^6$ carries an $E_6$-structure at the level of the full Dolbeault complex (Lurie $\mathrm{HA}.5.5.4.10$ applied to $\R^6$). Passage to $\bar\partial$-cohomology, via the Costello--Gwilliam holomorphic-twist construction (Vol 2, Ch.~5, Thm 5.1), contracts each holomorphic factor $\Omega^{0,\bullet}(\C)\simeq\C$, reducing the topological operad from $E_6$ to $E_3$. Dunn additivity $E_3 = E_1 \otimes_D E_1 \otimes_D E_1$ applies at the level of $\bar\partial$-cohomology, with one $E_1$-factor per holomorphic coordinate $z_1, z_2, z_3$ AFTER the Dolbeault--Koszul reduction — NOT as three commuting $E_1$'s on the three underlying $\C$'s (each $\C$ is two real dimensions, carrying $E_2$-structure topologically). Vol I lens: Vol I's $E_n$-chiral discipline (Pattern 276, notion A/B/C/D/E) must respect this reduction: the $E_3$ on hCS is a cohomological-level statement, and Dunn additivity at that level is the mechanism, not a kinematic product of three $E_1$'s. | Costello--Gwilliam \emph{Factorization Algebras in QFT} Vol 2 Ch 5, \S5.2.1, Thm 5.1; Lurie \emph{Higher Algebra} 5.5.4.10; Costello 2013 arXiv:1303.2632; Costello--Gaiotto 2021 arXiv:2108.01379; Vol II \texttt{chapters/connections/six\_d\_hcs\_e3\_chiral\_avatar\_platonic.tex} Thm \texttt{thm:hcs-e3-from-translation}. | Invoke when Dunn additivity is cited for 6d hCS on $\C^3$. If the proof-sketch says "three $E_1$'s from three $\C$'s" without naming Dolbeault--Koszul reduction, restore the $E_6 \rightsquigarrow E_3$ cohomological mechanism. |

## Wave-12 cross-programme anchor rows (2026-04-22, W12A--W12L; Vol I AP954--AP965 companions; Pattern 465--476 cache back-anchor)

Twelve confusion-pattern rows supplementing C1--C15 with the Vol III wave-12 (2026-04-22) cross-programme propagation. Each row pairs with the Vol I AP954--AP965 companion in `notes/antipatterns_catalogue.md` and the cache companion in `notes/first_principles_cache_comprehensive.md` Pattern 465--476. These rows restore the "wrong claim / ghost theorem / precise error / correct relationship / type" confusion-pattern format of entries 263--278 at the cross-programme lane-discipline scope; C1--C15 are constructive entries, W12A--W12L are confusion-pattern entries.

| # | Wrong Claim | Ghost Theorem | Precise Error | Correct Relationship | Type |
|---|-------------|---------------|---------------|----------------------|------|
| W12A | Vol I prose writes ``$\Phi: \mathrm{CY}_d \to \mathrm{ChirAlg}$ is a functor'' without specifying chain-level vs $(\infty,1)$-categorical lane. | Chain-level object-level $\Phi$ and $(\infty,1)$-categorical functor lift are both load-bearing at their precise scope; the chain-level statement is auditable against explicit complexes, the $(\infty,1)$-categorical statement against Lurie HA + Francis 2013. | Merges two lanes that occupy different epistemic registers. Morphism-preservation is a separate theorem from object-level assignment; conflating them loses precision at the Beilinson-dictum audit site. | Pattern 273 is a scope declaration, not a hierarchy: state the chain-level object-level $\Phi$ on the Stage-2 curve $C$, and flag any $(\infty,1)$-categorical-functor lift as conjectural (Vol II AP-V2-41 / V2-AP144). Both shadows are real; neither subsumes the other. | chain-level vs $(\infty,1)$-functor scope (AP954, Pattern 465) |
| W12B | Vol I prose writes bare $\kappa$ at any CY-to-chiral interface. | Four $\kappa_\bullet$ invariants are genuinely distinct: $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$, $\kappa_{\mathrm{cat}} = \chi(\mathcal O_X)$, $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Phi_N) = c_N(0)/2$, $\kappa_{\mathrm{fiber}}$. | Bare $\kappa$ collapses four distinct invariants; at $K3 \times E$ the total-space $\kappa_{\mathrm{cat}} = 0$, fibre $\kappa_{\mathrm{fiber}}(K3) = 2$; AP5 dual-indexing adds a second layer ($\Phi_{10}$ vs $\Phi_{12}$). | Every Vol I $\kappa$ in reader-facing prose carries its subscript from first keystroke; Theorem C complementarity $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}} + \kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^! \in \{0, 8, 13, 98/3, 250/3\}$; the B-row $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}(\Delta_5) = 5$. | $\kappa$-subscript discipline (AP955, Pattern 466) |
| W12C | Vol I writes ``$\mathrm{CoHA}(\mathbb C^3) = \mathcal W_{1 + \infty}$'' as an isomorphism. | CoHA is the positive half of the affine Yangian: $\mathrm{CoHA}(\mathbb C^3) = Y^+(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_1)$ (Schiffmann--Vasserot); $\mathcal W_{1 + \infty}$ arises through the evaluation slice. | Collapses the evaluation chain, drops the spectral parameter $\lambda$, drops Miki $S_3$-triality structure on $Y^+$. | $\mathrm{CoHA}(\mathbb C^3) = Y^+$; image under evaluation chain $Y^+ \hookrightarrow Y \xrightarrow{\mathrm{ev}_\lambda} \mathrm{End}(\mathcal W_{1 + \infty}[\lambda])$; extension ladder $Y^+ \to \mathcal W_\infty[c] \to \mathcal W_{1 + \infty}$ with tensor decomposition $\mathcal W_{1 + \infty} = \mathcal W_\infty[c] \otimes \mathcal H$. | CoHA / evaluation chain (AP956, Pattern 467) |
| W12D | Vol I statement ``$A$ is an $E_2$-chiral algebra at $d \ge 3$'' for $A$ the Stage-2 algebra output. | At $d \ge 3$ the $E_2$-braided structure is real, and $A$ does sit in a structured target. | Conflates $A$ with $\mathcal Z(\mathrm{Rep}(A))$; confuses braiding-on-module-centre with braiding-on-algebra. $A$ at $d \ge 3$ is $E_1$. | At $d \ge 3$: $A$ is $E_1$; $E_2$-structure lives on $\mathcal Z(\mathrm{Rep}(A))$, the Drinfeld centre of the module category (a different categorical object with its own derived complex). | $E_n$-on-wrong-object (AP957, Pattern 468) |
| W12E | Vol I cites Vol III's $\Phi_d$ output as universally $E_2$-chiral (or $E_1$-chiral) without naming $d$. | PTVV shifted-symplectic structure controls $E_n^{\mathrm{cl}}$; the output is $d$-dependent. | Silently fixes PTVV shift to one value, collapsing the $d$-dependent hierarchy. | PTVV table: $(d, \mathrm{shift}, E_n^{\mathrm{cl}}) \in \{(2, -2, E_2), (3, -1, E_1), (4, 0, E_0), (5, +1, E_5\text{-Poisson})\}$. Every Vol I reference names the triple. | PTVV shift discipline (AP958, Pattern 469) |
| W12F | Vol I cites ``canonical chiral algebra on $X$'' invoking only Costello--Li 2016 OR only Kontsevich--Tamarkin formality. | The canonical chiral algebra rests on both; each source is real and correctly named. | One-leg citation collapses the conjunction: Costello--Li at holomorphic locality; Kontsevich--Tamarkin at Hochschild formality. Each alone is insufficient. | Every citation of ``canonical chiral algebra'' names both Costello--Li 2016 (arXiv:1605.09439) AND Kontsevich--Tamarkin formality (Kontsevich 2003, Tamarkin 2003, both \emph{Lett Math Phys} 66). | citation-conjunction discipline (AP959, Pattern 470) |
| W12G | Vol I prose writes ``the shadow tower gives the Gaudin generators'', ``the bar construction gives the Koszul dual'', ``$\Phi$ gives a chiral algebra''. | Each construction does produce the second object via a concrete mechanism; the arrow exists. | The verb ``gives'' hides whether the operation is a chain-level map, a functor, a restriction, an inclusion, or a specialisation. | Every ``gives'' following a named construction is replaced by the specific arrow (``the shadow-tower depth-stratification map'', ``the cobar $\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}$ adjoint'', ``the chain-level morphism $\Phi$ assigns'', etc.) or flagged. | narration / arrow-naming discipline (AP960, Pattern 471) |
| W12H | Vol I states ``the Borcherds-product denominator equals the bar Euler characteristic'' with a single-sided citation. | The identity is real at the $K3 \times E + \Phi_{10}$ landmark (Borcherds 1995 + Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998). | CY-A without Theorem A produces a Hodge-supertrace identity without the bar-Euler reading; Theorem A without CY-A produces an Euler identity without a CY-side origin. | Every denominator-$=$-bar-Euler citation names BOTH CY-A$_d$ AND Vol I Theorem A within 20 lines. At $d = 3$: AP-CY49 + Vol I Theorem A jointly anchor the identity. | two-anchor citation discipline (AP961, Pattern 472) |
| W12I | Vol I writes ``class $\mathsf M$ $E_3$-bar is $6^g$-dimensional'' without ``at cohomology''. | Class $\mathsf M$ does carry finite $6^g$ cohomology at genus $g$ (per-handle tricomplex $P_{E_4}(t) = 3t + 3t^2$, $d_4$ collapse). | Scope confusion between chain-level complex (infinite) and cohomology (finite $6^g$ via $d_4$ collapse in the $E_4$ page). | Every class-$\mathsf M$ $6^g$ claim carries ``at cohomology'' qualifier. Chain-level: infinite. Cohomology: $6^g$, with per-handle tricomplex $P_{E_4}(t) = 3t + 3t^2$, $6 = 2 \cdot 3$ per handle. | chain-level vs cohomological scope (AP962, Pattern 473) |
| W12J | Vol I cites Vol III's CY-A$_3$ result as a full equivalence of CY$_3$ category with chiral-algebra output. | $\Phi_d = \mathrm{Sp}^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\Sigma_{d-1}, C} \circ \Phi^{\mathrm{FA}}_d$ factorisation is well-defined at $d = 3$; the Stage-1 output is $E_1$-rigid. | Conflates existence-and-rigidity (proved at chain-level on explicit factorisation-algebra complex) with $(\infty,1)$-categorical equivalence (frontier, Vol II AP-V2-41 / V2-AP144). | CY-A$_3$ reads as existence-plus-$E_1$-rigidity at the factorisation-algebra level; equivalence as $(\infty,1)$-categorical functor is frontier, Vol II AP-V2-41 / V2-AP144. | existence/rigidity vs equivalence scope (AP963, Pattern 474) |
| W12K | Vol I writes $\int_{\Sigma_2} E_3 \simeq E_1$ without naming whether $\Sigma_2$ is 2-real-dimensional or 1-complex-dimensional. | Dunn--Lurie additivity $\int_{\Sigma_2} E_3 \simeq E_1$ is a real theorem at 2-real-dimensional $\Sigma_2$. | Silent dimension-convention switch produces shift errors in Stage-2 specialisation. | Name ``2-real-dimensional $\Sigma_2$'' for Dunn--Lurie; for complex-dimension pushforwards name $\Sigma_{d-1}$ over complex dimension and cite MIXED-operation holomorphic pushforward (AP-V2-25). Vol II AP-V2-36 / V2-AP139 is primary. | Dunn--Lurie real-vs-complex (AP964, Pattern 475) |
| W12L | Vol I cites the three-sector bar complex $(B_{E_1}, B_{E_2}, B_{E_\infty})$ as an equivalence of $(\infty,1)$-categories. | Chain-level filtered quasi-isomorphism $B_{E_1} A \twoheadrightarrow B_{E_2} A \twoheadrightarrow B_{E_\infty} A$ is a genuine theorem with explicit KT + Costello--Li inputs. | Conflates chain-level filtered equivalence (theorem) with $(\infty,1)$-categorical-functor lift (frontier, Vol II AP-V2-41 / V2-AP144). | Read as chain-level filtered equivalence with explicit Kontsevich--Tamarkin + Costello--Li inputs; $(\infty,1)$-functor claim flagged as conjectural. | three-sector bar filtered frontier (AP965, Pattern 476) |

## Wave-15 cross-programme anchor rows (2026-04-22, W15A--W15D; Vol I AP985--AP988 companions; Pattern 477--480 cache back-anchor; propagated from Vol III AP-CY262, 263, 266, 268)

Four confusion-pattern rows propagated from the Vol III wave-15 (2026-04-22) cross-volume audit of 6d/5d holomorphic Chern--Simons anomaly-locus structure, PTVV shift discipline, critical-level rigidity, and the chiral Booth--Lazarev obstruction tower. Each row pairs with the Vol I AP985--AP988 companion in `notes/antipatterns_catalogue.md` and carries a Pattern 477--480 cache back-anchor. These rows continue the "wrong claim / ghost theorem / precise error / correct relationship / type" confusion-pattern format of W12A--W12L at the cross-programme lane-discipline scope. Vol III entries AP-CY264, AP-CY265, AP-CY267 are Vol III-specific (K3 Yangian internal combinatorics) and are NOT propagated to Vol I.

| # | Wrong Claim | Ghost Theorem | Precise Error | Correct Relationship | Type |
|---|-------------|---------------|---------------|----------------------|------|
| W15A | Vol I prose writes ``hCS$_6(\fg)$ anomaly is $C_2(\fg) = 2h^\vee$'' (quadratic Casimir). | The 1-loop BV anomaly of 6d hCS on a CY$_3$ target is a genuine cocycle-level obstruction controlled by a Lie-algebraic invariant of $\fg$. | Quadratic Casimir $C_2 = 2h^\vee$ is a scheme-dependent wave-function coefficient absorbed into a BV-trivial counter-term $\int \mathrm{tr}(A \partial A)$ via field redefinition; the TRUE cocycle-level anomaly is the cubic symmetric invariant $d^{abc}(\fg) = \mathrm{tr}(t^{(a}\{t^b, t^{c)}\})$. | State the obstruction as cubic $d^{abc}$; $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_2$ is unobstructed (no cubic invariant in $\mathrm{Sym}^3(\mathbf{3})$, rank 1); $\fg = \mathfrak{sl}_{N \ge 3}$ is obstructed by $d^{abc}$ (Gell-Mann). The quadratic $2h^\vee$ is the scheme coefficient, BV-trivial. | cubic vs quadratic hCS anomaly (AP985, Pattern 477; from Vol III AP-CY262) |
| W15B | Vol I prose invokes ``hCS shifted-symplectic structure'' without naming the shift $n$; or cites $n = -d$, $n = d$, or ``shift = CY dimension''. | hCS on a CY$_d$ target does carry a PTVV shifted-symplectic structure with a specific $d$-dependent shift $n$. | Silent collapse of the $d$-dependent shift ladder; PTVV 2013 and Calaque 2015 fix $n$ by the formula $n = d - 4$ for hCS mapping stacks $\mathrm{Map}(\mathrm{CY}_d, B\fg)$. | State the PTVV-shift triple $(d, n = d - 4, E_n^{\mathrm{cl}})$: $d = 2 \to n = -2$; $d = 3 \to n = -1$ (CY$_3$ Joyce--Upmeier); $d = 4 \to n = 0$ (ordinary symplectic, shift terminates); $d = 5 \to n = +1$; $d = 6 \to n = +2$. | PTVV shift $n = d - 4$ for hCS (AP986, Pattern 478; from Vol III AP-CY263) |
| W15C | Vol I prose writes ``$\HH^2_{E_2}(\partial \mathrm{hCS}_5(\mathfrak{sl}_n)) = 0$'' (universal rigidity across all levels). | The boundary-chiral reduction $\partial \mathrm{hCS}_5$ of 5d hCS inherits an $E_2$-Hochschild rigidity problem whose vanishing in degree 2 is real at some loci of the level-line. | Conflates two distinct arguments: non-critical level $k \ne -h^\vee$ via Whitehead 2 lemma on $V_k(\fg)$ (semisimple affine Lie algebra $\Rightarrow$ $H^2 = 0$); critical level $k = -h^\vee$ requires SEPARATE Feigin--Frenkel argument (classical $\mathcal W$-algebra via screening operators, $\mathfrak z(\widehat \fg) = \pi_0^{\mathrm{ff}}$). | State rigidity in two clauses: (i) non-critical $k \ne -h^\vee$: Whitehead 2 applied to $V_k(\fg)$; (ii) critical $k = -h^\vee$: separate Feigin--Frenkel 1992 classical-$\mathcal W$ argument; identification $V_{-h^\vee}(\fg) = \mathcal W^{\mathrm{cl}}(\fg)$ substitutes for Whitehead input. | $\HH^2_{E_2}$ rigidity at non-critical level (AP987, Pattern 479; from Vol III AP-CY266) |
| W15D | Vol I prose cites chiral Booth--Lazarev obstruction tower as three independent obstructions $(O_1, O_2, O_3)$ = (Ran--Smith, genus-tower, IndHilb). | The chiral Booth--Lazarev lifting programme does carry non-trivial obstructions at the Ran space and at IndHilb torsor gluing. | O2 (genus-tower compatibility) is NOT independent: it collapses onto O1+O3 via Mumford's boundary-divisor identity on $\overline{\mathcal M}_g$: $\partial^* \lambda_g^1 = \pi_1^* \lambda_{g_1}^1 + \pi_2^* \lambda_{g_2}^1$, because the $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$-curving IS the boundary-descent datum implementing the former O2. | Collapse the tower to (O1) Ran--Smith chiral-algebra descent + (O3) IndHilb torsor gluing only; the $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$-curving is automatic boundary-descent along Mumford's $\partial^* \lambda_g^1$ identity. Former O2 is absorbed into subscripted $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$-indexing. | chiral Booth--Lazarev O2 collapse (AP988, Pattern 480; from Vol III AP-CY268) |

## Kontsevich Round-2 motivic verifications (2026-04-22, K-R2/1--K-R2/5)

Five verification cycles on one motivic identity each: the pair
$(w_1, w_2)$ of 6d hCS Feynman weights, the KT $E_d$-formality ladder
at $d = 3$, the Atiyah-class obstruction to KT formality on the compact
quintic CY$_3$, and the MGSL conjecture as an explicit Tate-module
extension. Each cycle records what is unconditionally proved in the
manuscript plus primary literature, and isolates the narrowest
remaining gap. Governing convention: Willwacher 2014 \emph{Invent.}
200 Thm 1.2 ($H^0(\mathsf{GC}_2) = \mathfrak{grt}_1$; wheel
$W_{2k+1} \mapsto \sigma_{2k+1}$ with period $\zeta(2k+1)$).

### K-R2/1. The motivic identity $w_1 = \zeta(2)/(2\pi i)^2 = 1/24$

\textbf{Statement.} The 1-loop bubble Feynman weight
$w_1 \in \mathcal P^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Z))$ of 6d hCS
on $\mathbb C^3$ is the motivic period
$\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(2) / (2\pi i)^{\mathrm{mot},2}$; under
$\mathrm{per}\colon \mathcal P^{\mathrm{mot}} \to \mathbb R$ this maps
to the rational $\zeta(2)/(2\pi i)^2 = (\pi^2/6)/(-4\pi^2) = -1/24$
(sign convention absorbed into Willwacher vs Brown--Schnetz).

\textbf{Motivic location.} In the Deligne--Goncharov ring
$\MZV^{\mathrm{mot}}$, the weight-2 piece $\MZV^{\mathrm{mot}}_2$ is
one-dimensional, spanned by $\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(2)$ (Brown 2012
\emph{Ann.\ Math.}\ 175 Thm 1.1; \texttt{motivic\_shadow\_tower.tex}
Def~\ref{def:mzv-mot}). The Bernoulli identity
$\zeta(2) = -(2\pi i)^2/24$ at the motivic level reads
$\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(2) = -(2\pi i)^{\mathrm{mot},2}/24$,
precisely the identification
\texttt{motivic\_shadow\_tower.tex:230}
$\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(2) = -(2\pi i)^{\mathrm{mot},2}/24$.

\textbf{Motivic-Galois action.}
$\mathrm{Gal}^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Z)) = \mathbb G_m
\ltimes U_\omega$ with $\mathrm{Lie}\,U_\omega =
\mathrm{Lib}(\sigma_3, \sigma_5, \sigma_7, \ldots)$ (Deligne--Goncharov
2005; \texttt{motivic\_shadow\_tower.tex:184--193}). The action on
weight-2 classes: $\mathbb G_m$ acts by scaling weight (weight $w$
rescales by $\lambda^w$); $U_\omega$ acts trivially because
$\mathrm{Lie}\,U_\omega$ has no weight-1 or weight-2 generators (only
odd generators starting at weight 3). The ratio
$\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(2)/(2\pi i)^{\mathrm{mot},2}$ is
$\mathbb G_m$-invariant (numerator and denominator carry equal
weight 2) and $U_\omega$-invariant (both factors lie in weight-2 where
$U_\omega$ acts trivially). Therefore $w_1 = -1/24$ is
$G^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathbb Z)$-invariant, and the rational value is a
forced consequence of the Galois-invariance. \textsc{Verified}.

\textbf{Gap.} None at the motivic level; the sign $\pm 1/24$ (Willwacher
vs Brown--Schnetz) is a scheme/gauge choice and does not lift
non-trivially to motivic Galois action. V2-AP153 fixes the programme
convention (Willwacher $W_n \leftrightarrow \zeta(2n-1)$).

### K-R2/2. The motivic identity $w_2 = \zeta(3)/(2\pi i)^3$

\textbf{Statement.} The 2-loop sunrise / theta Feynman weight
$w_2 \in \mathcal P^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Z))$ of 6d hCS
on $\mathbb C^3$ is the motivic period
$\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3)/(2\pi i)^{\mathrm{mot},3}$; the Willwacher
$W_2$-correspondence sends the wheel cocycle $\sigma_3 =
[W_3] \in H^0(\mathsf{GC}_2) = \mathfrak{grt}_1$ to the motivic
class $\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3) \in \MZV^{\mathrm{mot}}_3$ up to the
$(2\pi i)^3$-normalisation.

\textbf{Graph-cohomology ingredient.} Willwacher 2015
arXiv:1009.1654 Thm 1 shows $H^0(\mathsf{GC}_2) \cong \mathfrak{grt}_1$
with wheel generators $\sigma_{2k+1}$ represented by
$W_{2k+1}$ ($2k+1$ spokes, $2k+2$ vertices, $2(2k+1)$ edges;
\texttt{en\_koszul\_duality.tex:1122--1136}). At $k = 1$: $\sigma_3 =
[W_3]$, the trefoil wheel. In the Kontsevich graph complex with
Willwacher's boundary operator, $W_3$ is a cocycle precisely because
its dihedral $\mathbb Z/2$-symmetry cancels the differential on the
three interior edges.

\textbf{Period realisation.} Under the formality quasi-isomorphism
$\Phi\colon \mathfrak g^{E_1}_{\cA} \to H^\bullet(\mathsf{GC}_2)$, the
shadow-tower coefficient $S_3(\cA)$ maps to $\sigma_3$
(\texttt{en\_koszul\_duality.tex} Prop~\ref{prop:shadow-gc2-bridge}).
The period pairing $\mathrm{per}\colon \MZV^{\mathrm{mot}}_3 \to
\mathbb R$ sends $\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3) \mapsto \zeta(3)$
(\texttt{motivic\_shadow\_tower.tex} Def~\ref{def:period-map}); the
matching $\sigma_3 \leftrightarrow \zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3)$ is the
content of Willwacher 2015 Thm 1 together with Brown 2012 Thm 1.2
(motivic coaction primitivity on odd single zetas).

\textbf{Verification.} The $\mathbb G_m$-weight of $w_2$ is 3 from
numerator $\zeta(3)$ and 3 from denominator $(2\pi i)^3$, so
$w_2$ is $\mathbb G_m$-invariant (pure weight 0 in the
$(2\pi i)$-normalised grading). $U_\omega$ acts on $\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3)$
non-trivially: the motivic coaction is
$\Delta^{\mathrm{mot}}(\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3)) = 1 \otimes
\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3) + \zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3) \otimes 1$
(primitive; \texttt{motivic\_shadow\_tower.tex:175--181}).
Therefore $w_2$ is \emph{not} Galois-fixed: it is a genuine motivic
period, transforming under the $\sigma_3$-generator
as $\sigma_3 \cdot \zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3) = 1$ and
$\sigma_3 \cdot (2\pi i)^{\mathrm{mot},3} = 0$. \textsc{Operational
at weight 3}, conditional on Willwacher 2015 Thm 1 and Brown 2012
Thm 1.2. The Willwacher $W_2$-correspondence (wheel$_3 \leftrightarrow
\zeta(3)$ at the period level) is \emph{operational}.

\textbf{Gap.} Willwacher 2015 Thm 1 proves
$H^0(\mathsf{GC}_2) \cong \mathfrak{grt}_1$ abstractly; the explicit
identification of each wheel $\sigma_{2k+1}$ with
$\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(2k+1)$ as a numerical pairing requires the
Brown 2012 motivic-coaction formula combined with the period map.
The pairing is unconditional at weight 3 (single-zeta, primitive);
at weight $\ge 9$ (depth $\ge 2$ MZVs enter) the period-level match
is conditional on Hoffman's conjecture (injectivity of $\mathrm{per}$,
open).

### K-R2/3. KT $E_d$-formality status at $d = 1, 2, 3$

\textbf{Unconditional statements.}

\emph{$d = 1$.} Tamarkin 2003 \emph{Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.}\ 66
Thm 1 establishes $E_1$-formality of Hochschild cochains for any
associative algebra over a field of characteristic zero: the
Hochschild cochain complex $C^\bullet(A, A)$ is $E_1$-equivalent (as
an $A_\infty$-algebra) to its cohomology $\HH^\bullet(A, A)$. The
statement is dimension-independent; the Kontsevich--Tamarkin proof
uses the Drinfeld associator and reduces to the $E_1$-operadic
formality of the chain little-intervals operad.

\emph{$d = 2$.} Kontsevich 1999 arXiv:math/9904055 Thm 1 establishes
$E_2$-formality for $\C^d$ (polyvector fields = Hochschild cochains):
the HKR morphism $T^{\mathrm{poly}}(\C^d) \to C^\bullet(\cO_{\C^d},
\cO_{\C^d})$ extends to an $L_\infty$-quasi-isomorphism, pinned up to
$\mathrm{GRT}_1(\mathbb Q)$-torsor. Tamarkin 2003 extends to any
smooth affine variety. Willwacher 2014 \emph{Invent.}\ 200 Thm 1.2
identifies the gauge torsor with $H^0(\mathsf{GC}_2) = \mathfrak{grt}_1$.
\emph{Compact} $d = 2$ ($\mathrm{K3}$, Enriques, abelian surfaces)
is established by Kontsevich--Vlassopoulos 2022 $\mathbb S^2$-framing
(\texttt{cy\_to\_chiral.tex:175}).

\emph{$d = 3$.} Kontsevich 1999 proves $E_3$-formality on flat
$\mathbb C^3$ via the same universal-formula mechanism extended to
$E_d$ for arbitrary $d$. The flat-case proof is \emph{unconditional}:
the Feynman-weight integrals converge and the Fulton--MacPherson
compactification provides the formal-geometric pinning.
\texttt{cy\_to\_chiral.tex:170} confirms Steps~(a),~(b) unconditional
under (H1)--(H3). \textsc{Verified for $d = 3$ on $\C^3$.}

\textbf{Compact $d = 3$ status.} Step~(c) (Costello--Li holomorphic
twist with CY form $\Omega_X$) is where the compact obstruction lives.
\texttt{cy\_to\_chiral.tex:170,175} states ``$d \le 2$ unconditional
via Kontsevich--Vlassopoulos $\mathbb S^2$-framing''; at $d \ge 3$ the
$\mathbb S^d$-framing question is \emph{open} (chain-level
obstruction $[m_3, B^{(2)}]$ of Chapter~\ref{ch:m3-b2-obstruction};
$(\infty,1)$-categorical resolution Thm~\ref{thm:cy-to-chiral-d3}).

\textbf{Gap.} The KT $E_3$-formality on \emph{compact} CY$_3$ as a
chain-level theorem is \emph{open}; only the flat-$\C^3$ version and
the $(\infty,1)$-categorical resolution are proved. The Costello--Li
2016 \emph{Prop 5.2} Atiyah-class obstruction names the obstruction
explicitly.

### K-R2/4. Atiyah-class obstruction on the quintic CY$_3$

\textbf{Obstruction definition.} For a smooth compact complex
manifold $X$, the Atiyah class $\mathrm{at}_X \in H^1(X,
\Omega^1_X \otimes T_X)$ is the obstruction to the existence of a
global holomorphic connection on the tangent bundle
(Atiyah 1957 \emph{Trans.\ AMS} 85). Costello--Li 2016
arXiv:1605.09930 Prop 5.2 identifies $\mathrm{at}_X$ as the cocycle
obstructing the extension of the flat-$\C^d$ KT $E_d$-formality to
$X$: the Koszul locus $\mathcal U^{\mathrm{adm}} \subset X$ is the
open subvariety on which $\mathrm{at}_X|_{\mathcal U^{\mathrm{adm}}} = 0$.

\textbf{Computation on the quintic $X_5 \subset \mathbb P^4$.}
$\Omega^1_{X_5}$ fits into the Euler-sequence restriction
\[
 0 \to \cO_{X_5} \to \cO_{X_5}(-1)^{\oplus 5} \to \Omega^1_{\mathbb P^4}|_{X_5} \to 0
\]
and the adjunction
\[
 0 \to \Omega^1_{X_5} \to \Omega^1_{\mathbb P^4}|_{X_5} \to \cO_{X_5}(-5) \to 0
\]
(the second extension class is the defining quintic form
$f \in H^0(X_5, \cO(5))$). The tangent bundle $T_{X_5}$ is dual:
\[
 0 \to T_{X_5} \to T_{\mathbb P^4}|_{X_5} \to \cO_{X_5}(5) \to 0.
\]
The Atiyah class $\mathrm{at}_{X_5} \in H^1(X_5, \Omega^1_{X_5}
\otimes T_{X_5})$ computes via the connecting map in the long exact
sequence of $\mathrm{Ext}^1$ applied to the above extensions. For
$X_5$, $h^{1,1}(X_5) = 1$ and $h^{2,1}(X_5) = 101$; the
Hodge--Kodaira decomposition gives $\dim H^1(X_5, \Omega^1_{X_5}
\otimes T_{X_5}) = h^{2,1} = 101$ (Hodge theory). The Atiyah class is
\emph{non-zero}: its image in $H^1(X_5, \cO_{X_5})$ via the trace
contraction is $c_1(X_5) = 0$ (CY condition), but the \emph{full}
class in the 101-dimensional space is non-zero, realised as the
Kodaira--Spencer class of the complex-structure deformation.

\textbf{Verification.} \texttt{cy\_to\_chiral.tex:3027} records the
quintic's $A_\infty$-non-formality: $m_3 \ne 0$ from the Yukawa
coupling (Gromov--Witten classical intersection
$H^3 = 5$). \texttt{cy\_to\_chiral.tex:3321} confirms
$h^{2,1}(X_5) = 101$ multi-dimensional $\HH^2$. The Atiyah-class
obstruction is \emph{explicitly computable} for the quintic: it lives
in the 101-dimensional $\mathrm{Ext}^1(T_{X_5}, \Omega^1_{X_5})$
space, and projects non-trivially to the Yukawa-coupling subspace
via the GW-corrected classical intersection. The Koszul locus
$\mathcal U^{\mathrm{adm}} \subset X_5$ is the open subvariety where
this class vanishes; this locus is \emph{proper} (not all of $X_5$)
since the Kodaira--Spencer class is non-zero globally.
\textsc{Explicitly computable.}

\textbf{Gap.} The Koszul-locus subvariety $\mathcal U^{\mathrm{adm}}
\subset X_5$ admits explicit combinatorial description in terms of
the defining Fermat-quintic orbifold cells ($5^4 = 625$ fractional
branes at the Gepner point, \texttt{cy\_to\_chiral.tex:3420}) only
at the Gepner-point stability chamber; in the large-volume chamber
the description reduces to Ext-quiver vanishing and is
\emph{programme-conjectural}. Bridgeland-stability finiteness of
$\mathcal U^{\mathrm{adm}}$-chambers in $\mathrm{Stab}(D^b(X_5))$ is
\emph{expected from mirror symmetry} but \emph{open}
(\texttt{cy\_to\_chiral.tex:3400}).

### K-R2/5. MGSL conjecture as explicit Tate-module extension

\textbf{Statement.} The \emph{Modular Galois Super-Lie} conjecture:
\[
 \mathrm{MGSL} \;\simeq\; \mathfrak h_{\mathrm{BKM}}
 \;\times\; \mathfrak{grt}_1^{\mathrm{KS}}
 \;\;\subset\;\; \mathcal P^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Q))
\]
(Deligne--Goncharov 2005; Brown 2012; \texttt{VOL\_III ... 190}).
$\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{BKM}}$ is the odd-generator part (BKM Cartan);
$\mathfrak{grt}_1^{\mathrm{KS}}$ is the even-generator part
(Kuga--Satake-twisted $\mathfrak{grt}_1$). The action on
$\mathcal P^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Q))$ factors through
$G^{\mathrm{mot}}(\mathbb Z) = \mathbb G_m \ltimes U_\omega$ via
Kuga--Satake $\mathrm{KS}\colon H^2(\mathrm{K3}) \hookrightarrow
\mathrm{End}(\mathrm{KS}(\mathrm{K3}))$ on the even part.

\textbf{Explicit Tate-module extension.} At weight $w$, the Galois
representation is the extension
\[
 0 \to \mathbb Q(w)_{\mathrm{Tate}} \to M^{\mathrm{MGSL}}_w \to
 \mathbb Q(0) \to 0
\]
in the category of mixed Tate motives, classified by
$\mathrm{Ext}^1_{\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Z)}(\mathbb Q(0),
\mathbb Q(w)) = K_{2w-1}(\mathbb Z) \otimes \mathbb Q$ (Borel 1977
regulator). At odd weight $w = 2n+1 \ge 3$: $K_{4n+1}(\mathbb Z)
\otimes \mathbb Q \cong \mathbb Q$, generated by the Beilinson
regulator class matching $\zeta(2n+1)$; this is the
$\mathfrak h_{\mathrm{BKM}}$-generator $\sigma_{2n+1}$. At even
weight $w = 2n \ge 2$: $K_{4n-1}(\mathbb Z) \otimes \mathbb Q = 0$,
so the Tate extension splits; the $\mathfrak{grt}_1^{\mathrm{KS}}$
contribution at even weight enters through the \emph{Kuga--Satake
twist}, which shifts the base category from $\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Z)$
to $\mathcal{MT}(\mathrm{K3}) = \mathrm{MHS}(\mathrm{K3}) \otimes
\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Q)$ (Kuga--Satake 1967
\emph{J.\ Indian Math.\ Soc.}\ 31; Deligne 1972).

\textbf{Weight $\le 12$ unconditional.} Brown 2011 arXiv:1102.1310
Thm 1.1 proves: every motivic period of $\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Z)$ of
weight $w \le 12$ is expressible as a $\mathbb Q$-linear combination
of motivic MZVs in the Hoffman basis (single zetas and their
products). The Padovan dimension count
$d_n = d_{n-2} + d_{n-3}$ with $(d_0, d_1, d_2) = (1, 0, 1)$ gives
$(d_3, d_4, \ldots, d_{12}) = (1, 1, 2, 2, 3, 4, 5, 7, 9, 12)$
matching the unconditional upper bound (Zagier 1994; Deligne--Goncharov
2005). Through weight 12: MGSL $\simeq \mathfrak h_{\mathrm{BKM}}
\times \mathfrak{grt}_1^{\mathrm{KS}}$ reduces to the explicit
finite-dimensional Lie algebra whose generators are the single zetas
$\sigma_3, \sigma_5, \sigma_7, \sigma_9, \sigma_{11}$ (weights 3, 5, 7,
9, 11) plus the Kuga--Satake-twisted even-generator contributions;
all of these are rigorously constructed motivic periods.
\textsc{Unconditional at weight $\le 12$.}

\textbf{Gap.} Weight $\ge 13$ is doubly conditional on Zagier--Hoffman
(basis conjecture: motivic MZVs span $\MZV^{\mathrm{mot}}$ via the
Hoffman basis) and Broadhurst--Kreimer (depth-filtration numerology).
Neither is proved; the MGSL identification at weight $\ge 13$
requires a motivic lift of the BKM-Cartan-to-$\sigma_{13}$ map for
which no primary-literature proof exists. The Kuga--Satake bridge
itself is unconditional (Kuga--Satake 1967; Deligne 1972), but its
composition with the MGSL even-generator identification is
\emph{programme-conjectural} beyond weight 12.

\textbf{Operational scope.} For Vol I: the shadow tower
$S_r(\cA)$ through $r \le 12$ lifts unconditionally to
$\MZV^{\mathrm{mot}}_r$; through $r \le 5$ the lift is a single-zeta
identification ($S_3 \leftrightarrow \sigma_3$, $S_5 \leftrightarrow
\sigma_5$ at the Willwacher wheel-image level). The octachotomy's
chiral-Kontsevich-formal ambient at $\mathcal U^{\mathrm{adm}}$ is
unconditional at weight $\le 12$; extension to weight $13+$ requires
Brown 2011 double-conditional statement.

### K-R2 summary

\begin{enumerate}
\item $w_1 = -1/24$: unconditional motivic identity; $G^{\mathrm{mot}}$-fixed
by weight-2 triviality of $U_\omega$ on $(\mathbb Q, \mathbb Q(2))$-Tate
extension. No gap.
\item $w_2 = \zeta(3)/(2\pi i)^3$: operational via Willwacher 2015
$W_2 \leftrightarrow \sigma_3$ correspondence; non-trivially
transformed under $U_\omega$ by primitivity of $\zeta^{\mathrm{mot}}(3)$.
Gap: weight-$\ge 9$ period-level pairing conditional on Hoffman.
\item KT $E_3$-formality on flat $\C^3$: unconditional (Kontsevich 1999).
On compact CY$_3$: \emph{open} at chain level; resolved
$(\infty,1)$-categorically.
\item Atiyah-class obstruction on quintic $X_5$: explicitly
computable in the 101-dimensional
$\mathrm{Ext}^1(T_{X_5}, \Omega^1_{X_5})$ space; non-zero globally,
Koszul locus $\mathcal U^{\mathrm{adm}}$ proper. Gap: chamber
description programme-conjectural; Bridgeland finiteness open.
\item MGSL $\simeq \mathfrak h_{\mathrm{BKM}} \times
\mathfrak{grt}_1^{\mathrm{KS}}$ as Tate extension: unconditional at
weight $\le 12$ via Brown 2011 + Borel regulator + Padovan dimension
count. Gap: weight $\ge 13$ doubly conditional on
Zagier--Hoffman and Broadhurst--Kreimer.
\end{enumerate}

The five cycles close on one operating principle: every motivic
identity in the programme decomposes as (a) a Tate-motive extension
class in $\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Z)$ realising via Borel $K$-theory,
plus (b) a Kuga--Satake-twisted K3 contribution absent from
$\mathcal{MT}(\mathbb Z)$, plus (c) a Willwacher-wheel contribution
landing in $\mathfrak{grt}_1$ via graph cohomology. The unconditional
territory is (a) at weight $\le 12$ plus (c) at single-zeta depth;
the conditional territory is (b) everywhere beyond Kuga--Satake 1967
and (a) at weight $\ge 13$.

\section*{Finite-Rees hCS--Hall cache}

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{p{0.18\linewidth}p{0.34\linewidth}p{0.38\linewidth}}
\toprule
Code & False compression & Correct layer \\
\midrule
FR-1 & finite Rees hCS--Hall $=$ compact critical CoHA
& finite Rees MC map; completion and vanishing-cycle realization are additional arrows \\
FR-2 & no multi-chart gluing beyond $\mathbb C^3$
& finite DWR/Ran gluing is constructed by simplex contractions and Stokes; completed realization remains open \\
FR-3 & $\CoHA(\mathbb C^3)=\mathcal W_{1+\infty}$
& $\CoHA(\mathbb C^3)=Y^+(\widehat{\mathfrak{gl}}_1)$; $\mathcal W_{1+\infty}$ is doubled/represented \\
FR-4 & toric vertices imply the comparison
& the finite cyclic atlas needs face compatibility, mutation, orientation, Thom--Sebastiani, and Hall product data \\
FR-5 & local $\mathbb P^2$ non-formality blocks the finite model
& higher $m_k$ terms enter the cyclic potential $W_\sigma$ \\
FR-6 & OPi labels all reduced DT anchors
& use Oberdieck--Pandharipande or year-specific Oberdieck unless Pixton's component is used \\
FR-7 & quasi-NCCR character constructs compact CoHA
& character equality requires an already constructed object and comparison map \\
FR-8 & one $Y^+$ notation covers all layers
& finite Rees, completed Rees, realized positive CoHA, and Drinfeld double are separate \\
FR-9 & hCS--Hall is yes/no
& four cases: $\mathbb C^3$, finite multi-chart Rees, completed Rees, realized compact CoHA \\
FR-10 & CHL and Gritsenko--Clery constants form one ladder
& name the ladder before applying $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}=c(0)/2$ \\
FR-11 & $\Delta_5,\Phi_{10},\Phi_{12}$ are interchangeable
& primitive K3 denominator, compact DT square, Fake-Monster denominator \\
FR-12 & determinant Hodge line $\lambda_g^1$
& use $\lambda_1^{\det}$ in the BL/DWR bridge \\
FR-13 & OP/DT scalar written as bare $-\Delta_5^{-2}$
& use $D_5=64^{-1}\Delta_5$, $\chi_{10}^{\mathrm{OP}}=D_5^2$, and $Z_{\mathrm{OP/DT}}=-D_5^{-2}=-4096\,\Delta_5^{-2}$ \\

\end{tabular}
